The Metaphor of Seeing Death
Baqillani explains the poet's meaning of 'seeing death' as a metaphor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends the permissibility of metaphorical language in theological texts, using a poet's statement 'seeing death' as a case study.

Core Idea
Metaphors do not compromise creed; they reflect linguistic convention.

The objector points to a line of poetry where the poet says 'I saw their faces toward death looking' and argues that death is invisible, so the line is impossible. Baqillani's response teaches us how to handle such figurative language: by identifying the intended meaning behind the words. This passage shows that Sunni theology does not reject metaphor but interprets it consistently with rational and linguistic norms.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the poetic line
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the objector's challenge: death cannot be seen, so how can the poet claim to see it?
2
Identify Baqillani's two interpretations
Baqillani gives two possible meanings for 'death' in the line: first, as the causes of death (blows, stabs); second, as the heroes who cause death. Find where he introduces each.
Both rely on the linguistic principle of calling something by its cause or associated entity.
3
Examine the supporting poetic evidence
Read the additional poems by Jarir and another poet. How do they use 'death' to refer to a hero?
These examples strengthen Baqillani's argument that the metaphor is culturally accepted.
4
Reflect on the principle
Baqillani applies the rule that 'a thing is named by the name of its cause.' Ask yourself: how does this principle protect the creed from false literal interpretations?
This connects to the larger topic of God's visibility (ru'yat Allah).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا فما معنى قول الشاعر: وَيَوْمَ بِذِي قَارٍ رَأيْتُ وُجُوهَهُمْ إلَى الْمَوْتِ مِنْ وَقْعِ السُّيُوفِ نَوَاظِرُ والموت لا يُرى ولا يُنظر إليه؟ قيل لهم: ما أراد الشاعر إلا رؤية الأبصار؛ وإنما أراد بالموت الضرب والطعن وفلق الهام، لأن ذلك يُسمى في اللغة موتاً، لأنه أسباب الموت وما يقع عنده غالباً، والشيء عندهم يُسمّى باسم سببه. ويمكن أيضاً أن يكون أراد بذكر الموت الأبطال الذين يوجد الموت عند كرّها وإقدامها. قال جرير: أنا المَوْتُ الَّذِي حُبِّرتَ عَنْهُ فَلَيْسَ لِهَارِبِ مِنِّي نَجَاءُ. وقال آخر: يَا أَيُّهَا الرَّاكِبُ الْمُرْجَى مَطِيَّتُهُ سَائِل بَنِي أَسَدٍ مَا هَذِهِ الصَّوْتُ وَقُلْ لَهَا بَادِرُوا بِالْعُذْرِ وَالتَمِسُوا قَوْلاً يُبَرِّتُكُمْ إِنِّي أَنَا الْمَوْتُ. يريد به البطل الذي يكون عند فعله الموت.
Then if they say: What is the meaning of the poet's statement: 'And on the day at Dhi Qār I saw their faces, toward death from the strike of swords, looking' – while death is not seen nor looked at? Say to them: The poet only meant the seeing of the eyes; he only intended by 'death' the striking and stabbing and splitting of skulls, because that is called 'death' in language, since it is the cause of death and what usually occurs with it, and a thing is named by the name of its cause. It is also possible that he meant by mentioning 'death' the heroes (al-abṭāl) with whose charge and advance death occurs. Jarīr said: 'I am death, about whom you were informed; there is no escape for a fleeing one from me.' And another said: 'O rider whose mount is hoped, ask the Banī Asad what this is! And tell them to hasten with excuse and seek a statement that acquits you, for I am death.' He intends by it the hero with whose act death occurs.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding a poetic line. The objector cites a line where the poet says 'I saw their faces toward death looking,' arguing that death is invisible, so how can one see it? Baqillani answers that the poet is using metaphorical language. He gives two interpretations: first, the poet meant seeing the actual causes of death (blows, stabs), which are called death by synecdoche. Second, the poet may have meant the heroes (al-abṭāl) whose actions cause death, and then 'seeing death' means seeing those heroes. Baqillani supports this with two other poems: one by Jarīr who says 'I am death,' and another poet who says 'I am death,' again meaning the heroic warrior. The point is that such metaphors do not prove that God is not seen, because human language uses figures of speech.

الأبطال

السبب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objector assumes that any statement about 'seeing death' must be literal, implying that if a text contains such language, it is false or contradictory.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the poet used metaphor: 'death' refers to its causes or the heroes causing it. Literal interpretation is not required.

Key Takeaway
Metaphorical language is a natural part of human speech; understanding it requires identifying the intended referent, not rejecting the text.

Refutation of a Poetic Argument Regarding Vision
Baqillani refutes a poetic argument against the vision of God by explaining the meaning of 'وجوه'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes a misinterpretation of the word 'وجوه' by distinguishing between its literal and metaphorical usage based on context and the attribute 'نضارة'.

Core Idea
Scriptural terms derive their meaning from divine usage, not poetic license.

Baqillani now turns to an objection based on poetry. An opponent cites a line where 'وجوه' seems to refer to tribal leaders. Baqillani responds by arguing that the Quranic verse 'وجوه يومئذ ناضرة' uses the word literally because radiance ('نضارة') is only attributable to a physical face. Thus, the poetic usage does not undermine the possibility of seeing Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation once to grasp the flow of the objection and answer.
Pay attention to the two poetic citations.
2
Identify the objection
Locate the poetic claim and understand its intended challenge regarding the word 'وجوه'.
The objector implies that 'وجوه' means leaders, not physical faces.
3
Analyze Baqillani's response
Notice the two-part answer: first, the poem is unknown among scholars, so it lacks authority; second, even if authentic, the word 'وجوه' in the Quran is used literally because of the attribute 'نضارة'.
The Quranic context (radiance) determines the literal meaning.
4
Reflect on the method
Understand how Baqillani uses the Quran's own description to fix the meaning of a word, overriding poetic precedents.
This shows the primacy of scriptural context over external sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال آخر : يأَيُّهَا الرَّاكِبُ الْمُرْجَى مَطِيَّتُهُ سَائِل بَنِي أَسَدٍ مَا هَذِهِ الصَّوْتُ وَقُلْ لَهَا بَادِرُوا بِالْعُذْرِ وَالتَمِسُوا قَوْلاً يُبَرِّتُكُمْ إِنِّي أَنَا الْمَوْتُ یرید به البطل الذي يكون عند فعله الموت
فإن قيل : فما معنى قول الآخر:
وُجُوهٌ بِهَا لَيْلَ الْحِجَازِ عَلَى النَّوَى إِلَى مَلِكٍ رُكن الْمَغَارِبِ نَاظِرَهُ قيل لهم : هذا شعر لا يعرفه أحد من أهل العلم، فلا حجة فيه وإن صح ، لم يفسد ما قلناه لأننا قد قلنا إن الوجوه المقرونة بذكر البلدة والعشيرة إنما يراد به سادة الناس. والله تعالى وصف الوجوه التي هي الجوارح بأنها تنظر إليه، لأنه تعالى وصفها بما لا يجوز أن يوصف به إلا الجارحة حيث قال : وجوه يومئذ ناضرة . والنضارة لا تكون إلا في الجارحة التي هي الوجه.
He said: 'O rider whose mount is eagerly awaited, ask the sons of Asad what this sound is, and say to them: hasten with apology and seek a word that will acquit you; I am death.' He intends by it the hero who causes death when he acts. If it is said: 'What is the meaning of the other's saying: Faces whereby the night of Hijaz in distance towards a king, the pillar of the Maghrib, looking at him?' It is said to them: This is poetry unknown to any scholar, so there is no proof in it. Even if it were authentic, it would not invalidate what we said, because we have said that 'faces' mentioned alongside a town and tribe are intended to mean the nobles of the people. And Allah Almighty described the faces that are the bodily limbs as looking at Him, because He described them with what is only permissible for the limb, when He said: 'Faces on that Day are radiant' (75:22). Radiance is only in the limb which is the face.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer regarding a poetic argument. The author first cites a line of poetry that seems to use 'death' metaphorically. Then an objector quotes another line: 'Faces... looking at a king' and asks its meaning. The author replies that this poetry is unknown to scholars and thus not a valid proof. Even if it were authentic, it does not undermine their position because the word 'وجوه' when mentioned alongside a town and tribe refers to the leaders of the people, not literal faces. However, in the Quran, when Allah says 'وجوه يومئذ ناضرة' (Faces on that Day are radiant), He is describing the literal facial feature because 'نضارة' (radiance) only applies to the face as a bodily organ. Thus, the Quranic usage confirms that 'وجوه' can mean the physical face, supporting the possibility of seeing God (since the faces look at Him). The poetry's usage does not contradict this.

Key Terms
وجوه
نضارة
الجارحة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the word 'وجوه' in the Quran always means 'leaders' or 'nobles' rather than the physical face.
Correction: Baqillani shows that in the verse 'وجوه يومئذ ناضرة', the word must refer to the physical face because radiance (نضارة) only applies to that bodily limb.

Checkpoint

A) It means the leaders of a tribe.
B) It refers to the physical face because 'نضارة' only applies to the face.
C) It is metaphorical for honor.
D) It means the people of paradise.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic description of faces as 'ناضرة' proves that 'وجوه' can refer to the physical face, supporting the possibility of seeing God.

Interpreting Quranic Verses on Capacity: Refuting Pre-Action Ability
Baqillani explains Quranic verses to refute pre-action capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani interprets Quranic verses on burden and capacity to refute the claim that capacity exists before the action.

Core Idea
Quranic verses on burden limit obligation to present ability, not pre-existing capacity.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses an objection raised by opponents who use two Quranic verses to argue for pre-action capacity. He clarifies that the verses refer to the immediate ability to fulfill obligations, such as a wife's capacity to pay maintenance at the time, and do not establish a capacity that exists before the action.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: an opponent's question followed by Baqillani's response.
The opponent cites two verses: 2:286 and 65:7.
2
Identify the opponent's argument
The opponent implies that the verses prove capacity exists before the action, because Allah only burdens within capacity. Understand why this is a plausible reading.
3
Understand Baqillani's interpretative move
Baqillani specifies the context: the verse about 'wives' means they are not obliged beyond what they can manage at the moment. He explicitly denies that the verse establishes pre-action capacity.
This refutes the opponent's general interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فإن قالوا: فما معنى قوله تعالى : لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا وسعها ، و لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا ما آتاها؟ [نفقات؟] قيل لهم : المراد بذلك والله أعلم أنه لم يكلف أحداً من الزوجات إلا ما وجد وتمكن منه دون ما لا تناله يده . ولم يرد به إثبات الاستطاعة قبل الفعل .
Question: So what is the meaning of His statement, Exalted is He, 'Allah does not burden a soul beyond its capacity' and 'Allah does not burden a soul except with what He has given it'? It was said to them: The intent of that—and Allah knows best—is that He did not burden any of the wives except with what she found and was able to do, beyond what she cannot reach. He did not intend thereby to establish capacity (istita'a) before the action.
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer about the interpretation of two Quranic verses: 'La yukallifu Allahu nafsan illa wus'aha' (al-Baqara 2:286) and 'La yukallifu Allahu nafsan illa ma ataha' (al-Talaq 65:7). The opponents argue that these verses imply capacity exists before the action, since the burden is only what one can bear. Baqillani responds by specifying the referent: the verse about wives (from the context of divorce and maintenance) means that wives are not obligated beyond what they can manage at the time, not that they had capacity before. He explicitly states that the verse does not establish pre-action capacity (istita'a qabl al-fi'l).

Key Terms
تكليف (taklif)
وسع (wus')
استطاعة (istita'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verses about burden prove that capacity must exist before the action.
Correction: The verses refer to the present ability to fulfill obligations, not a capacity that exists prior to the action. Baqillani interprets them contextually as referring to wives' maintenance.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani say the verse 'La yukallifu Allahu nafsan illa wus'aha' means?
A) It proves capacity exists before the action
B) It refers only to the ability to pay maintenance at the moment
C) It means people are not obligated beyond their pre-existing ability
D) It abrogates all obligations

Key Takeaway
Baqillani interprets Quranic verses on burden as referring to present ability, not pre-existing capacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a difficult religious duty, do you first calculate whether you are 'capable enough' before acting, or do you trust that Allah only asks of you what He will enable you to do in that moment? Which approach better reflects the meaning of 'لا يكلف الله نفساً إلا وسعها'?
?
Think of a time you delayed or avoided an act of worship because you felt you lacked the strength. How does Baqillani's explanation—that capacity is given at the moment of action—challenge your excuse? Will you take a step of obedience today despite feeling unprepared?
?
If Allah's justice means He never burdens us beyond our present ability, what does that demand from you when you are tempted to say 'I can't'? Is it possible that your 'I can't' is really a refusal to act on the capacity Allah has already given you right now?

Interpreting the Ransom Verse: Baqillani's Rebuttal
Baqillani interprets the ransom verse to exclude the meaning of ability (tawq).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani interprets the verse 'wa 'ala alladhina yutiqunahu fidyah' to argue against pre-action capacity, using variant readings and abrogation.

Core Idea
The variant reading shifts the focus from ability to burden, undermining the opponent's proof.

This passage shows Baqillani responding to an objection based on a Quranic verse often used to argue that capacity must exist before action. He carefully parses the verse's meaning, offers alternative interpretations, and introduces a variant reading that removes any mention of ability. Through linguistic and textual analysis, he strengthens the Ash'ari position on human capacity.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first interpretation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the question posed by the opponents and Baqillani's initial response that 'yutiqunahu' refers to those who find fasting difficult but attempt it. He also claims the verse is abrogated.
This interpretation emphasizes effort, not inherent ability.
2
Consider the alternative interpretation
Pay attention to the second possible meaning: those who are able to feed others (i.e., afford ransom) but cannot fast. This shifts the focus to financial ability, not physical capacity to fast.
Both interpretations avoid implying pre-action capacity.
3
Examine the variant reading
Look at the variant 'yutawwanahu' (from tawq, meaning burden). This reading does not mention qudra or taqa at all. Reflect on how this supports Baqillani's argument against the opponent's proof.
The variant is cited as an existing recitation, not invented by Baqillani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فإن قالوا : فما معنى قوله عزّ وجلّ : وعلى الذين يطيقونه فدية ؟ . قيل لهم : معنى ذلك على الذين يطيقون الصيام إن أرادوه وتكلّفوه وعدلوا عن الإفطار . والآية منسوخ حكمها على هذا التأويل. ويمكن أن يكون المراد على الذين يطيقون الإطعام ولا يقدرون على الصيام فدية، إذا أفطروا . وقد قرىء وعلى الذين يطوقونه فدية يعني يؤمرون به ويُكلَّفونه ، ولم يعرض على هذه القراءة لذكر القدرة والطاقة .
Question: So what is the meaning of His statement, Mighty and Majestic, 'And upon those who are able [yutiqunahu], a ransom'? It was said to them: The meaning of that is upon those who are able to fast if they intend it and undertake it with difficulty and turn away from breaking the fast. And the ruling of the verse is abrogated according to this interpretation. It is also possible that the meaning is upon those who are able to feed [others] but cannot fast, a ransom, if they break the fast. And it has been recited as 'wa 'ala alladhina yutawwanahu fidyah', meaning they are commanded and burdened with it, and this recitation does not mention ability (qudra) and capacity (taqa).
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer about the verse 'Wa 'ala alladhina yutiqunahu fidyatun' (al-Baqara 2:184). The opponents likely used this verse to argue for capacity before action. Baqillani gives two interpretations: first, 'yutiqunahu' means those who find fasting difficult but attempt it, and the verse is abrogated. Second, it could mean those who are able to feed others (i.e., afford ransom) but cannot fast. He then notes a variant reading 'yutawwanahu' (from tawq, meaning burden), which clearly does not refer to ability, thus removing the proof for pre-action capacity. He emphasizes that this variant avoids mentioning qudra or taqa altogether.

Key Terms
يطيق (yutiq)
فدية (fidya)
نسخ (naskh)
قراءة (qira'a)
توق (tawq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The variant reading 'yutawwanahu' is a later alteration or inauthentic.
Correction: Baqillani cites it as an existing recitation ('wa qad quri'a'), implying it was known and accepted. It is a legitimate reading that supports his argument.

Checkpoint
How does the variant reading 'yutawwanahu' affect the argument about capacity?
A) It proves capacity before action
B) It means hardship, not ability
C) It is a later addition
D) It supports the opponent's position

Key Takeaway
Baqillani uses the variant reading 'yutawwanahu' to argue that the verse refers to burden, not ability, thus removing the proof for pre-action capacity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you approach a verse that seems to support your own view, do you stop to consider alternative interpretations or variant readings? How might your certainty about a matter be challenged by what Baqillani did here?
?
Baqillani offered multiple interpretations, including one based on a variant reading. Are you willing to question the 'standard' text you've always known, or do you find it unsettling? What would it take for you to accept a different recitation?
?
The opponents used the verse as proof for ability. If you were in their place, how would you react when confronted with a variant reading that undermines your argument? Would you seek to understand it, or would you dismiss it? Examine your own heart: do you love truth more than your own positions?

Interpreting Istita'a in the Hajj Verse
Baqillani explains that Hajj verse requires means (zad), not pre-action capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani interprets the phrase 'man istata'a' in the Hajj verse as referring to actual possession of means, not a pre-existing capacity.

Core Idea
The Hajj verse requires resources, not latent ability.

Opponents of the Ash'ari position on capacity (istita'a) often cite the Hajj verse to argue that ability must exist before action. In this short passage from al-Tamhid, Imam al-Baqillani responds by clarifying that the verse speaks of having provisions (zad), not of a metaphysical capacity. This distinction is crucial for understanding the Ash'ari doctrine of acquisition (kasb).

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice that the answer is cut short but the key point—'whoever finds provision (zad)'—is clear.
The passage is an objection-and-answer format.
2
Identify the objection
The opponents argue: if ability (istita'a) is mentioned in the Qur'an, doesn't that prove ability exists before the action? Understand why this is a challenge to the Ash'ari view.
The objection uses a scriptural proof to argue for pre-action capacity.
3
Analyze Baqillani's response
Baqillani reinterprets 'istita'a' in the verse as referring to having the means (zad). This means the verse does not support pre-action capacity but rather the possession of resources.
This aligns with the Ash'ari position that capacity is simultaneous with the action.
4
Reflect on the broader lesson
Consider how this interpretation defends the Ash'ari doctrine against scriptural objections. The verse is about obligation based on means, not about metaphysical ability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فإن قالوا : فما معنى قوله تعالى : والله على الناس حج البيت من استطاع إليه سبيلاً ؟ . قيل لهم : معناه أن الله أوجب الحج على كل من وجد زاداً
Question: So what is the meaning of His statement, Exalted is He, 'And upon the people is the pilgrimage to the House for whoever is able [istata'a] to find a way to it'? It was said to them: Its meaning is that Allah made the pilgrimage obligatory upon everyone who finds provision (zad)...
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer about the Hajj verse (Al 'Imran 3:97). The opponents argued that 'man istata'a' (whoever is able) implies capacity exists before the action. Baqillani responds that the verse means that Hajj is obligatory only on those who possess the means (zad, provisions), not on those who have a pre-existing latent ability. The answer is incomplete in the provided text, but the key point is that 'istita'a' here refers to actual possession of resources, not a metaphysical capacity before the act.

Key Terms
استطاعة (istita'a)
حج (hajj)
زاد (zad)
سبيل (sabil)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Hajj verse proves that ability (istita'a) must exist before the action.
Correction: Baqillani shows that 'istita'a' in the verse refers to having provisions (zad), not a pre-existing capacity. The verse speaks about the condition for obligation, not about the metaphysical timing of ability.

Checkpoint

B) Possession of provisions (zad)

Key Takeaway
The Hajj verse does not support pre-action capacity; it bases obligation on actual possession of provisions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
This lesson teaches that obligation follows from having means (zad), not from mere potential. What obligations in your life are you delaying by telling yourself you are 'not able' when you actually lack the means? Will you stop making excuses?

Interpretation of 'Fattaqullah Ma Istata'tum'
Baqillani interprets a Qur'anic phrase on human capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's precise interpretation of the Qur'anic command to fear Allah 'as much as you are able' and how it relates to human capacity free from defect and incapacity.

Core Idea
Human capacity is defined by ability without defect, not by absolute power.

In this short mas'ala, Imam Baqillani addresses a key question about the meaning of the Qur'anic phrase 'ma istata'tum' in the verse 'Fattaqullah ma istata'tum'. How much ability does God require? Baqillani clarifies that the ability referenced is the normal human capacity to act or refrain, provided there is no defect or incapacity. This interpretation has important implications for understanding human responsibility and divine obligation.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a question is posed, then answered.
The questioner asks about the meaning of a Qur'anic phrase.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on the terms 'mustati'een' (capable), 'mu'awwafin' (defective), and 'ajizin' (incapable). Understand their precise meanings.
These terms define the boundaries of human capacity.
3
Understand the doctrine
Baqillani's answer ties the command to the absence of impediments. Reflect on how this interprets divine obligation realistically.
4
Apply the lesson
Consider a common misunderstanding: that 'ma istata'tum' means any effort. Baqillani corrects this.
The correct understanding is ability without defect or incapacity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
فإن قالوا فما معنى قوله تعالى: فاتقوا الله ما استطعتم؟
قيل لهم: معناه: ما كنتم مستطيعين للفعل أو لتركه، غير مؤوفين ولا عاجزين.

Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage is a question-and-answer (mas'ala) concerning the interpretation of a Qur'anic verse. The questioner asks about the meaning of 'as much as you are able' (ma istata'tum). Baqillani's answer explains that the capacity referred to is the ability to either perform the action or refrain from it, provided the person is not suffering from any defect (not 'mu'awwafin') or incapacity (not 'ajizin'). Thus, the verse commands within the bounds of normal human capability, not absolute or limitless ability.

Key Terms

مستطيع
عجز
آفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'ma istata'tum' implies any degree of effort or that it commands the impossible.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies it means ability without impediment — the person is not defective or incapable.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani restricts the command to fear Allah to situations where one has unimpaired ability to act or refrain.

Baqillani's Interpretation of 'Faman Lam Yastati'
Baqillani explains the verse on feeding the poor as alternative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's restriction of the Quranic substitute for fasting to cases of genuine incapacity, excluding personal preference.

Core Idea
Not every difficulty excuses a substitute; only genuine incapacity.

In this concise mas'ala, Imam Baqillani addresses a potential misinterpretation of a Quranic ruling. The verse provides an alternative for those who cannot fast, but who exactly qualifies? Baqillani clarifies that the permission is limited to those with real physical inability, not those who simply prefer not to fast.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
First, read the passage in Arabic and its literal translation to grasp the question-and-answer structure.
Note the unclear phrase 'الإيثار تركه'—likely a scribal issue.
2
Identify the conditions
Look for the two conditions Baqillani gives for excused substitution: 'عجز' (incapacity) and 'آفة' (defect).
These are the only valid reasons; mere preference is excluded.
3
Contrast with the mistaken view
Understand that some might think the verse allows anyone who finds fasting hard to substitute. Baqillani rejects that.
The key is that 'لا يستطع' here means cannot, not 'prefers not to.'
4
Reflect on the wider principle
Consider how this illustrates a broader usul al-fiqh principle: legal permissions are tied to valid excuses, not whims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
فإن قالوا فما معنى قوله فمن لم يستطع فإطعام ستين مسكيناً؟
قيل لهم: معناه أن من لم يستطع الصيام لعجز أو آفة، فعليه الإطعام دون من لم يستطعه الإيثار تركه [؟].
Issue: If they say: What is the meaning of His statement: 'And whoever cannot find [the means] then a fast of sixty days'? It is said to them: Its meaning is that whoever cannot fast due to incapacity or a defect, then feeding [the poor] is incumbent upon him, not the one who cannot do it due to preference and abandonment [؟].
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This is another mas'ala on Qur'anic interpretation. The verse gives an alternative: one who cannot fast should feed sixty poor people. Baqillani explains that the incapacity here is due to actual inability ('ajz) or a defect (afa), not due to mere choice or preference. The phrase 'man lam yastati'hu al-ithar tarkahu' is problematic but likely means the one who cannot do it because he prefers to abandon it—such a person is not excused; he must fast. Thus, only those with genuine impediments are allowed the alternative.

Key Terms
استطاعة
عجز
آفة
إطعام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse permits anyone who finds fasting difficult to substitute with feeding the poor.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that only those with genuine incapacity or a defect are permitted the substitution, not those who merely prefer not to fast.

Checkpoint

A) Anyone who finds fasting difficult
B) Only those who cannot fast due to incapacity or a defect
C) Those who prefer not to fast
D) Anyone who can afford to feed the poor

Key Takeaway
Baqillani emphasizes that only genuine physical inability, not personal preference, permits a substitute for fasting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Quranic Proofs for Burdens Beyond Capacity
Baqillani provides three Quranic proofs for the permissibility of burdens beyond capacity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three Quranic proofs used by Baqillani to establish that God may burden His servants beyond their capacity, and how these proofs address the objection of injustice.

Core Idea
The Quran itself shows that God can command what is beyond human capacity without injustice.

Imam Baqillani defends the Ash'ari position that God may burden beyond capacity by turning to the Quran. He cites three verses that, when properly understood, demonstrate that such burdens are not unjust or foolish. This lesson takes you through each proof and its logical force.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first proof
Read the opening objection and the first proof from the verse 'وكانوا لا يستطيعون سمعاً'. Notice how Baqillani interprets 'hearing' as acceptance.
This proof establishes that 'inability' can refer to acceptance, not just physical hearing.
2
Understand the second proof
Examine the second proof from the verse about justice between wives. God commands justice while informing us we cannot achieve it perfectly.
This shows that God can command what is beyond full human capacity.
3
Analyse the third proof
Study the third proof from the believers' supplication 'لا تحملنا ما لا طاقة لنا به'. Baqillani argues that if such burdening were injustice, the believers would have asked God not to oppress, but they did not.
God praises the believers for this supplication, implying the request is not for avoidance of injustice.
4
Reflect on the overall argument
Consider how the three proofs together show that burdening beyond capacity is compatible with God's justice and wisdom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : تقولون إن الله يكلف عباده ما لا يطيقون حسب ما ذكرتم. فما الدليل على جواز هذا التكليف وحسنه من القديم؟ قيل له : قوله تعالى : وكانوا لا يستطيعون سمعاً. والسمع ها هنا القبول باتفاق، لأن الكفَّار قد كانوا يسمعون ما يؤمرون به وينهون عنه ويدركون دعوة الرسل. وهو محمول على تأويل قولهم: «فلان ما يقال له»، و «لا يسمع ما نقوله شيئاً» أي : لا يقبل ذلك، وليس يريدون أنه لا يدرك الأصوات. ويدل على ذلك أيضاً قوله : ولن تستطيعوا أن تعدلوا بين النساء ولو حرصتم. وقد أمر الله بالعدل بينهنّ وأوجبه مع إخباره أنا لا نستطيع ذلك. ويدل على صحة ذلك من القديم، وأنه عدل وحكمة، إخباره عمن أحسن الثناء عليه والمدح له أنهم رغبوا إليه في أن لا يُحمّلهم ما لا طاقة لهم به. فقال إخباراً عنهم : ربنا ولا تحملنا ما لا طاقة لنا به. فلو كان تكليف ما لا يطاق ظلماً وعبثاً وقبيحاً من الله تعالى، لكانوا قد رغبوا إليه في أن لا يظلمهم ولا يسفه عليهم ولا يوجب من الأوامر ما يخرج به عن حدّ الحكمة. والله أجل من أن يثني على قوم أجازوا ذلك عليه. فدل هذا أيضاً على ما وصفناه.
If someone says: 'You claim that God burdens His servants with what they cannot bear as you mentioned. What is the proof for the permissibility and goodness of this burden from the Eternal?' It is said to him: His statement the Most High: 'And they were not able to hear.' And 'hearing' here means acceptance by agreement, because the disbelievers used to hear what they were commanded and forbidden and understood the call of the messengers. And it is interpreted according to their saying: 'So-and-so is not spoken to,' and 'He does not hear anything we say,' meaning he does not accept it; they do not mean that he does not perceive sounds. And that is also indicated by His statement: 'And you will never be able to be just between women even if you desire.' And God commanded justice between them and made it obligatory while informing us that we cannot do that. And the correctness of that from the Eternal, that it is justice and wisdom, is indicated by His informing about those whom He praised and commended, that they beseeched Him not to burden them with what they cannot bear. He said informing about them: 'Our Lord, do not burden us with what we cannot bear.' If burdening with what cannot be borne were oppression, frivolity, and evil from God the Most High, they would have beseeched Him not to oppress them, not to treat them foolishly, and not to impose commands that would take Him outside the bounds of wisdom. And God is too exalted to praise a people who allowed that against Him. So this also indicates what we have described.
Source pages p. 337

Commentary
This passage provides three Quranic proofs for the permissibility of God burdening beyond capacity. First, the verse about disbelievers not being able to hear (Q 18:101) is interpreted as inability to accept, not physical hearing. Second, the verse about not being able to be fully just among wives (Q 4:129) while being commanded to be just. Third, the believers' supplication 'do not burden us with what we cannot bear' (Q 2:286) is used: if such burdening were unjust, they would have asked God not to oppress, but instead they asked only for themselves, and God praised them for it.

Key Terms
لا يستطيعون سمعاً
القبول
عدل
حكمة
ظلم
عبث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'inability' always refers to physical impossibility.
Correction: The verses show that 'inability' can refer to moral or psychological capacity, as with the disbelievers' inability to accept faith.

Checkpoint
What is the interpretation of 'سمعاً' in the verse 'وكانوا لا يستطيعون سمعاً'?
A) Physical hearing.
B) Acceptance.
C) Understanding.
D) Both A and C.

Key Takeaway
The Quran itself shows that God can command what is beyond human capacity, and this is consistent with His wisdom and justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a command of Allah that seems beyond your ability—like perfect justice or complete patience—do you despair, or do you strive knowing that the command itself is a mercy to draw you closer? What change in your heart would make you approach such commands with hope rather than frustration?
?
The believers in the Quran asked not to be burdened beyond capacity. Have you ever truly felt that a divine command was impossible for you? How can you reconcile that feeling with the knowledge that Allah's commands are always just and wise, even when you struggle?
?
If you were to examine your own life, are there areas where you have given up on a divine command because you thought it was beyond you? What would it mean for your faith to take the first step in obedience, trusting that Allah rewards the effort even if perfection is unattainable?

Quranic Evidence for Divine Creation of Actions
Baqillani presents Quranic evidence and counters an alternative interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani uses the verse 'Allah created you and what you do' to argue that Allah creates human actions, and how he refutes the interpretation that it refers to idols.

Core Idea
The verse 'Allah created you and what you do' proves actions are created, not just objects.

Imam Baqillani now turns to Quranic evidence to support the doctrine that Allah creates human actions. He cites a key verse and immediately addresses a potential misinterpretation. This lesson walks through the proof and the refutation, showing the precision of kalam reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic proof
Read the verse 'And Allah created you and what you do' and the author's claim that it shows Allah creates our very actions.
The author uses the word 'what you do' to refer to the actions themselves.
2
Notice the supporting evidence
See how Baqillani cites another verse about reward ('Reward for what they used to do') to clarify that the object of creation is the action itself, not an object.
The reward is placed on the actions, not on objects.
3
Analyze the objection and response
Understand the objection that 'what you do' could mean the idols they made, and the reply that idols are bodies, not actions.
Bodies cannot be considered acts of worshipers in reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على ذلك أيضاً من القرآن قوله تعالى : والله خلقكم وما تعملون . فأخبر أنه خالق لنفس عملنا كما قال: جزاء بما كانوا يعملون، فأوقع الجزاء على نفس أعمالهم. فإن قالوا ما أنكرتم أن يكون أراد أنه خلق الأصنام التي عملوا قيل لهم : الأصنام أجسام، والأجسام لا يجوز أن تكون أعمالاً للعباد على الحقيقة.
And among what also indicates that from the Qur'an is His statement, exalted: 'And Allah created you and what you do.' So He informed that He is the creator of our very action, just as He said: 'Reward for what they used to do,' so He placed the reward upon their very actions. If they say: What prevents you from saying that He meant that He created the idols that they made? It is said to them: Idols are bodies, and bodies cannot be actions of the servants in reality.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage adduces Quranic evidence from the verse 'And Allah created you and what you do' (al-Saffat 96). The author interprets 'what you do' as the actions themselves, not the objects. He supports this by citing another verse that places reward on 'what they used to do,' showing the act itself is the object. Then an objection is raised: perhaps 'what you do' refers to the idols they made. The reply is that idols are bodies, and bodies cannot be acts of worshipers in reality, thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
وما تعملون
خالق
أعمال
الأصنام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that 'what you do' in the verse refers to the objects that people make, such as idols.
Correction: The author argues that the verse refers to the actions themselves, not the objects, because idols are bodies and cannot be considered actions of the servants.

Checkpoint
How does the author refute the objection that 'what you do' in the verse refers to idols?
A) Idols are not created by God
B) Idols are bodies, not acts
C) The verse is metaphorical
D) Idols are eternal

Key Takeaway
The verse 'Allah created you and what you do' is taken as proof that Allah creates human actions, not just the objects of those actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah creates both your good deeds and your sins, how does that change the way you ask for forgiveness or gratitude? Will you now thank Him for every good action and seek refuge from every sin, knowing He is the source of both?
?
When you commit a sin, do you blame Allah for creating it? How does this verse force you to take responsibility despite believing in divine creation? What does that mean for your repentance?
?
The verse says 'Reward for what they used to do' – your very actions are the basis for judgment. Are you living today as if every action you do is being created for a purpose? How can you align your will with Allah's creation of your actions?

Objection from 'talaqqafu' and Linguistic Refutation
Objection using al-A'raf 117 and response distinguishing act from object

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani uses a linguistic argument to refute the objection based on the verse 'talaqqafu ma yafikun' by distinguishing between the act and the object.

Core Idea
The verse refers to the fabricated thing, not the act of fabrication.

This passage presents a clever objection from opponents who cite the verse about Moses' staff swallowing the magicians' fabrications. Baqillani responds with a precise linguistic point: the Arabic construction 'ma yaf'alun' denotes the object of the action, not the action itself. By examining similar constructions like 'ma yakulun' (what they eat) and 'ma yanhitun' (what they carve), the error becomes clear.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully along with the literal translation. Notice the question-and-answer structure.
Pay attention to the key terms 'يأفكون' and 'مأفوك'.
2
Identify the objection
The objectors cite verse 7:117. Ask yourself: what do they think this verse proves?
They think it implies that the act of fabrication (ifk) exists.
3
Understand the linguistic refutation
Baqillani argues that 'ma yafikun' is the object (mafuk), just as 'ma yakulun' is the eaten. Grasp this analogy.
The same pattern applies to 'ma yashrabun' (what they drink) and 'ma yadribun' (what they strike).
4
Apply the second analogy
Consider the verse 'Do you worship what you carve?' (37:95). Notice that 'ma tanhitun' (what you carve) is the carved object, not the act of carving.
This reinforces the linguistic point.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Baqillani declares the objection invalid. Ensure you see why the linguistic distinction is decisive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أليس قد قال تعالى : تلقف ما يأفكون . قيل لهم : أجل، لأن الله تعالى ما ذكر إفكهم، بل ذكر مأفوكهم، لأن ما يأفكون هو المأفوك كما أن ما يأكلون ويشربون ويضربون هو المأكول والمشروب والمضروب وكذلك قوله : أتعبدون ما تنحتون . إنما يعرض تعالى فيه لذكر النحت وإنما ذكر المنحوت، لأن ما ينحتون هو منحوتهم لا نحتهم . فبطل تعلقهم وتعليلهم.
If they say: Did He not say, exalted: 'It swallows what they fabricate'? It is said to them: Indeed, because God, exalted, did not mention their fabrication, but rather mentioned their fabricated thing, because 'what they fabricate' is the fabricated thing just as 'what they eat and drink and strike' is the eaten, drunk, and struck. And similarly His statement: 'Do you worship what you carve?' He only mentions carving therein, but He mentioned the carved thing, because 'what they carve' is their carved thing, not their carving. So their attachment and their argument are invalidated.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage presents another objection and its linguistic refutation. The objectors ask about the verse 'It swallows what they fabricate' (al-A'raf 117), thinking it implies the act of fabrication. The answer is that the verse does not mention the act of fabrication (ifk) but the fabricated thing (mafuk). The linguistic point is that 'ma yafikun' (what they fabricate) is the object, like 'ma yakulun' (what they eat) is the eaten. Similarly, 'Do you worship what you carve?' (al-Saffat 95) mentions the carved object, not the carving. Thus their objection collapses.

Key Terms
يأفكون
مأفوك
ينحتون
منحوت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the phrase 'ma yafikun' refers to the act of fabrication (ifk) itself, implying that the magicians are creators.
Correction: In Arabic, 'ma yaf'alun' constructions denote the object of the action, not the action. The verse refers to the fabricated things, not the act.

Checkpoint
What is the linguistic argument against the objection from 'talaqqafu ma yafikun'?
A) The verb is passive
B) 'Ma yafikun' means the fabricated thing, not the act of fabrication
C) The verse is abrogated
D) The word is ambiguous

Key Takeaway
The linguistic form 'ma yaf'alun' refers to the object of the action, not the action itself, which refutes the objection based on the verse.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read 'It swallows what they fabricate' (al-A'raf 7:117), did you ever pause to consider that the verse might be misused to grant the magicians real power? Now that Baqillani has clarified the linguistic point, examine your own heart: are there areas where you inadvertently attribute independent power to created things (like wealth, health, or people) that belongs only to Allah? What specific step will you take today to realign your trust in Allah alone?
?
Baqillani uses precise, analytical reasoning to defend tawhid against a seemingly minor linguistic objection. Reflect on your own efforts to understand your faith: are you satisfied with surface-level knowledge, or do you dig deeper into the proofs that safeguard your iman? What is one objection to Islamic belief you have encountered, and how can you apply Baqillani's care to uncover its flaw rather than dismissing it casually?
?
The verse 'Do you worship what you carve?' (al-Saffat 37:95) redirects attention from the act of carving to the carved object. In your life, do you ever focus on your own actions (deeds, worship) to the point of forgetting that the object of worship is Allah Himself? How can you ensure that your worship remains centered on Him, not on your own performance? Commit to one concrete change in your daily 'ibadah to make it more Allah-focused.

The Qur'anic Proof from Saba' 18 that Determination is Creation
Quranic proof connecting determination and creation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani uses the verse from Surah Saba' to establish that Allah's determination (taqdir) is an act of creation.

Core Idea
Divine determination is not planning—it is creating.

This final proof from the Qur'an is concise yet powerful. Imam Baqillani cites the verse in which Allah says He 'determined the journey' in the land of Saba'. He then clarifies that this determination from Allah is itself the creation of the thing. Let's examine how this verse supports the doctrine that Allah creates all actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and its implication
Read the Arabic verse 'Wa qadarna fiha al-sayr' and its translation. Notice the key word 'qadarna' (We determined).
The verse is from Surah Saba', verse 18.
2
Examine the author's equation
The author explicitly states: 'And determination from Him is the creation of the thing.' This is the core of the argument—taqdir equals khalq.
This is a direct claim that determination is a form of creation.
3
Reflect on the doctrinal significance
Ask yourself why this matters for divine attributes. If determination is creation, then God's act of determining is not separate from His creative act—it is the same.
This reinforces that Allah creates all things, including human actions.
4
Consider the common misunderstanding
Some might think taqdir is merely planning or setting a measure. The author corrects this by equating it with creation itself.
This misunderstanding is addressed in the lesson's misconception section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويدل على ذلك أيضاً من القرآن قوله عزّ وجلّ: وقدرنا فيها السير سيروا فيها ليالي وأياماً آمنين والتقدير منه هو خلق الشيء.
And it also indicates that from the Qur'an is His statement, mighty and majestic: 'And We determined in them the journey; travel in them secure by night and day.' And determination from Him is the creation of the thing.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This final Quranic proof cites 'And We determined in them the journey; travel in them secure by night and day' (Saba' 18). The author explains that determination (al-taqdir) from Allah is a form of creation (khalq al-shay'). Thus the verse shows that determining the journey is an act of creation, supporting that God creates acts.

Key Terms
تقدير
خلق
سير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think taqdir is merely planning or setting a measure, not an act of creation.
Correction: The author explicitly states that determination from Allah is the creation of the thing, showing that taqdir is a creative act.

Checkpoint
What does the verse 'Qadarna fiha al-sayr' show about God's action?
A) God creates journeys
B) Determination is a form of creation
C) God gives directions
D) Travel is forbidden

Key Takeaway
Allah's determination (taqdir) is an act of creation, as shown by the Qur'anic verse in Surah Saba'.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a significant event in your life that you attributed to 'fate' or 'qadr'. Do you now see that it was not just a plan but a direct creation by Allah, moment by moment? How does this change your gratitude and submission?
?
If Allah's determination creates every detail, what does that say about your own efforts? Are you ever tempted to think your actions are independent? Confess that sincerely to yourself, and commit to seeing every outcome—good or bad—as Allah's creation.
?
When you plan for the future, do you truly believe that Allah's determination is a creative act? Will you pray differently tonight, asking not just for guidance but for His creative determination to shape your steps? Write down one area where you will trust His creative determination more.

Refuting the Qadariyya Proof: 'And You Create Falsehood'
Baqillani refutes the Qadariyya interpretation of 'takhluquna ifkan'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Qadariyya interpretation of the verse 'takhluquna ifkan' by demonstrating that 'khalq' here means fabrication, not creation.

Core Idea
You create falsehood means you fabricate lies, not that you have creative power.

The Qadariyya used the verse 'And you create falsehood' to argue that humans create their own actions. Baqillani responds by clarifying the linguistic meaning of 'khalq' in this context. In this lesson, you will see how he dismantles their proof using the Quran itself and Arabic usage.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Qadariyya proof
Recognize that the Qadariyya cited the verse 'takhluquna ifkan' to claim that humans have creative power over their actions.
This is the sect's argument that Baqillani is refuting.
2
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Baqillani first states their argument, then gives the answer.
3
Identify the linguistic move
Baqillani says 'khalq' can mean lying and fabrication. This redefines the verb in the verse.
The key term is 'اختلاق' (fabrication).
4
Examine the supporting evidence
Baqillani cites two other Quranic verses and a common phrase to confirm this meaning.
See 'إن هذا إلا اختلاق' and 'إن هذا إلا خلق الأولين'.
5
Reflect on the refutation
Consider why this interpretation blocks the Qadariyya inference. They cannot claim creative power if the verse means 'you fabricate lies'.
This lesson shows how linguistics can refute theological errors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ذكر آيات من القرآن يحتج بها القدرية في أن العباد يخلقون أفعالهم.
استدلوا بقوله تعالى: (وتخلقون إفكاً). فالجواب عنه أنه تعالى عنى: إنكم تختلقون كذباً، أي: تتخرصون وتكذبون كذباً. فالخلق يكون بمعنى الكذب والاختلاق. ومنه قوله تعالى: (إن هذا إلا اختلاق) و (إن هذا إلا خلق الأولين) يعنون كذبهم. وقولهم: هذا حديث مخلوق، يريدون به هذا المعنى.
Chapter mentioning verses from the Quran by which the Qadariyya argue that servants create their own actions. They adduce His saying, the Exalted: 'And you create falsehood' (takhluquna ifkan). The answer to that is that He, the Exalted, meant: 'You fabricate lies', i.e., you pretend and lie, a lie. So 'khalq' can mean lying and fabrication. And from that is His saying, the Exalted: 'This is nothing but fabrication' (in hadha illa ikhtilaq) and 'This is nothing but the fabrication of the ancients' (in hadha illa khuluq al-awwaleen), meaning their lies. And their saying: 'This is a fabricated hadith' (hadha hadith makhluq) intends this meaning.
Source pages p. 353

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a Qadariyya proof text. The Qadariyya cite the verse 'And you create falsehood' (Quran 29:17) to claim that humans create their own actions (since 'takhluquna' implies creation). The author responds by explaining that the verb 'takhluqun' here means 'you fabricate lies,' not 'you create' in the ontological sense. He supports this by noting that the word 'khalq' can mean lying and fabrication, and he cites two other Quranic verses ('This is nothing but fabrication' and 'This is nothing but the fabrication of the ancients') where the same root is used to mean fabricated lies. Additionally, he points to the common expression 'a fabricated hadith' (hadith makhluq) to confirm this linguistic usage.

Key Terms

اختلاق
كذب
إفك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believe the verse 'takhluquna ifkan' proves that humans create their own actions.
Correction: The verse uses 'khalq' in the sense of fabricating lies, not ontological creation, as shown by Quranic and linguistic evidence.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the word 'takhluquna' in the verse 'Wa takhluquna ifkan'?
A) As referring to the creation of physical objects.
B) As meaning 'you fabricate lies'.
C) As meaning 'you discriminate'.
D) As meaning 'you commit sins'.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani refutes the Qadariyya proof by showing the verse uses 'khalq' in the sense of fabrication, not ontological creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever interpreted a Qur'anic verse to support your own desires or opinions rather than seeking its true meaning? How did you justify that to yourself? Will you commit to seeking scholarly tafsir before assuming a meaning?
?
The Qadariyya used this verse to support their view, ignoring the linguistic context. How often do you find yourself reading your own preconceptions into Allah's words? What practical step will you take to ensure you submit to the text rather than making it submit to you?
?
Baqillani shows that even a single word can be misunderstood if taken out of context. Do you approach the Qur'an with humility, ready to be corrected by scholars, or with pride in your own understanding? Will you seek knowledge from those grounded in the tradition?

Interpreting Creation Not in Vain: Purpose of Reward and Punishment
Baqillani interprets 'not in vain' as referring to the purpose of reward and punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's interpretation of the Quranic statement that creation is not in vain, as referring to the divine purpose of reward and punishment, and how this refutes those who deny the afterlife.

Core Idea
'Not in vain' means creation has a purpose: rewarding the righteous and punishing the wicked.

This lesson examines a key objection against the necessity of reward and punishment. The objectors use Quranic verses that say creation is not in vain or is by truth to argue that there should be no falsehood in creation. Baqillani clarifies that these verses are about God's purpose in creating, not about the absence of evil. By reading carefully, you will see how he defends the doctrine of the afterlife.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and verses cited
Read the passage and note the two Quranic verses quoted: 'We did not create ... in vain' (38:27) and 'except with truth' (15:85). Pay attention to how the objectors use these verses to argue against the presence of falsehood in creation.
The objectors equate 'vain' (bāṭil) with human sinful actions.
2
Identify the objector's logic
Understand the objectors' reasoning: If creation is not in vain and is based on truth, then the actions of servants that are vain (bāṭil) would contradict the verses. They imply that human sins make creation pointless.
This logic assumes that everything within creation must reflect the purpose of creation.
3
Follow Baqillani's response
Baqillani explains that 'not in vain' means God created with the intention of rewarding the obedient and punishing the disobedient. The verse is a refutation of those who deny resurrection and judgement, not a statement that no evil exists.
The key is the phrase 'while He does not intend to reward...' – creation's purpose is tied to the afterlife.
4
Connect to the broader doctrine
See how this answer defends the necessity of the Hereafter. The objection is invalid because it misinterprets the verse. Creation's purpose is precisely to enable reward and punishment, which requires judgement.
This lesson reinforces the importance of reward and punishment as the ultimate purpose of creation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أفليس قد قال الله عزّ وجلّ : وما خلقنا السموات والأرض وما بينهما باطلا ذلك ظنُّ الذين كفروا . وقال : وما خلقنا السموات والأرض وما بينهما إلا بالحق . والباطل من أفعال العباد ليس بحق . قيل لهم : معنى ذلك أنه ما خلق السموات والأرض وما بينهما وهو لا يريد إثابة المتقين الطائعين ولا مجازاة المسيئين المذنبين والكافرين على ما يتوهمه من زعم أنه لا حشر ولا نشر ولا ثواب ولا عقاب . فلذلك قال تعالى : وذلك ظن الذين كفروا فويل للذين كفروا من النار ، يعني : من إنكارهم الثواب والجزاء والعقاب .
If they say: Did not Allah, Mighty and Majestic, say: 'And We did not create the heavens and the earth and what is between them in vain; that is the assumption of those who disbelieve' (Quran 38:27), and He said: 'And We did not create the heavens and the earth and what is between them except with truth' (Quran 15:85). And vain (bāṭil) from the actions of the servants is not truth. It is said to them: The meaning of that is that He did not create the heavens and the earth and what is between them while He does not intend to reward the God-fearing obedient ones nor to recompense the evil-doing sinners and disbelievers, according to what is assumed by one who claims that there is no gathering, no resurrection, no reward and no punishment. Therefore He said, Exalted: 'And that is the assumption of those who disbelieve, so woe to those who disbelieve from the Fire' (Quran 38:27), meaning: because of their denial of reward, recompense, and punishment.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This is a third objection and answer. The objectors cite verses stating that creation is not in vain (bāṭil) and that it is by truth (ḥaqq), whereas human sins are bāṭil (false/foolish). They argue that if human sins are bāṭil, then creation would include bāṭil, contradicting the verses. The response explains that 'not in vain' means God created with a purpose: to reward the obedient and punish the disobedient. It does not mean that everything within creation is true. The bāṭil of human actions does not negate the truth of creation's purpose. The verse is a refutation of those who deny resurrection and judgement, not a statement that no evil exists. Thus the objection is invalid.

Key Terms

حق
جزاء
ثواب
عقاب
حشر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'creation is not in vain' means that everything in creation is good and there should be no evil or sin.
Correction: Baqillani explains that the verse refers to God's overarching purpose of reward and punishment, not that every individual action is true or good. Evil actions are part of a broader plan that includes judgement.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, the verse 'ما خلقنا السموات والأرض وما بينهما باطلا' means that:
A) Nothing in creation is pointless
B) God created with the intention of rewarding and punishing
C) There is no evil in creation
D) Human actions are always true

Key Takeaway
The Quranic statement that creation is not in vain affirms God's purpose of reward and punishment, not the absence of evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see injustice or evil in the world, do you feel that creation has lost its purpose? How does Baqillani's explanation that creation's purpose is judgement, not perfection, challenge that feeling? Will you now see such events as evidence that judgement must come rather than as evidence that God created in vain?
?
Do you live today as if the ultimate purpose of your existence is to be rewarded or punished in the afterlife? Or do you act as if this world is the final arena, making your actions seem without eternal consequence? What would change if you truly believed that every moment is part of God's plan for your eventual recompense?
?
The objectors in this passage assumed that if creation is true, then every human action must be true. Have you ever judged God's creation by the flawed actions of people, concluding that it is all meaningless? How can you shift your perspective to see the whole picture of judgement that gives meaning even to sin?

Explaining the 'Twisting Tongues' Verse
Baqillani explains the verse about twisting tongues as referring to Jewish distortion of the Torah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Mu'tazilite misinterpretation of the 'twisting tongues' verse and why it is about textual falsification, not the creation of actions.

Core Idea
The verse is about distorting scripture, not about who creates actions.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a key objection from opponents who cite Quran 3:78 to argue that humans create their own speech. He demonstrates that the verse actually refers to the Jews' deliberate falsification of the Torah. Understanding this refutation clarifies the correct method of interpreting ambiguous verses and protects against theological error.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's objection
Read the question posed by the opponents: they cite Quran 3:78 and ask for its meaning. Notice that they are using this verse to argue against the doctrine that God creates actions.
The opponents likely are Mu'tazilites who believe humans create their own actions.
2
Understand Baqillani's interpretation
Baqillani explains that the verse refers to the Jews who twisted their tongues while reciting the Torah, altering its words and lying about its content. They claimed those distortions were from God.
The key words are 'they lied about the Torah, distorted it, concealed the description of the Prophet.'
3
Note the explicit rejection
God denies that He revealed the Torah in that altered manner or commanded them to say such things. The verse is a condemnation of falsification, not a statement about who creates actions.
4
Recognize the argumentative context
Baqillani clarifies that the original disputation was not about the creation of actions; thus the ignorance is not supported by this verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة وإن قالوا فما معنى قوله : يلوون ألسنتهم بالكتاب لتحسبوه من الكتاب وما هو من الكتاب ويقولون هو من عند الله وما هو من عند الله ؟ قيل لهم : معنى ذلك أنهم كذبوا التوراة وحرّفوها وكتموا صفة النبي صلّى الله عليه وآله وسلم والبشارة به، وادعوا أن الله تبارك وتعالى كذلك أنزل التوراة وتعبدهم أن يقولوه. فأنكر الله ذلك وقال وما هو من عند الله أي لم أنزل التوراة كذلك ولا تعبدتهم بالإخبار بما أخبروا به. ولم تكن المناظرة في خلق الأفعال، فيكون للجهال في ذلك متعلق .
A question: And if they say: What is the meaning of His statement: 'They twist their tongues with the Book that you may suppose it from the Book while it is not from the Book, and they say: It is from God while it is not from God'? It is said to them: The meaning of that is that they lied about the Torah and distorted it and concealed the description of the Prophet, may God bless him and his family and grant them peace, and the good news of him, and they claimed that God, blessed and exalted, revealed the Torah in that manner and commanded them to say it. So God denied that and said: 'And it is not from God', i.e., I did not reveal the Torah in that manner nor did I command them to report what they reported. And the argument was not about the creation of actions, so that the ignorant would have a support in that.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is an answer to an opponent's objection. The opponents cite the verse from Surah Al 'Imran (3:78) about those who twist their tongues with the Book, making it appear as scripture when it is not. They interpret this as evidence that God does not create human actions (since the twisting is attributed to them, not to God). Baqillani refutes this by giving the correct exegesis: the verse refers to the Jews who altered the Torah and concealed the prophecies of Muhammad. They falsely claimed that God revealed those distortions. The verse is not about the metaphysical issue of the creation of actions; it is about textual falsification. Therefore, the opponents have no valid support from this verse for their doctrine.

Key Terms
الوون
تحريف
توراة
بشارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse about 'twisting tongues' proves that humans create their own speech and actions independently of God.
Correction: The verse actually refers to the Jews distorting the Torah and falsely attributing their alterations to God. It is about textual falsification, not the creation of actions.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the correct interpretation of the verse about 'twisting tongues with the Book'?
A) It refers to Jews distorting the Torah and hiding prophecies.
B) It refers to Muslims misquoting the Quran.
C) It proves that humans create their own speech.
D) It is about grammatical mistakes in recitation.

Key Takeaway
The verse about 'twisting tongues' refers to Jewish distortion of the Torah, not to the metaphysical issue of who creates human actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In what ways have you twisted your tongue or concealed the truth about Islam to avoid discomfort or gain acceptance? What will you do this week to speak the truth fully, even if it costs you?
?
When you read the Quran, do you rely on sound tafsir or have you ever twisted a verse to support a personal opinion? Repent and commit to learning the correct interpretation before you speak.
?
The Jews claimed that their distortions were from God. Have you ever asserted something as 'Islamic' without verifying it? How will you ensure that what you attribute to God is truly from Him?

4 min
Refuting a Misinterpretation of Al-Imran 3:78
Baqillani explains that the verse about distorting scripture does not concern the debate on creation of acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani refutes a potential misinterpretation of Al-Imran 3:78 in the debate on the creation of human acts.

Core Idea
A verse about scripture distortion does not prove human self-creation of acts.

This lesson addresses a common yet mistaken use of a Qur'anic verse. Some might argue that Al-Imran 3:78 supports the idea that humans create their own actions, but Imam al-Baqillani shows that the verse actually rebukes the Jews for falsifying scripture. Let's see how he closes off this argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the English translation. Pay attention to the verse reference and the phrase 'creation of acts'.
The passage is dense; read slowly.
2
Identify the objection
Notice that someone could use the verse to argue that humans claim actions are from Allah when they are not, implying humans create their own acts. Baqillani is answering this implicit objection.
The objection is not directly stated but derived from the verse.
3
Understand Baqillani's refutation
Baqillani explains the verse refers to Jews distorting the Torah and falsely attributing words to Allah. He explicitly states this has nothing to do with the debate on the creation of acts.
This prevents the ignorant from using the verse as evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لتحسبوه من الكتاب وما هو من الكتاب ويقولون هو من عند الله وما هو من عند الله؟ قيل لهم: معنى ذلك أنهم كذبوا التوراة وحرّفوها وكتموا صفة النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم والبشارة به، وادعوا أن الله تبارك وتعالى كذلك أنزل التوراة وتعبدهم أن يقولوه. فأنكر الله ذلك وقال: وما هو من عند الله أي لم أنزل التوراة كذلك ولا تعبدتهم بالإخبار بما أخبروا به. ولم تكن المناظرة في خلق الأفعال، فيكون للجهال في ذلك متعلق.
They consider it to be from the Book when it is not from the Book, and they say it is from Allah when it is not from Allah? It was said to them: The meaning of that is that they lied against the Torah, altered it, concealed the description of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) and the glad tidings of him, and claimed that Allah, blessed and exalted, sent down the Torah like that and obligated them to say it. So Allah denied that and said: 'And it is not from Allah' meaning 'I did not send down the Torah like that, nor did I obligate them to inform with what they informed.' And the debate was not about the creation of acts, such that the ignorant would have a point of attachment in that.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer. The objection is implicitly drawn from the verse (Al-Imran 3:78), which might be used by some to argue that the creation of acts is not from Allah. Baqillani explains that the verse actually rebukes the Jews for distorting the Torah and falsely attributing words to Allah, not for any claim about the creation of human acts. He then explicitly states that this verse has no bearing on the debate about the creation of acts (خلق الأفعال), thereby closing off a potential argument for those who advocate that humans create their own acts. The lesson defends the integrity of scripture and refutes a misapplication of the verse.

Interpreting Musa's Statement: 'This is from the Work of Satan'
Baqillani explains why Musa attributed an action to Satan, not to Allah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani interprets Musa's attribution of an action to Satan as a moral and religious classification, not a denial of divine creation.

Core Idea
Attributing evil to Satan is moral, not creative; Allah alone creates.

Musa's statement in the Quran seems to attribute an action to Satan rather than to Allah. Does this mean Satan creates some acts? Baqillani addresses this objection by distinguishing between moral attribution and creative agency. He shows that the prophets and companions used such language without compromising tawhid.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Begin by reading the passage carefully, noting the question and Baqillani's structured response.
The objector cites Quran 28:15.
2
Identify the consensus argument
Notice that Baqillani starts by stating that the Ummah agrees the physical act is not created by Satan. This refutes any literal reading.
3
Understand the moral attribution
Baqillani explains that Musa meant the act is of the kind of evil Satan does and is from Satan's religion, not that Satan created it.
This is the key interpretive move.
4
Note the warning against shirk
Baqillani emphasizes that Musa did not intend to deny Allah's creation or associate partners, as that would be shirk unbecoming of a prophet.
5
See the companion support
The passage ends with a quote from Abu Bakr and Ibn Mas'ud using similar language, confirming the interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فإن قالوا: فما معنى قوله: فوکزه موسى فقضى عليه قال هذا من عمل الشيطان؟ فكيف لم يقل «هذا من عمل الرحمن»؟. قيل لهم: لا خلاف بين الأمة أن وكز موسى القبطي ليس من عمل الشيطان، وخلقه فلا تعلق لكم في الظاهر. وإنما أراد عليه السلام أنه من جنس الشر الذي يفعله الشيطان وأنه من دين الشيطان ومما يأمر به ويدعو إليه وأنه ليس من دين الرحمن ولا مما تعبد به ودعا إليه وضمن الثواب عليه. ولم يرد إخراج الباري عزّ وجلّ عن الخلق وإثبات شريك له فيه من شيطان أو غيره. لأن هذا شرك من قائله، وهو نبي يجل عن هذه الصفة. وهذا هو معنى قول أبي بكر الصديق وابن مسعود وغيرهما من الصحابة: «وإن يكن خطأ فمن الشيطان».
Question: What is the meaning of His statement: 'So Moses struck him and finished him; he said: This is from the work of Satan.' Why did he not say 'This is from the work of the Most Merciful'? It was said to them: There is no disagreement among the Ummah that Moses' striking of the Copt is not from the work of Satan, nor his creation, so you have no attachment in the apparent. Rather, he (peace be upon him) meant that it is of the kind of evil that Satan does, and that it is from the religion of Satan and from what he commands and calls to, and that it is not from the religion of the Most Merciful nor from what He obligated and called to and promised reward upon. And he did not intend to remove the Creator, mighty and majestic, from creation and to establish a partner with Him in it from Satan or other. Because that would be shirk from its speaker, and he is a prophet, exalted above this attribute. And this is the meaning of Abu Bakr As-Siddiq and Ibn Mas'ud and other companions: 'And if it is a mistake, it is from Satan.'
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a structured objection and answer. The objector cites the verse where Musa strikes the Egyptian and then says 'This is from the work of Satan' (Al-Qasas 28:15), asking why he did not attribute it to the Most Merciful. Baqillani's response begins by stating the consensus that the physical act of striking is not created by Satan. He then explains that Musa's statement is a moral and religious classification: the act is of the same kind as evil deeds that Satan commands, and it belongs to Satan's religion, not Allah's. He adds that Musa did not intend to deny Allah's creation of the act or to associate a partner with Him, as that would be shirk unbecoming of a prophet. Finally, he supports this interpretation with a quote from Abu Bakr and Ibn Mas'ud, who said 'If it is a mistake, it is from Satan.' The lesson defends tawhid by showing that moral attribution to Satan does not negate divine creation.

Key Terms

دين الشيطان
دين الرحمن
الوكز

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Musa's words imply Satan creates some acts.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies it is a moral, not creative, attribution; Allah alone creates.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what did Musa mean by saying 'this is from the work of Satan'?
A) That Satan created the act.
B) That the act is of the kind of evil that Satan does and is from his religion.
C) That Allah had no part in the act.
D) That the act was a sin that could not be forgiven.

Key Takeaway
Musa's statement 'this is from the work of Satan' means the act is of the kind of evil Satan commands, not that Satan creates it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
