Interpreting 'Except to Be Obeyed by Allah's Permission'
Baqillani offers two interpretations of the verse in An-Nisa 64.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two possible interpretations of the phrase 'by Allah's permission' in the verse about obedience to prophets, as explained by Imam Baqillani.

Core Idea
Baqillani shows that 'Allah's permission' can mean His knowledge or His command.

This lesson examines a question about a key Qur'anic verse. The verse says that messengers are sent 'except to be obeyed by Allah's permission.' What does this mean? Does it imply that obedience only happens when Allah directly wills it? Imam Baqillani offers two careful interpretations that preserve Allah's sovereignty while making sense of the text. Let's explore them.

Guided Path
1
Read and understand the objection
The objection asks for the meaning of the verse. Read the Arabic passage and translation to grasp the question.
Notice that the objection is presented as a hypothetical question.
2
Study the first interpretation
Baqillani's first interpretation limits the obedience to those whom Allah knows will obey. Consider how this preserves divine knowledge.
3
Study the second interpretation
The second interpretation says the verse means the prophet commands obedience, and 'permission' refers to Allah's command. Compare the two interpretations.
Both interpretations avoid implying that Allah's permission is limited or contingent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فإن قالوا: فما معنى قوله: وما أرسلنا من رسول إلا ليطاع بإذن الله؟. قيل لهم: معنى ذلك: إلا ليطيعه من في المعلوم أنه يطيع وينقاد دون من علم أنه لا يطيع ولا ينقاد. ويمكن أن يكون التأويل في ذلك: إلا ليأمر بطاعته والانقياد له فيكون معنى «إِلَّا لِيُطَاعَ»: إلا ليأمر المكلفين بطاعته جميعهم لتقع الطاعة من جميعهم.
Question: What is the meaning of His statement: 'And We did not send any messenger except to be obeyed by Allah's permission'? It was said to them: The meaning of that: except that he be obeyed by those whom it is known that they will obey and submit, excluding those whom He knows will not obey nor submit. And it is possible that the interpretation of that is: except that he commands obedience and submission to him, so the meaning of 'except to be obeyed' is: except that he commands all obligated ones to obey him, so that obedience occurs from all of them.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer concerning the verse in An-Nisa (4:64). The objection raises the question of how to understand 'except to be obeyed by Allah's permission.' Baqillani offers two possible interpretations. The first interpretation is that the verse refers only to those whom Allah knows will obey – i.e., the obedience of the believers – while those whom Allah knows will disobey are excluded. The second interpretation is that the verse means that the prophet is sent to command all people to obey him, and the phrase 'by Allah's permission' indicates that the command is issued with His leave, and obedience is expected from all, though not all comply. Both interpretations preserve Allah's sovereignty and avoid any implication that His permission is limited in a way that contradicts His omnipotence.

Key Terms
بإذن الله
في المعلوم
الانقياد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'by Allah's permission' means obedience only occurs if Allah directly causes it.
Correction: Baqillani shows it can refer to divine knowledge of who will obey or to the command itself, not necessarily direct causation.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is one of the two interpretations Baqillani gives for 'except to be obeyed by Allah's permission'?
A) The verse means that prophets are only obeyed if Allah forces obedience.
B) The verse refers only to those whom Allah knows will obey.
C) The verse means that Allah's permission allows disobedience.
D) The verse abrogates the obligation to obey prophets.

Key Takeaway
Imam Baqillani offers two valid interpretations of 'by Allah's permission' in the verse, showing theological flexibility while preserving divine sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

How does Baqillani's first interpretation (permission as knowledge) challenge that excuse? Identify one command you have been neglecting and commit to acting on it today without waiting for ease.
?
Both interpretations in this passage place responsibility on you: either you are among those known to obey, or you are commanded to obey. Which of these two realities do you need to take more seriously right now? Write down one specific area where you have been failing to obey and state exactly what obedience looks like starting now.
?
If a prophet were sent to you today, would you obey him 'by Allah's permission'? That permission is either Allah's knowledge of your choice or His command to you. Which do you think is more decisive for your obedience? What change in your daily habits would show that you are taking Allah's command seriously, regardless of your feelings?

Interpreting the Verse of Creation for Worship
Baqillani answers an objection about the verse's scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's method of reconciling the general verse about creation for worship with the reality that many do not worship.

Core Idea
The verse refers only to those Allah knows will worship, not every individual.

A common question arises: if Allah created all jinn and humans to worship Him, why do so many disbelieve? Baqillani answers by showing that the verse is specific, not universal. He uses another Quranic verse to support his interpretation. Let's examine his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once to understand the flow: first the objector's question, then Baqillani's answer.
2
Identify Baqillani's key move
Notice how Baqillani specifies the verse: 'He intended some of the jinn and humans.' This is the core interpretive step.
The word 'some' is crucial.
3
Examine the supporting verse
Baqillani cites another verse about creating many for Hell. Ask yourself: how does this prove the first verse is not universal?
4
Understand the theological significance
This reconciliation affirms that divine knowledge and will encompass both the believers and the disbelievers. Reflect on why this is important in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة فإن قالوا: فما معنى قوله تعالى وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون؟. قيل لهم: أراد بعض الجن والإنس، وهم الذين علم أنهم يعبدونه. لأنه قال تعالى في آية أخرى: ﴿ ولقد ذرأنا لجهنم كثيراً من الجن والإنس ﴾ أي: إنه خلق لجهنم كثيراً من الجن والإنس.

It was said to them: He intended some of the jinn and humans, those whom He knew would worship Him. Because He said, exalted, in another verse: 'And We have created for Hell many of the jinn and humans' meaning: He created for Hell many of the jinn and humans.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage is an objection and answer about the verse in Surat Adh-Dhariyat (51:56). The objector questions how the general statement that all jinn and humans are created for worship can be true when many do not worship. Baqillani answers that the verse is not universal; it refers only to 'some' of the jinn and humans – those whom Allah knew would worship. He supports this by citing another verse (Al-A'raf 7:179) where Allah explicitly says He created many for Hell. Thus, the purpose of worship applies to the elect, while others are created for punishment. The lesson reconciles the two verses and affirms that divine knowledge and will are comprehensive.

D) He says the verse applies only to humans, not jinn.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani resolves the apparent contradiction by specifying that the purpose of worship applies only to those Allah knows will worship, not all beings.

The Three Aspects of Divine Guidance
Baqillani enumerates three aspects of divine guidance for believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three distinct aspects of Allah's guidance (hidayah) for believers as explained by Imam Baqillani.

Core Idea
Divine guidance is threefold: creating faith, supporting it, and leading to Paradise.

Imam Baqillani addresses a question about the meaning of divine guidance for believers. He explains that guidance is not a single event but encompasses multiple divine acts. This passage clarifies the comprehensive nature of Allah's guidance, showing that it includes the initial creation of faith, ongoing support, and final reward.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: a question followed by a three-part answer.
Pay attention to the word ' وقد ' which signals the additional aspects.
2
Identify the three aspects
Locate the three ways Allah guides believers: (1) creating guidance and illuminating hearts, (2) expanding chests and granting tawfiq, (3) guiding to Paradise. Understand each aspect's wording.
The second aspect lists several actions: sharh al-sadr, tawfiq, i'aanah, tashil.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters. It shows that guidance is continuous, involves both initial faith and ongoing support, and extends to the Hereafter. This counters the view that guidance is only the initial call.
This connects to broader discussions of divine will and human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : وما معنى هدايته للمؤمنين؟ . قيل له : قد يهديهم بأن يخلق هداهم ويُنوّر بالإيمان قلوبهم . وقد أيضاً بأن يشرح صدورهم ويتولّى توفيقهم له وإعانتهم عليه وتسهيله لهم السبيل إليه كل ذلك هداية منه لهم. وقد يهديهم أيضاً في الآخرة إلى الثواب وطريق الجنة وذلك هدى لهم من فعله
So if he says: What is the meaning of His guidance for the believers? It is said to him: He guides them by creating their guidance and illuminating their hearts with faith. And also by expanding their chests and undertaking their tawfiq (success) for it and assisting them upon it and facilitating for them the path to it – all of that is guidance from Him for them. And He also guides them in the Hereafter to reward and the path of Paradise, and that is guidance for them from His action.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage answers the question about the meaning of hidayah for believers. The answer distinguishes three levels: (1) creating guidance in the heart, i.e., creating faith; (2) facilitating and supporting them in following the faith through expanding the chest (sharh al-sadr), granting tawfiq (divine success), assisting, and making the path easy; and (3) guiding them to Paradise in the afterlife. All of these are acts of guidance from Allah, showing that hidayah is a comprehensive divine act that includes both initial creation of faith and ongoing support, as well as final reward.

Key Terms
هدى
خلق الهدى
توفيق
شرح الصدر
إرشاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Guidance is only the initial call or invitation to faith.
Correction: Guidance includes the creation of faith, continuous support, and final entry into Paradise, as shown in this passage.

Checkpoint

A) Two: creating faith and leading to Paradise.
B) Three: creating faith, facilitating, and leading to Paradise.
C) Four: calling, creating faith, expanding chest, and rewarding.
D) One: only creating guidance.

Key Takeaway
Allah's guidance for believers is a multi-faceted divine act that creates faith, sustains it through support, and ultimately leads to Paradise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Refuting an Objection from Quran 6:111
Baqillani answers an objection based on Quran 6:111 about unbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends free will against a deterministic reading of Quran 6:111 by highlighting the exception clause and the verse's limited scope.

Core Idea
Quran 6:111 does not prove determinism; it only negates belief at those specific signs.

This passage presents a theological objection and Baqillani's crisp response. The objector cites a Quranic verse that seems to suggest nothing can cause faith. Baqillani dismantles this argument by pointing to two overlooked details in the verse itself. Understanding this refutation clarifies how kalam balances divine power with human accountability.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the verse
Begin by reading the objector's citation of Quran 6:111. Notice how it appears to support a fatalistic view: even extraordinary signs would not lead to belief.
The verse mentions three signs: angels, dead speaking, and all things gathered.
2
Identify Baqillani's first response: the exception
Find where Baqillani points to the exception phrase 'unless God wills'. Understand that this shows faith remains subject to divine will, not a lack of capacity in signs.
The exception changes the meaning entirely.
3
Identify the second response: scope limitation
Notice Baqillani's argument that the verse only negates belief at those specific signs, not all possible signs. This leaves room for other means that could bring about faith.
4
Synthesize the refutation
Combine both points: the exception shows God's will is the decisive factor, and the limited scope leaves other possibilities open. Conclude that the objection fails.
This two-part response is a classic kalam method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : أفليس قد قال الله تعالى: ﴿ ولو أننا نزلنا إليهم الملائكة وكلمهم الموتى وحشرنا عليهم كل شيء قبلا ما كانوا ليؤمنوا ﴾؟ . قيل له : قد استثنى في آخر الآية بقوله : إلا أن يشاء الله فبطل ما قلتم. وعلى أنه أخبر أنهم لا يؤمنون أبداً عند هذه الآيات، إنزال الملائكة وتكلم الموتى وحشر كل شيء قبلا، ولم يقل التي هي ليس في المقدور فعل شيء يؤمنون عنده . فقد يمكن أن يكون في المعلوم أنه لو فعل بهم غير هذه الآيات لآمنوا . فبطل ما قالوه .
If someone says: Did God not say, 'And even if We sent down to them the angels and the dead spoke to them and We gathered against them every thing facing them, they would not have believed'? It is said to him: He made an exception at the end of the verse by His saying 'unless God wills', so what you said is invalid. And also He informed that they would never believe at these signs—the sending down of angels, the speaking of the dead, and the gathering of every thing facing them—and He did not say that there is no act in capability that they would believe at. For it could be known that if He had done other than these signs with them, they would have believed. So what they said is invalid.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair. The objector quotes Quran 6:111, which states that even if angels came down and the dead spoke etc., the disbelievers would not believe, arguing that nothing can cause faith. Baqillani's response has two parts: First, God made an exception with 'unless God wills', meaning faith is ultimately by God's will. Second, the verse only says they would not believe at those specific signs; it does not say they cannot believe at any other sign. Thus, the objection fails.

Key Terms
استثناء
مقدور
آيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Quran 6:111 proves determinism — that no signs can ever cause belief.
Correction: Baqillani shows the verse includes an exception ('unless God wills') and only negates belief at those specific signs, not all possible signs.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the flaw in the objection based on Quran 6:111?
A) The verse is abrogated
B) The verse only excludes belief at those specific signs, not all signs
C) The verse was revealed for a different community
D) The objector misquoted the verse

Key Takeaway
Quran 6:111 does not prove that faith is impossible; it only negates belief at those specific signs, and the exception 'unless God wills' preserves divine power over faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Consider a time you felt that certain people could never be guided. How does Baqillani's emphasis on the specificity of signs challenge your assumptions? Are you too quick to judge others' capacity for faith? What practical step can you take to trust in God's ability to guide?
?
The verse's exception 'unless God wills' is often overlooked. In your own life, do you truly live with the conviction that God's will is over all things, even your own choices? What area of your life do you need to surrender more fully to that reality?

The Source of Security: Revelation and Consensus
Baqillani explains that revelation and consensus prevent God from punishing believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Islamic scholars rely on revelation and consensus, rather than reason alone, to guarantee that God will not punish believers.

Core Idea
Revelation and consensus, not reason, assure us of God's justice.

In kalam, one of the most challenging questions is: if God is absolutely powerful and just, what prevents Him from acting contrary to His promises? An objector might doubt the reliability of God's threat and promise. In this passage, Baqillani responds by grounding our certainty in two revealed sources: the prophetic teaching and the consensus of the Muslim community.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. The objector asks: 'What gives you security from God punishing the believers?' Notice the challenge: reason alone does not forbid it.
The objector is assuming that reason permits both possibilities.
2
Identify the two sources of security
Baqillani gives two sources: 'tawqif al-nabi' (prophetic instruction) and 'ijma' al-muslimin' (consensus of Muslims). Find these in the Arabic text.
These are transmitted, not rational, sources.
3
Understand the role of necessary knowledge
Baqillani mentions that God's reports give necessary knowledge (darura) that the events will not occur. Reflect on how revelation creates certainty.
This shows the epistemological foundation of the answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : فما الذي يؤمنكم من تعذيبه المؤمنين وتنعيمه الكافرين. قيل له: يؤمننا من ذلك توقيف النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم، وإجماع المسلمين على أنه لا يفعل ذلك. وعلى أنه قد أخبر أخباراً علموا قصده به ضرورة إلى أن ذلك لا يكون . ولولا هذا التوقيف والخبر، لأجزنا ما سألت عنه .
If he says: What gives you security from His punishing the believers and blessing the disbelievers? It is said to him: What gives us security from that is the instruction of the Prophet—may God bless him and his family and grant him peace—and the consensus of the Muslims that He does not do that. And that He has told reports by which they know His intent necessarily that this will not happen. And were it not for this instruction and report, we would have permitted what you asked about.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer pair. The objector asks: If reason does not preclude God from punishing believers and rewarding disbelievers, then what prevents Him from actually doing so? Baqillani answers that the security (يؤمننا) comes from two sources: first, the prophetic instruction (توقيف النبي) — i.e., revelations and prophetic statements that inform us of God's promise and threat; second, the consensus of the Muslim community (إجماع المسلمين) that God will not do that. Moreover, God has given reports (أخبار) from which the Prophet's community knows with certainty (ضرورة) that this will not happen. Baqillani emphasizes that without these revealed sources, reason alone would not forbid it.

Key Terms
يؤمننا
توقيف
إجماع
أخبار
ضرورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That reason alone can determine God's future actions without revelation.
Correction: Baqillani shows that reason alone does not forbid God from punishing believers; we rely on revelation and consensus.

Checkpoint
What gives Muslims security that God will not punish believers?
A) Rational proof
B) Prophetic instruction and Muslim consensus
C) The fact that believers are good
D) God's inability to do so

Key Takeaway
Without revelation and consensus, reason alone cannot guarantee that God will not punish believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
When you sin, do you quickly rationalize that 'God is forgiving' without consulting what He has actually revealed about repentance? What would it look like for you to take the revealed warnings and promises as seriously as this passage demands?

Mu'tazilite Divine Promise and Threat
States the Mu'tazilite doctrine on obligatory reward and necessary punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite doctrine that reward is obligatory upon Allah and punishment is necessary for unrepentant grave sinners, and how this differs from the majority view.

Core Idea
For the Mu'tazila, Allah's justice makes reward and punishment binding obligations.

This passage presents a central Mu'tazilite tenet: that divine promise and threat are not merely contingent but carry a binding necessity based on Allah's justice. Before examining the proof, we must grasp their precise claim: reward is a binding obligation (ḥatm) on Allah, and punishment is necessary (wājib) for the unrepentant grave sinner. The author then contrasts this with the majority's view that punishment can be waived.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong language: 'ḥatm' and 'wājib'.
2
Identify the Mu'tazilite claim
Find where the passage states that reward is obligatory upon God and punishment is necessary for the unrepentant grave sinner.
3
Contrast with the majority
The passage says punishment is not obligatory according to the majority. Note the reasoning: reward cannot be nullified, punishment can be waived.
This is a key difference between Mu'tazila and Ash'aris.
4
Understand 'determined one being liable'
The passage explains that even if punishment can be waived, the liability itself makes eternal punishment appropriate when it occurs. Reflect on this nuance.
This concept upholds divine justice even with potential forgiveness.
5
Reflect on significance
Consider why this doctrine matters for understanding God's justice and the role of human actions in determining divine response.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما وعد الله تعالى من الثواب أو توعد به من العقاب، فقوله الحق ووعده الصدق وذهبت المعتزلة إلى أن الثواب حتم على الله تعالى والعقاب واجب على مقترف الكبيرة إذا لم يتب عنها. ولا يجب العقاب عند الأكثرين وجوب الثواب، لأن الثواب لا يجوز حبطه والعقاب يجوز إسقاطه عند البصريين وطوائف من البغداديين ولكن المعين بكونه مستحقاً يحسن لوقوعه مستحقاً، ولو لم يكن كذلك لما حسن العقاب على التأبيد، فهذا حقيقة أصلهم.
And whatever God Almighty promised of reward or threatened of punishment, His word is truth and His promise is true. The Mu'tazila held that reward is obligatory (ḥatm) upon God Almighty and punishment is necessary (wājib) upon the committer of a grave sin if he does not repent of it. Punishment is not obligatory according to the majority as reward is obligatory, because reward cannot be nullified and punishment can be waived according to the Basrans and groups of the Baghdadis, but the determined one being liable is good because it occurs as a liability, and if it were not so, then eternal punishment would not be good. This is the reality of their doctrine.
Source pages p. 402

Commentary
This passage presents the Mu'tazilite position on divine promise (wa'd) and threat (wa'id). It begins by affirming that God's statements about reward and punishment are true. Then it specifies the Mu'tazilite view: reward is a binding obligation (ḥatm) on God, and punishment is necessary (wājib) for the grave sinner who does not repent. The passage contrasts this with the majority view that punishment is not obligatory in the same sense as reward, because reward cannot be annulled whereas punishment can be forgiven according to the Basran Mu'tazila and some Baghdadis. However, even with the possibility of forgiveness, the liability itself (al-mu'ayyan bi-kawnihi mustahiqqan) is such that the punishment is appropriate when it occurs. If it were not appropriate, eternal punishment would not be suitable. This, it says, is the essence of their doctrine.

Key Terms
الوعد
الوعيد
الثواب
العقاب
حتم
واجب
الكبيرة
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Mu'tazilites denied God's freedom in rewarding; they actually affirmed obligation based on His justice.
Correction: The Mu'tazila did not deny divine freedom; rather they held that God's justice necessitates that He fulfill His promises and threats. This is not a constraint on God but a consequence of His perfection.

Checkpoint
According to the Mu'tazilite position stated in this passage, what is the status of punishment for the grave sinner who does not repent?
A) It is optional for God to apply it.
B) It is necessary (wājib) and will be applied.
C) It can be waived by any intercession.
D) It is not possible because of God's mercy.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila held that reward is an obligation upon Allah and punishment is a necessary consequence for unrepentant grave sinners, based on His justice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that Allah is obligated to reward you for your good deeds, would your worship become more about earning rather than loving? How does the Mu'tazilite view challenge you to reflect on the purity of your intentions?
?
The Mu'tazila held that punishment for unrepentant grave sin is necessary. Do you treat God's mercy as a license for sin, or do you feel the weight of His justice? Where do you stand between presumption and despair?
?
When you consider the greatness of Allah, do you feel entitled to His reward or humbled by His mercy? Does this passage expose any arrogance or fear in your heart?

Ash'ari Refutation via Master-Servant Analogy
Ash'ari argument that the servant does not deserve reward from God

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the master-servant analogy demonstrates that reward from God is not obligatory but a matter of divine grace.

Core Idea
The servant does not deserve reward; worship is gratitude, not a transaction.

This passage presents a key Ash'ari argument against the Mu'tazilite view that God must reward believers. Using everyday analogies from master-slave and father-son relationships, al-Baqillani shows that even in human contexts, service does not obligate extra reward when the master already provides everything. Read on to see how this reasoning applies to God and His servants, ultimately concluding that reward is by grace, not requirement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's analogies unfold naturally.
The passage uses two analogies: master-slave and father-son.
2
Identify the two analogies
Notice the first analogy: a master who provides for his slave's needs does not owe extra reward for the slave's service. The second: a father who supports his son does not owe extra for the son's respect. Both show that no additional compensation is due when basic needs are already met.
The analogies are designed to be intuitive and universally understood.
3
Apply the analogy to God and humans
Extend the reasoning: God's blessings are infinite and continuous, while human worship is minimal and itself a form of gratitude. Gratitude cannot logically demand compensation, as that would lead to infinite regress.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that reward (thawāb) is not an obligation due to human merit but a gift of divine grace (faḍl). Worship is a response to blessings, not a transaction that binds God.
This refutes the Mu'tazilite doctrine of 'obligatory reward'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فنحن نلزمهم على موجب أصلهم أمثلة لا قبل لهم بها منها أن السيد إذا كان يقوم بمؤن عبده وإزاحة علله والعبد يخدمه غير مستفرغ جهده، بل كان مودعاً معظم أفعاله فلا يستحق العبد على سيده شيئاً على مقابل الخدمة المستحقة عليه. وكذلك المعظم في عشيرته، إذا كان يكرم ولده ويقيم أوده، والولد يكرمه، ويرعاه ويطلب مرضاته ويتوخاه، فلا يستوجب بإزاء خدمته مزيداً على ما يناله من الإحسان الدار عليه .. فإذا كان هذا سبيل من يخدم مثله، فالعبد الذي لو قوبلت عبادته بنعماء الله تعالى عليه في لحظة لأبرت نعماء الله تعالى وأربت على جميع قرباته والرب تعالى يستحق لأن يعبد، والنعم منه على العباد تتري، ولو حاول العبد عدها لم يحصها. فكيف يستوجب العبد بالنزر اليسير من أعماله ، وهو الغريق في أنعم الله تعالى مزيد ثواب لولا فضله العظيم. ثم عبادة العبد شكر للنعم، وليس من حكم العقل في مستقر العوائد استيجاب عوض على بذل واجب هو عوض. ولو استحق العبد لشكره عوضا لاستحق الرب تعالى على ما يوليه من الثواب عوضاً ولا محيص عن ذلك.
So we oblige them, according to the requirement of their doctrine, with examples they cannot handle. Among them is that if the master provides for his slave's maintenance and removes his problems, and the slave serves him without exerting his full effort, rather most of his actions are entrusted, then the slave does not deserve anything from his master in return for the service due from him. Likewise, the revered one among his clan: if he honors his son and supports his needs, and the son honors him, cares for him, seeks his pleasure and is considerate, then he does not deserve for his service an increase beyond what he receives of the continuous kindness. So if this is the way of one who serves like him, then consider the slave whose worship, if weighed against the blessings of God Almighty upon him in a moment, would make God's blessings abundant and surpass all his acts of devotion. And the Lord Almighty deserves to be worshipped, and blessings from Him upon the servants come successively; if the servant tried to count them he could not. So how can the servant deserve, with the paltry amount of his deeds while he is drowning in God's blessings, an increase of reward without His great grace? Then the slave's worship is gratitude for blessings, and it is not a rational judgment in established customs to deserve compensation for performing an obligation that is itself a compensation. And if the servant deserved a compensation for his gratitude, then the Lord Almighty would deserve a compensation for what He bestows of reward, and there is no escape from that.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazilite doctrine of obligatory reward using analogical reasoning. The author (al-Baqillani) presents examples from human relationships to demonstrate that even in worldly contexts, a servant or child does not deserve extra reward beyond the ongoing care they already receive. The argument proceeds in three steps. First, a master who fully provides for his slave's needs does not owe the slave anything extra for the slave's service, especially if the slave is not even exerting full effort. Second, similarly, a father who constantly provides for his son does not owe the son extra compensation for the son's respectful service, because the son is already benefiting from the father's bounty. Third, applying this to the relationship between God and His servants, the disparity is infinitely greater: God's blessings are overwhelming and continuous, while the servant's worship is minimal. Worship is essentially gratitude (shukr) for blessings, and it is not rationally required that gratitude itself be compensated; if it were, it would lead to an infinite regress where God would also deserve compensation for giving the initial reward. Thus, reward is not obligatory but a matter of divine grace (faḍl).

Key Terms
السيد
العبد
الخدمة
الشكر
الثواب
الفضل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That this analogy denies all human merit and effort.
Correction: The analogy does not deny that human effort has value or that God may reward it; it only denies that such effort obligates God to reward. Reward is freely given by grace, not earned as a right.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion of the master-servant analogy regarding the servant's reward?
A) The servant deserves a greater reward because of his service.
B) The servant does not deserve extra reward beyond the ongoing kindness.
C) The servant's service cancels the master's obligation.
D) The servant's gratitude is a form of payment.

Key Takeaway
Reward from God is not an obligation but a gift of divine grace, because worship is gratitude for blessings already received.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you pray or do good deeds, do you ever feel a subtle sense that God 'owes' you something in return? How does this passage challenge that feeling, and what would change in your worship if you truly believed all reward is pure grace?
?
Think of a specific blessing you received today—did you thank God for it? And did you, even unconsciously, feel that your prayer or kindness somehow 'repays' that blessing? How does al-Baqillani's argument about gratitude not being compensable expose the flaw in that thinking?
?
If reward is not deserved, does that make your worship feel meaningless? Or does it free you from a transactional mindset? Which is more difficult for you to accept, and what do you need to change in your heart to embrace this truth with gratitude and humility?

Baqillani Refutes an Interpretation of the Reward Verse
Baqillani refutes an interpretation limiting the reward verse to those without major sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes a specific interpretation of the reward verse (27:89) by showing that its threat applies only to disbelievers, not to believing sinners.

Core Idea
Baqillani restricts the verse's threat to disbelievers to avoid contradicting other verses.

This passage addresses a common hermeneutical challenge: how to reconcile verses that promise reward for good deeds with verses that threaten punishment for sins. Baqillani refutes an interpretation that would limit the reward verse only to those without major sin, arguing instead that the threat applies exclusively to disbelievers. By doing so, he preserves the consistency of the Quranic text and the hope for believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the dialogue structure: premise, objection, refutation.
2
Identify the premise and objection
Locate the initial premise about no contradiction, then the objector's claim that the reward verse is conditional on not committing major sins.
The objector uses the phrase 'إذا لم يقتل نفساً مؤمنة...'.
3
Analyze the refutation
Examine how Baqillani responds by asserting that the threat applies to those with no faith or good deeds—the disbelievers.
The refutation pivots from conditional to absolute kufr.
4
Reflect on the implication
Consider that this interpretation preserves the verse's consistency and offers hope for believers who sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم يُرَدْ بالخلود في جهنّم، وأن يُرتب ذلك ترتيباً لا يجوز معه نقض بعض الآيات بعضاً. فإن قال: إنما أراد بقوله: من جاء بالحسنة فله خير منها كذا إذا لم يقتل نفساً مؤمنة ولم يعص ولم يتعدَّ حدوده. قيل له: لا، بل أراد بالوعيد على قتل النفس المؤمنة وتعدي حدوده وفعل معصيته من لم يكن منه إيمان ولا حسنة، وهم الكفار وهذا أولى.
Eternal punishment in Hell was not intended, and that this was arranged in a way that does not allow contradicting some verses with others. If he says: 'He only meant by His statement: "Whoever comes with a good deed will have better than it" thus if he did not kill a believing soul and did not disobey and did not transgress His limits.' We say to him: No, rather He intended by the threat upon killing the believing soul, transgressing His limits, and committing disobedience, one who had no faith and no good deed, and they are the disbelievers, and this is more appropriate.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit. The author first states a premise: the intended meaning of certain Quranic verses is not eternal punishment for grave sinners; rather, the verses are arranged so that no contradiction arises. Then an objector claims that the verse "Whoever comes with a good deed will have better than it" (Quran 27:89) is conditional on the person not having committed murder, disobedience, or transgression. The author refutes this by saying the verse's threat (of punishment) is actually directed at those who have no faith and no good deeds—i.e., disbelievers—not at believers who commit sins. The refutation reasserts that the threat applies to disbelievers, preserving the consistency of the Quranic text.

Correction: Baqillani explains the threat is only for disbelievers, not for believers who sin.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani restricts the threat of punishment in the reward verse to disbelievers, preserving the hope for believing sinners.

Specification Undermines Literal Reading of Threat Verses
Baqillani concludes the apparent meaning cannot be clung to due to possibility of specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes clinging to the apparent meaning of punishment verses by showing the possibility of specification and the balancing counter-evidence.

Core Idea
Apparent meaning is not final when specification is possible.

Baqillani wraps up his argument that the apparent meanings of threat verses cannot be taken at face value because they could be specific to certain individuals or contexts. He then tackles a direct objection from Quranic verses about the wicked, showing that even these may be limited and are countered by verses about the righteous, which highlight the primacy of tawhid and faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice how the argument flows from a conclusion to an objection and a response.
The passage is dense but structured as a logical exchange.
2
Identify the Argument Structure
Find the conclusion, the objection, the response, and the counter-argument. Notice how Baqillani uses the possibility of specification (ihtimal) to defend his position.
The objection is from the verse 'Indeed the wicked are in Hellfire'.
3
Reflect on the Methodological Principle
Ask yourself: Why does the mere possibility of specification invalidate clinging to the apparent meaning? How does the counter-verse about the righteous strengthen the argument?
This connects to the broader principle that Quranic verses may be qualified by other verses or contexts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، فقد بطل التعلق بظاهر هذه الآي مع جواز احتمالها. وكذلك الجواب إن تعلقوا بقوله تعالى: وإن الفجار لفي جحيم وبما جرى مجراه. قيل لهم: يحتمل أن يكون أراد بعض الفجار دون سائرهم. وعورضوا بقوله: إن الأبرار لفي نعيم وأعظم البر التوحيد والإيمان الذي لا يحصل الإنسان بارّاً مطيعاً إلا بوجوده.
And when it is so, then clinging to the apparent meaning of these verses has become invalid, due to the possibility of their specification. And similarly the answer if they cling to His statement Almighty: 'And indeed the wicked are in Hellfire' and what runs in its course. We say to them: It is possible that He intended some of the wicked, not all of them. And they are countered by His statement: 'Indeed the righteous are in bliss,' and the greatest righteousness is Tawhid and faith, by which a person does not become a righteous obedient one except through its existence.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage presents a conclusion and a final objection-answer. First, Baqillani concludes that because 'man' can be specific, clinging to the apparent meaning (zāhir) of threat-verses is invalid when there is a possibility of specification. Then he addresses an objection based on the verse 'Indeed the wicked are in Hellfire' (Quran 82:14). The response is that this verse may also refer to some wicked people, not all. Moreover, they are countered by the verse 'Indeed the righteous are in bliss' (Quran 82:13), noting that the greatest righteousness is tawhid and faith, without which no one can be truly righteous and obedient. Thus, the verses about wickedness are balanced by those about righteousness, preventing a universal condemnation of grave sinners.

Key Terms
ظاهر
الآي
احتمال
الفجار
الأبرار
التوحيد

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse 'Indeed the wicked are in Hellfire' applies to all sinners without exception.
Correction: Baqillani shows the verse may be specific to some wicked people, not all, and is counterbalanced by the verse about the righteous, which indicates that faith is the key to salvation.

Checkpoint

D) He says it is metaphorical

Key Takeaway
Apparent meanings of threat verses are not definitive due to the possibility of specification and the presence of counter-evidence from other verses.

?

?
Baqillani counters the threat verse with the righteous verse, noting that true righteousness is based on tawhid and faith. Are you relying on your own actions to be counted among the righteous, or do you have the faith that makes you righteous? Examine your heart: if you were to die today, would you have the certainty of that faith?
?
The greatest righteousness is tawhid and faith, without which no one can be righteous. This means your salvation hinges on faith, not just actions. Have you ever taken your faith for granted? How can you actively strengthen your tawhid so that you are truly among the righteous described in the verse?

Legal Punishments Are Trials, Not Punishment
Baqillani responds to the objection that legal punishments prove the sinner deserves punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that legal punishments (ḥudūd) are trials (imtiḥān) and not punishments (ʿiqāb), and how this relates to the sinner's ultimate reward.

Core Idea
Legal punishments in this world are trials, not final judgments.

This passage addresses a common objection: if a sinful believer still deserves reward for his faith, why does he face legal punishments in this world? Baqillani provides a clear response: these punishments are not punishment in the Hereafter sense but are trials for purification. He supports this with parallel examples from Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
The objectors claim that if the sinner deserved reward, he would not be cursed or punished in this world. Baqillani replies that these legal punishments are actually trials (imtiḥān), not punishments (ʿiqāb).
Notice the key distinction between worldly measures and afterlife reward.
2
Examine the parallel argument
Baqillani argues that the sinner still enjoys worldly benefits like marriage, inheritance, and burial in Muslim cemeteries. These are not considered reward (thawāb) in the afterlife sense, so why would legal punishments be considered punishment?
This shows consistency in treating worldly acts differently from eschatological reward.
3
Consider the objection and counter-objection
The objectors retort that those benefits are not reward. Baqillani counters that legal punishments are also not punishment because they apply even to the repentant saint (al-tā'ib al-walī).
The application of ḥudūd to the repentant shows they are not punitive in the ultimate sense.
4
Reflect on the final analogy
Baqillani adds that blame and hatred from the community are not punishment either, using the example of truthful witnesses whose testimony is rejected due to procedural defects.
This reinforces that worldly judgments are not eschatological punishments.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: لو كان مستحقاً للثواب، لم يُلْعَن ولم يُهَن في الدنيا ولزالت عنه الحدود.
قيل لهم : هذه الحدود ليست بعقاب، وإنما هي امتحان .
ثم يقال لهم : ولو لم يستحق الفاسق بطاعته الثواب، لم يستحق المناكحة والموارثة والدفن في مقابر المسلمين .
فإن قالوا : هذه الأمور ليست بثواب .
قيل لهم : والحدود ليست بعقاب لأنها جارية على التائب الولي . وكذلك ذمنا وبغضنا ليس بعقاب، لأنه جارٍ على شهود الزني إذا اختلفت شهادتهم ونقص عددهم، وإن كانوا صادقين أبراراً عند الله عزّ وجلّ . ولا فصل في شيء من ذلك .
For they said: If he were deserving of reward, he would not be cursed nor humiliated in this world, and legal punishments would be removed from him. It is said to them: These legal punishments are not punishment; rather, they are trial. Then it is said to them: And if the sinner did not deserve reward for his obedience, he would not deserve marriage, inheritance, and burial in Muslim cemeteries. If they say: These matters are not reward. It is said to them: And legal punishments are not punishment because they are applied to the repentant saint (al-tā'ib al-walī). Likewise, our blame and hatred are not punishment, because they apply to witnesses of adultery when their testimonies differ and their number decreases, even if they were truthful righteous people in the sight of God Almighty. And there is no distinction in any of that.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The objectors argue that if a sinful believer still deserves reward for his faith and obedience, then legal punishments (ḥudūd) should not be applied to him in this world—since they would indicate he is being punished. Baqillani responds that these punishments are not punishment (ʿiqāb) in the Hereafter sense; rather, they are trials (imtiḥān) intended for purification. He then uses a parallel argument: the sinner still enjoys worldly benefits such as marriage, inheritance, and burial in Muslim cemeteries, which are not considered reward (thawāb). When the objectors object that these are not reward, Baqillani counters that legal punishments are similarly not punishment because they are applied even to the repentant saint (al-tā'ib al-walī). He gives another example: blame and hatred are not punishment because they apply to witnesses whose testimony is rejected due to procedural defects, even if they are truthful and righteous. Thus, there is no valid distinction—worldly legal measures do not reflect the ultimate reward or punishment in the afterlife.

Correction: Baqillani clarifies they are trials (imtiḥān) and do not negate ultimate reward; they are applied even to the repentant saint.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Legal punishments in this world are trials (imtiḥān) and do not indicate that the sinner deserves punishment in the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face difficulty or punishment in this world for your mistakes, do you interpret it as a sign that God is displeased with you? How would your attitude change if you truly believed that worldly punishments are trials and not indicators of your ultimate standing with Him? Reflect on a specific situation where you can apply this distinction starting today.
?
If you were a repentant saint undergoing a legal punishment for a sin, would your trust in God's mercy and justice be shaken? How does Baqillani's argument that such punishments are not punishment but trials affect your view of God's justice? What would you tell yourself in that moment to hold firm?

The Doctrine of Intercession and Refutation of the Mu'tazila
Baqillani establishes intercession for major sinners and answers the Mu'tazilite objection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni doctrine of intercession for major sinners and how Baqillani refutes the Mu'tazilite objection using textual evidence and logical reasoning.

Core Idea
Intercession benefits major sinners; the Mu'tazila limit it to increasing reward.

In this passage from the Tamhid, Baqillani turns to the topic of intercession, a key point of contention between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila. He first establishes the consensus on the principle and its application to major sinners, then addresses the Mu'tazilite claim that intercession only increases reward, not removes punishment. The refutation hinges on interpreting a Quranic verse as specific to a particular group and time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the English translation to get the overall argument.
Notice the structure: consensus, proof, objection, answer.
2
Identify the two opposing views
Baqillani presents the Sunni view (intercession for major sinners) and the Mu'tazilite view (only for increasing reward). List the differences.
3
Examine the proof for the Sunni view
Note the hadith 'My intercession is for the major sinners of my community' and the verse that equates seeking forgiveness with intercession. How do they support the doctrine?
The verse is used to show that the Prophet's intercession covers believers' sins.
4
Understand the Mu'tazilite objection
The Mu'tazila cite a verse denying intercession on a specific day. Why do they think this contradicts the Sunni view?
They interpret the verse as general and absolute.
5
Grasp Baqillani's refutation
Baqillani argues that the pronoun in the verse refers to specific individuals (disbelievers) and a specific time, so it does not negate intercession for others at other times. How does this reasoning preserve the Sunni doctrine?
This is a key logical move: restricting the scope of a general-sounding verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في الشفاعة
ومما يدل على جواز الغفران لعصاة أهل الملة ما ورد من الأخبار
اعلم أن الأمة أجمعت على أصل الشفاعة، وهي عندنا لأهل الكبائر من الأمة لقوله عليه السلام: «شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي» وبقوله تعالى: واستغفر لذنبك وللمؤمنين والمؤمنات أي ولذنب المؤمنين لدلالة القرينة؛ وطلب المغفرة شفاعة. وقالت المعتزلة: إنما هي لزيادة الثواب لا لدرء العقاب، لقوله تعالى: ﴿ واتقوا يوماً لا تجزي نفس عن نفس شيئا ولا يقبل منها عدل ولا تنفعها شفاعة ﴾، وهو عام في شفاعة النبي وغيره. الجواب: إنه لا عموم في الأعيان؛ لأن الضمير لقوم معينين فلا يلزم أن لا تنفع الشفاعة غيرهم. ولا في الأزمان لأنه لوقت مخصوص فلا يلزم عدم نفعها في غير ذلك الوقت.
Chapter on Intercession. And among what indicates the permissibility of forgiveness for the sinners of the religious community is what has been reported from the reports. Know that the community (al-ummah) has agreed upon the principle of intercession, and it is, in our view, for the major sinners of the community according to his statement, peace be upon him: 'My intercession is for the major sinners of my community' and by His statement, Exalted is He: 'And ask forgiveness for your sin and for the believing men and believing women' — meaning the sin of the believers due to contextual evidence; and seeking forgiveness is intercession. The Mu'tazila said: It is only for increase of reward, not for warding off punishment, according to His statement, Exalted is He: 'And fear a Day when no soul will avail another at all, nor will compensation be accepted from it, nor will intercession benefit it,' and it is general regarding the intercession of the Prophet and others. The answer: There is no generality in individuals, because the pronoun refers to specific people, so it does not necessitate that intercession does not benefit others. Nor in times, because it is for a specific time, so it does not necessitate the absence of its benefit at other times.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This is a definition-and-proof passage followed by an objection-and-answer. Baqillani begins a new chapter on intercession (shafāʿa). He states that the Ummah has consensus on the principle of intercession, and that it applies specifically to the major sinners (ahl al-kabā'ir) based on a hadith and a Quranic verse (asking forgiveness for the believers). Seeking forgiveness is equated with intercession. He then presents the Mu'tazilite objection: intercession is only for increasing reward (thawāb), not for removing punishment (ʿiqāb), citing the verse warning of a Day when no intercession will benefit. Baqillani answers by arguing that the verse is not general in its application: the pronoun refers to specific individuals (disbelievers) and a specific time, so it does not negate intercession for others at other times. This refutation preserves the doctrine of intercession for major sinners.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'no intercession will benefit it' proves that no intercession is possible on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: Baqillani argues the verse is specific to certain individuals (disbelievers) and a specific time, so it does not negate intercession for believing major sinners.

Checkpoint
What is the Mu'tazilite view on intercession according to Baqillani?
A) It is for major sinners only
B) It is only for increase of reward, not for warding off punishment
C) It is only for the Prophet himself
D) It is not established at all

Key Takeaway
Intercession for major sinners is established by consensus, hadith, and Quran, and the objection is refuted by showing the relevant verse is not general in its application.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a major sin, do you truly believe the Prophet's intercession can benefit you, or do you secretly doubt it because you feel unworthy? How does that doubt affect your repentance and hope in God's mercy?
?
The Mu'tazila feared that intercession for forgiveness would make people take sin lightly. Examine your own heart: does the promise of intercession make you more careless about sin, or does it drive you to deeper gratitude and obedience?
?
If you had been raised in the Mu'tazilite school, reading the verse 'no intercession will benefit it,' would you have had the humility to accept the hadith and the Sunni interpretation? Where in your life might intellectual pride be blocking you from submitting to revelation?

Hadith Evidence for Intercession and Denial by Khawarij and Qadariyya
Baqillani cites hadith evidence for intercession and notes sectarian denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni evidence for intercession from hadith and the denial of intercession by the Khawarij and Qadariyya.

Core Idea
Intercession is a proven Sunni doctrine supported by hadith, but rejected by deviant sects.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani presents additional textual evidence for the doctrine of intercession (shafa'a). He cites the statement of al-Baghdadi, the interpretation of the praiseworthy station as intercession, and two key hadiths: the Prophet's reserved intercession for major sinners and his choice of intercession over half his community entering Paradise. He also notes that the Khawarij and Qadariyya deny intercession for sinners, but truthfully they have no share in it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Get a feel for the flow of evidence.
2
Identify the sources of evidence
Notice that Baqillani uses a statement from al-Baghdadi, an exegetical interpretation, and two hadiths. List them.
This shows the multi-layered evidence for intercession.
3
Understand the doctrine of intercession according to Ahl al-Sunnah
The passage affirms intercession for prophets and believers for each other. Note that intercession is not limited to the Prophet.
4
Reflect on the denial by Khawarij and Qadariyya
Baqillani mentions that these sects deny intercession for sinners, but notes that they are truthful in having no share of it. What does this imply about their position?
It implies that their denial excludes them from the benefit.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونقل البغدادي في الشفاعة إثبات أهل السنّة الشفاعة للأنبياء عليهم السلام والمؤمنين بعضهم في بعض على قدر منازلهم. وقال: وقال المفسرون في تفسير المقام المحمود أنه الشفاعة. وفي الحديث: ادّخرت شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي. وروي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خير أن يدخل نصف أمته الجنة وبين الشفاعة فاختار الشفاعة وأخبر يدخلون الجنة بلا حساب كل واحد منهم يشفع في سبعين ألفاً وسأله عكاشة بن يدعو الله أن يجعله منهم فدعا له. وأنكرت الخوارج والقدرية الشفاعة في أهل الذنوب وهم صادقون في أن لا حظ لهم منها.
And Al-Baghdadi reported in [the book] Al-Shafāʿa: The Ahl al-Sunnah affirm intercession for the prophets, peace be upon them, and for the believers for one another according to their ranks. And he said: The exegetes said in the interpretation of 'the praiseworthy station' (al-maqām al-maḥmūd) that it is intercession. And in the hadith: 'I have reserved my intercession for the major sinners of my community.' And it is related that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was given the choice between half of his community entering Paradise and intercession, and he chose intercession, and he informed that they will enter Paradise without account, each one of them will intercede for seventy thousand, and ʿUkāsha ibn asked [him] to pray that he be among them, so he prayed for him. And the Khawarij and Qadariyya denied intercession for the sinful, and they are truthful in that they have no share of it.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage provides additional evidence for intercession from transmitted reports and scholarly statements. Baqillani cites Al-Baghdadi's affirmation that Ahl al-Sunnah believe intercession applies to prophets and to believers for each other according to their ranks. He then mentions that the exegetes interpret the 'praiseworthy station' (al-maqām al-maḥmūd) as intercession. Two famous hadiths are quoted: the Prophet's reserved intercession for major sinners, and his choice between half the community entering Paradise and intercession—he chose intercession and informed that many will enter Paradise without account and intercede for others. The story of ʿUkāsha ibn Miḥṣan seeking to be among those is included. Finally, Baqillani notes that the Khawarij and Qadariyya deny intercession for sinners, but they are truthful in that they themselves have no share of it, implying their denial excludes them.

The Oath to Perform a Work Deserving Intercession
Baqillani answers a question about a man who swears to do an action that merits intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's resolution of the dilemma concerning an oath to perform an action that merits intercession, and how he distinguishes between deserving intercession and being among its people.

Core Idea
Intercession is a divine favor, not earned by any action.

A tricky question arises: if a man swears to perform an action that merits intercession, what should he do? Avoid sins (but then he doesn't need intercession) or commit sins (violating consensus)? Baqillani navigates this by clarifying that intercession is a gift, not a wage, and then prescribes specific beliefs and actions for those who swear to become among its recipients. Let's explore his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma
Read the initial question and the apparent paradox: if avoiding sins makes intercession unnecessary, and committing sins is forbidden, what can the swearer do?
This sets up the need for a nuanced answer.
2
Identify Baqillani's distinction
Notice that Baqillani splits the oath into two types: one to 'deserve' intercession (impossible) and one to become among its 'people' (possible).
The Arabic verb 'yastaḥiqqu' implies earning, which is false.
3
Examine the prescribed actions
For the second type, Baqillani lists specific beliefs and actions: uphold tawḥīd and prophethood, avoid innovation, dissociate from innovators, and curse deniers.
These are not 'meriting' intercession but making one eligible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسألونا في هذا الباب عن رجل حلف بطلاق امرأته وعتق مماليكه أو حلف بالله تعالى أن يعمل عملاً يستحق به الشفاعة. وقالوا لنا ما الذي يلزم هذا الحالف؟ فإن قلتم نأمره باجتناب المعاصي، فمن اجتنبها لا يحتاج إلى الشفاعة وإن قلتم نأمره بالمعاصي خالفتم الإجماع في هذا. وجوابنا عن هذا السؤال أن الحالف إن حلف على أن يعمل عملا يستحق به الشفاعة حانت في يمينه يمينه لأن من نال الشفاعة في الآخرة فإنما ينالها بفضل من الله تعالى بلا استحقاق وإن حلف أن يعمل عملاً يصير به من أهل الشفاعة أمرناه بأن يعتقد أصولنا في التوحيد والنبوات وأن يجتنب البدع الضالة وأن يتبرأ من أهل البدع على العموم وممن لا يرى الشفاعة على الخصوص وأن يلعن منكري الشفاعة من الخوارج والقدرية، فإنه إذا اعتقد ذلك بَرَّ عينه. وكان ممن يجوز الشفاعة ان كان له ذنب وجاز أن يكون هو شفيعاً لغيره جعلنا الله من أهلها برحمته.
And they asked us in this chapter about a man who swore by divorcing his wife and freeing his slaves or swore by God Almighty to do a work that would make him deserve intercession. And they said to us: What is incumbent upon this swearer? For if you say we command him to avoid sins, then whoever avoids them does not need intercession; and if you say we command him to commit sins, you would violate consensus on this. And our answer to this question: If the swearer swore to do a work that would make him deserve intercession, his oath is broken (ḥānat fī yamīnihi), because whoever attains intercession in the Hereafter only attains it by the favor of God Almighty without deserving. And if he swore to do a work through which he would become among the people of intercession, we command him to believe in our principles concerning tawḥīd and prophethoods, to avoid misguiding innovations, to dissociate from the people of innovation in general and from those who do not see intercession specifically, and to curse the deniers of intercession from the Khawarij and Qadariyya. For if he believes that, his oath is fulfilled (barra ʿaynahu). And he would be among those for whom intercession is permissible—if he had a sin, and it is possible that he himself could be an intercessor for others. May God make us among its people by His mercy.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This is an objection-and-answer passage. The questioners present a dilemma: if a man swears to do an action that merits intercession, does one command him to avoid sins (making intercession unnecessary) or command him to commit sins (violating consensus)? Baqillani answers by distinguishing two types of oaths. First, if the oath is to perform an action that would make him 'deserve' (yastaḥiqqu) intercession, the oath is automatically broken (ḥānat) because no one deserves intercession; it is purely a favor (faḍl) from God. Second, if the oath is to become among the 'people of intercession' (ahl al-shafāʿa), Baqillani commands the swearer to adopt orthodox beliefs: believe in tawḥīd and prophethoods, avoid innovations (bidʿa), dissociate from innovators and specifically from those who deny intercession, and curse the deniers from Khawarij and Qadariyya. If he does so, his oath is fulfilled (barra ʿaynahu), and he becomes eligible for intercession—both for himself (if he has sins) and as an intercessor for others.

Key Terms
يمين
حنث
بر
استحقاق
فضل
بدعة
تبرؤ
لعن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'meriting' intercession means performing good deeds to earn it.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that intercession is a divine favor (faḍl), not something earned (istihqāq).

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what should a person do if he swears to become among the people of intercession (ahl al-shafāʿa)?
A) Commit sins to need intercession
B) Avoid sins and perform good deeds
C) Believe in orthodox principles, avoid innovation, dissociate from innovators, and curse deniers of intercession
D) Ask the Prophet directly for intercession

Key Takeaway
Intercession is a favor from God, not earned; the proper way to become among its people is through correct belief and dissociation from error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as if you can earn God's favor through your own actions, or do you truly rely on His grace? Ask yourself: what is your real hope for intercession — your deeds or Allah's mercy?
?
Baqillani commands dissociating from those who deny intercession and even cursing them. Is there a group or person you tolerate in your heart whose views contradict this core belief? Are you willing to distinguish yourself from them, even at social cost?
?
If intercession is a favor not earned, then what are you doing today that reflects total dependence on Allah's bounty? List one habit that reveals you trust your own righteousness more than His grace, and commit to changing it this week.

Evidence for the Prophet's Intercession for Major Sinners
Baqillani lists hadith and scholarly consensus establishing intercession for major sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural evidence from hadith and scholarly consensus that establishes the Prophet's intercession for major sinners.

Core Idea
Intercession for major sinners is affirmed by multiple hadith and scholarly consensus.

Imam Baqillani now turns to the evidence for a key doctrine: the Prophet's intercession for those who commit major sins. He presents a series of hadith reports and scholarly testimonies that together make a strong case. As you read, notice how he combines direct prophetic statements, multiple chains of transmission, and the interpretive tradition.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith evidence
Start by reading the Prophet's own statement reserving intercession for major sinners. This is the core textual proof.
2
Identify the chain of narrators
Notice the list of companions who transmitted this hadith. This shows the report is widely attested.
The multiple narrators strengthen reliability.
3
Understand the response to objections
Baqillani addresses possible objections: that intercession might be for others or restricted to certain times. See how he refutes these.
4
Note the scholarly consensus and interpretation
He cites al-Baghdadi and the commentators on 'the Praised Station' to show that Ahl al-Sunnah affirm intercession for prophets and believers.
5
Reflect on the additional hadith
The final hadith about choosing intercession over half the nation entering Paradise highlights the great mercy and benefit of intercession.
This also shows the Prophet's preference for intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهم الثابتة المتظاهرة في إثبات شفاعة الرسول (صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم) في أهل الكبائر نحو قوله عليه السلام: ادخرت شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي. وقد روى خبر الشفاعة عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم عدة أنس بن مالك وجابر بن عبد الله. ورواه حذيفة عن أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه عن النبي صلى الله عليه. وروى معبد بن هلال وثابت البناني ذلك في خبر طويل عن أنس بن مالك. ورواه أيضاً أبو سعيد الخُدْري عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم. الشفاعة غيرهم. ولا في الأزمان لأنه لوقت مخصوص فلا يلزم عدم نفعها في غير ذلك الوقت. ونقل البغدادي في الشفاعة إثبات أهل السنّة الشفاعة للأنبياء عليهم السلام والمؤمنين بعضهم في بعض على قدر منازلهم. وقال: وقال المفسرون في تفسير المقام المحمود أنه الشفاعة. وفي الحديث: ادّخرت شفاعتي لأهل الكبائر من أمتي. وروي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم خير بين أن يدخل نصف أمته الجنة وبين الشفاعة فاختار الشفاعة وأخبر يدخلون الجنة بلا حساب كل واحد منهم يشفع في سبعين ألفاً وسأله عكاشة بن يدعو الله أن يجعله منهم فدعا له.
From them are the established and manifest [reports] regarding the affirmation of the intercession of the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family) for the people of major sins, such as his saying, peace be upon him: 'I have reserved my intercession for the people of major sins from my nation.' And several [companions] narrated the report of intercession from the Prophet, peace be upon him and his family: Anas ibn Malik and Jabir ibn Abd Allah. And Hudhayfah narrated it from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may God be pleased with him, from the Prophet, peace be upon him. And Ma'bad ibn Hilal and Thabit al-Bunani narrated that in a long report from Anas ibn Malik. And also Abu Sa'id al-Khudri narrated it from the Prophet, peace be upon him and his family. Intercession is for others. And it is not [restricted] to times because it is for a specific time, so it does not necessitate that its benefit is absent at other times. And al-Baghdadi transmitted regarding intercession the affirmation of Ahl al-Sunnah of intercession for the prophets, peace be upon them, and for the believers for each other according to their ranks. And he said: And the commentators said in the interpretation of the Praised Station (al-maqam al-mahmud) that it is intercession. And in the hadith: 'I have reserved my intercession for the people of major sins from my nation.' And it is narrated that the Prophet, peace be upon him, was given the choice between entering half of his nation into Paradise and intercession, and he chose intercession, and he informed that they would enter Paradise without reckoning, each one of them interceding for seventy thousand, and 'Ukashah asked him to supplicate God to make him among them, so he supplicated for him.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage presents the textual evidence for the doctrine of intercession (shafa'ah) for major sinners (ahl al-kaba'ir). Baqillani begins by stating that among the established and manifest reports is the Prophet's hadith 'I have reserved my intercession for the people of major sins from my nation.' He then lists the companions who narrated this report: Anas ibn Malik, Jabir ibn Abd Allah, Hudhayfah from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, Ma'bad ibn Hilal and Thabit al-Bunani in a long report from Anas, and Abu Sa'id al-Khudri. He then addresses a possible objection that intercession might be for others or restricted to certain times, clarifying that it is for a specific time on the Day of Resurrection, so its benefit is not negated at other times. He then cites al-Baghdadi's transmission that Ahl al-Sunnah affirm intercession for prophets and believers according to their ranks. He mentions that the commentators interpret 'the Praised Station' (al-maqam al-mahmud) as intercession. He repeats the hadith of reserved intercession and adds another report: the Prophet was given the choice between half of his nation entering Paradise without reckoning and intercession; he chose intercession, and each intercessor would intercede for seventy thousand. 'Ukashah asked to be among them, and the Prophet supplicated for him. This establishes the doctrine and its scriptural basis.

أهل الكبائر
المقام المحمود

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession is only for prophets or only at certain times, or that it benefits only minor sinners.
Correction: The passage clarifies that intercession is for major sinners from the Muslim nation, affirmed by multiple hadith and scholarly consensus, and it occurs on the Day of Resurrection.

Key Takeaway

Refuting the Denial of Intercession
Baqillani refutes denial of intercession with objection and answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes the Khawarij and Qadariyah denial of intercession through a dilemma and its resolution.

Core Idea
Intercession is by God's grace, not earned by deeds.

The Khawarij and Qadariyah denied intercession for sinners, posing a dilemma: if someone swears to do a deed that deserves intercession, what do you command? Baqillani's answer clarifies that intercession is not earned but granted by grace, and the correct path is to uphold correct beliefs and disavow those who deny intercession.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic and English translation. Notice the structure: the opponents' dilemma followed by Baqillani's twofold answer.
The passage uses a hypothetical oath scenario to frame the debate.
2
Identify the dilemma
Find the two options presented by the Khawarij and Qadariyah. Why do they think this creates a contradiction?
3
Understand Baqillani's first answer
Baqillani distinguishes between 'deserving' intercession and 'being among its people'. The first is impossible because intercession is by grace, so the oath is broken.
This avoids both horns of the dilemma.
4
Understand Baqillani's second answer
If the oath is about becoming among the people of intercession, the person must believe correctly and disavow deniers. This fulfills the oath and makes him eligible for intercession.
Note the emphasis on belief and disavowal, not sinning.
5
Reflect on the theological point
Intercession is by God's grace, not earned. This refutes the Kharijite and Qadarite denial and shows that intercession is possible without requiring sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأنكرت الخوارج والقدرية الشفاعة في أهل الذنوب وهم صادقون في أن لا حظ لهم منها. وسألونا في هذا الباب عن رجل حلف بطلاق امرأته وعتق مماليكه أو حلف بالله تعالى أن يعمل عملاً يستحق به الشفاعة. وقالوا لنا ما الذي يلزم هذا الحالف؟ فإن قلتم نأمره باجتناب المعاصي، فمن اجتنبها لا يحتاج إلى الشفاعة وإن قلتم نأمره بالمعاصي خالفتم الإجماع في هذا. وجوابنا عن هذا السؤال أن الحالف إن حلف على أن يعمل عملا يستحق به الشفاعة حانت في يمينه يمينه لأن من نال الشفاعة في الآخرة فإنما ينالها بفضل من الله تعالى بلا استحقاق وإن حلف أن يعمل عملاً يصير به من أهل الشفاعة أمرناه بأن يعتقد أصولنا في التوحيد والنبوات وأن يجتنب البدع الضالة وأن يتبرأ من أهل البدع على العموم وممن لا يرى الشفاعة على الخصوص وأن يلعن منكري الشفاعة من الخوارج والقدرية، فإنه إذا اعتقد ذلك بَرَّ عينه. وكان ممن يجوز الشفاعة إن كان له ذنب وجاز أن يكون هو شفيعاً لغيره جعلنا الله من أهلها برحمته.
And the Khawarij and Qadariyah denied intercession for the people of sins, and they are truthful in that they have no share of it. And they asked us in this chapter about a man who swore by divorcing his wife and freeing his slaves, or swore by God Almighty to do a deed by which he deserves intercession. And they said to us: What is incumbent upon this oath-taker? If you say we command him to avoid sins, then whoever avoids them has no need for intercession; and if you say we command him to commit sins, you would violate the consensus in this. And our answer to this question is: If he swore to do a deed by which he deserves intercession, his oath has become due [i.e., he has broken it], because whoever attains intercession in the hereafter attains it by God's grace without deserving it. And if he swore to do a deed by which he becomes among the people of intercession, we command him to believe in our principles of tawhid and prophethoods, and to avoid deviant innovations, and to disavow the people of innovation generally, and specifically those who do not consider intercession, and to curse the deniers of intercession from the Khawarij and Qadariyah. For if he believes that, his oath is fulfilled. And he becomes among those for whom intercession is permissible if he has a sin, and it is permissible for him to be an intercessor for others. May God make us among its people by His mercy.
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The Khawarij and Qadariyah denied intercession for sinners, and they posed a dilemma: if someone swears to do a deed that deserves intercession, what do you command him? If you tell him to avoid sins, then he doesn't need intercession; if you tell him to commit sins, you violate consensus. Baqillani gives a twofold answer. First, if the oath is about 'deserving' intercession, it is impossible because intercession is purely by God's grace, not earned. So the oath is broken. Second, if the oath is about 'becoming among the people of intercession', it means the person should adhere to correct beliefs (tawhid, prophethood), avoid innovation, and disavow and curse those who deny intercession (i.e., the Khawarij and Qadariyah). By doing so, his oath is fulfilled, and he becomes eligible for intercession if he sins, and can even intercede for others. This refutes the objection by showing that intercession is by grace, and the correct path is belief and disavowal of deniers, not sinning.

Key Terms
خوارج
قدرية
شفاعة
استحقاق
فضل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession can be earned or deserved by performing specific deeds.
Correction: Intercession is purely by God's grace (فضل), not by any deed of the person. Even prophets and angels intercede by God's permission and mercy, not because the sinner deserves it.

Checkpoint

B) Avoid all sins

D) Perform a specific good deed

Key Takeaway
Intercession is by God's grace, not earned; true belief and disavowal of denial make one eligible for it.

?
