The Great Intercession: Prophets Defer to Muhammad
Baqillani narrates the detailed hadith of the Prophet's intercession on the Day of Resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the narrative of the Prophet Muhammad's intercession on the Day of Resurrection as reported in the hadith, and why other prophets defer to him.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession is the ultimate mercy for believers with even the smallest faith.

Baqillani presents this long hadith to establish the doctrine of intercession (shafa‘a) as a cornerstone of Sunni belief. The narrative shows that while all prophets are righteous, only Muhammad is granted the specific role of interceding for the entire community. This passage teaches us about the Prophet's unique station and God's boundless mercy.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narrative
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice the sequence: people in turmoil, prophets approached one by one, each declining until Muhammad accepts.
2
Identify the pattern of refusal
Each prophet declines by referring to a later prophet with a specific title (Khalil, Kalim, Spirit/Word). Why do they decline? What does this tell us about their roles?
Adam declines first, then Ibrahim, Musa, Isa.
3
Examine Muhammad's acceptance and intercession
Muhammad accepts and goes before the Lord. Notice the three rounds of prostration and request. Each time he asks for his nation and is granted a different threshold of faith.
First: grain of barley/wheat; second: mustard seed; third: (incomplete) smallest atom.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
This hadith emphasizes the Prophet's elevated status and the mercy of God. It also shows that intercession is for believers, even those with minimal faith. Consider how this supports Sunni teachings on shafa‘a.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أنس بن مالك: سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم يقول: إذا كان يوم القيامة، ماج الناس بعضهم في بعض. فيؤتى آدم فيقال له: يا آدم اشفع في ذرّيّتك. فيقول: لست لها، ولكن عليكم بإبراهيم، فإنه خليل الرحمن. فيؤتى إبراهيم فيقال له مثل ذلك. فيقول: لست لها ولكن عليكم بموسى فإنه كليم الرحمن. فيؤتى موسى، فيقول: لست لها ولكن عليكم بعيسى، فإنه روح الله وكلمته. قال: فيؤتى عيسى فيقول: لست لها ولكن عليكم بمحمد. فأوتى، فأقول: أنا لها. فأنطلق فأستأذن على ربّي. فيؤذن لي عليه، فأقوم بين يديه، فيلهمني محامده فأحمده بتلك المحامد. ثم أخر ساجداً فيقال لي: يا محمد ارفع رأسك وقل تُسْمع وسل تُعْطَ واشفع تُشَفّع. فأقول: يا ربّ أمتي أمتي! فيقال لي: انطلق فمن كان في قلبه إما قال مثقال ذرة أو مثقال شعيرة من إيمان، فأخرجه منها. قال: فأخرجه ثم أعود فأحمده بتلك المحامد وأخرّ ساجداً. فيقال لي: يا محمد، ارفع رأسك وقل تسمع وسل تعط واشفع تشفع. فأقول: يا ربّ أمتي أمتي! فيقال لي انطلق فمن كان في قلبه مثقال خردلة من إيمان، فأخرجه منها. قال: فأنطلق فأفعل ذلك. ثم أحمده بتلك المحامد، ثم أخرّ ساجداً، فيقال لي: يا محمد ارفع رأسك وقل تسمع وسل تعطه واشفع تشفع. فأقول: يا ربّ أمتي أمتي! فيقال: انطلق، فمن كان في قلبه
Anas ibn Malik said: I heard the Messenger of God, peace be upon him and his family, say: When the Day of Resurrection comes, people will surge into one another. Then Adam will be brought and it will be said to him: O Adam, intercede for your offspring. He will say: I am not for it, but go to Ibrahim, for he is the Khalil of the Most Merciful. Then Ibrahim will be brought and the like will be said to him. He will say: I am not for it, but go to Musa, for he is the Kalim of the Most Merciful. Then Musa will be brought, he will say: I am not for it, but go to 'Isa, for he is the Spirit of God and His Word. He said: Then 'Isa will be brought, he will say: I am not for it, but go to Muhammad. So I will be brought, and I will say: I am for it. So I will go and ask permission of my Lord, and permission will be given to me. Then I will stand before Him, and He will inspire me with praises, and I will praise Him with those praises. Then I will prostrate, and it will be said to me: O Muhammad, raise your head, speak and you will be heard, ask and you will be given, intercede and your intercession will be accepted. So I will say: O Lord, my nation, my nation! It will be said to me: Go, and whoever has in his heart (he said) a grain of barley or a grain of wheat of faith, bring him out from it. He said: So I will bring him out. Then I will return and praise Him with those praises and prostrate. It will be said to me: O Muhammad, raise your head, speak and you will be heard, ask and you will be given, intercede and your intercession will be accepted. So I will say: O Lord, my nation, my nation! It will be said to me: Go, and whoever has in his heart a mustard seed of faith, bring him out from it. He said: So I will go and do that. Then I will praise Him with those praises, then prostrate, and it will be said to me: O Muhammad, raise your head, speak and you will be heard, ask and you will be given, intercede and your intercession will be accepted. So I will say: O Lord, my nation, my nation! It will be said: Go, and whoever has in his heart...
Source pages p. 420

Commentary
This passage is a hadith (narrative) of the great intercession, narrated by Anas ibn Malik. Baqillani presents it as one of the established reports supporting the doctrine of intercession. The hadith describes the events of the Day of Resurrection: people are in turmoil, and the prophets are approached successively to intercede. Adam, Ibrahim, Musa, and 'Isa each decline and refer to the next prophet, until it reaches Muhammad, who accepts. He then goes to his Lord, prostrates, and is granted permission to intercede. He asks for his nation, and the first time he is told to bring out those who have a grain of barley or wheat of faith. He does so. Then a second time, he is told to bring out those who have a mustard seed of faith. He does so. The hadith shows that the Prophet's intercession is for believers with even minimal faith, and it proceeds in stages. The passage ends incomplete, but it communicates the core message of the Prophet's unique role in intercession and the mercy of God.

يوم القيامة
خليل الرحمن
كليم الرحمن
روح الله
مثقال خردلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession is only for the Prophet Muhammad and no other prophet.
Correction: This hadith shows that other prophets are also approached and could potentially intercede, but they defer to Muhammad, indicating his unique role and that the great intercession for the entire community is specifically his.

Checkpoint

B) They refer to the next prophet because of their own sins
C) They indicate that Muhammad is more deserving of intercession
D) They are not present on that day

Key Takeaway
The Prophet Muhammad is the only one who accepts the task of intercession, showing his unique mercy and status, and intercession is granted for believers with even the smallest faith.

?
If only a mustard seed of faith qualifies you for intercession, what does that tell you about the state of your heart? Are you cultivating that seed or neglecting it?

The Prophet's Intercession on the Day of Resurrection
Narrates the hadith of intercession with successive prophets and Muhammad's ultimate intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sequence of the Prophet's intercession and the conditions for those who receive it.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession extends even to those with the smallest amount of faith.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani narrates a hadith detailing the Prophet Muhammad's intercession on the Day of Judgment. It shows the unique role of the Prophet among the prophets. The hadith describes successive rounds of intercession for believers based on their faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith narrative
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the sequence of prophets and the dialogue.
This is a prophetic hadith, so it carries authority.
2
Identify the deferral chain
Observe how Adam, Ibrahim, Musa, and Isa each decline intercession and direct to the next prophet. The chain ends with Muhammad accepting.
This highlights Muhammad's superiority.
3
Analyze the three rounds of intercession
The Prophet intercedes three times for those with decreasing amounts of faith: from a grain/barley grain to a mustard seed to less than a mustard seed. Note the repeated phrases and the fourth round for 'La ilaha illa Allah'.
Each round shows the vastness of his intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقول: إذا كان يوم القيامة، ماج الناس بعضهم في بعض. فيؤتى آدم فيقال له: يا آدم اشفع في ذريتك. فيقول: لست لها، ولكن عليكم بإبراهيم فإنه خليل الرحمن. فيؤتى إبراهيم فيقال له مثل ذلك. فيقول: لست لها ولكن عليكم بموسى فإنه كليم الرحمن. فيؤتى موسى، فيقول: لست لها ولكن عليكم بعيسى فإنه روح الله وكلمته. قال: فيؤتى عيسى فيقول: لست لها ولكن عليكم بمحمد. فأوتى، فأقول: أنا لها. فأنطلق فأستأذن على ربي. فيؤذن لي، فأقوم بين يديه، فيلهمني محامده فأحمده بتلك المحامد. ثم أخر ساجداً فيقال لي: يا محمد ارفع رأسك وقل تسمع وسل تعط واشفع تشفع. فأقول: يا رب أمتي أمتي! فيقال لي: انطلق فمن كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة أو مثقال شعيرة من إيمان فأخرجه منها. قال: فأخرجه ثم أعود فأحمده بتلك المحامد وأخر ساجداً. فيقال لي: يا محمد ارفع رأسك وقل تسمع وسل تعط واشفع تشفع. فأقول: يا رب أمتي أمتي! فيقال لي: انطلق فمن كان في قلبه مثقال خردلة من إيمان فأخرجه منها. قال: فأنطلق فأفعل ذلك. ثم أحمده بتلك المحامد، ثم أخر ساجداً، فيقال لي: يا محمد ارفع رأسك وقل تسمع وسل تعطه واشفع تشفع. فأقول: يا رب أمتي أمتي! فيقال: انطلق، فمن كان في قلبه أدنى من مثقال حبة من خردل من إيمان فأخرجه من النار ثلاث مرات. وزاد الحسن البصري في هذه الرواية عن أنس ابن مالك وثلاثة وعشرين رجلاً. قال: حدثني أنس أنه قال: "فأقوم الرابعة فأحمده بتلك المحامد، ثم أخر ساجداً. قال: فيقال لي: ارفع رأسك وقل تسمع وسل تعطه واشفع تشفع. فأقول: يا رب ائذن لي فيمن قال: لا إله إلا الله. فيقال لي: ليس لك ذلك، ولكن وعزتي وكبريائي وعظمتي لأخرجن منها من قال: لا إله إلا الله!"
He says: When the Day of Resurrection comes, people will surge into one another. Then Adam will be brought and it will be said to him: O Adam, intercede for your offspring. He will say: I am not for that, but go to Ibrahim, for he is the Friend of the Merciful. Then Ibrahim will be brought and the like will be said to him. He will say: I am not for that, but go to Musa, for he is the Interlocutor of the Merciful. Then Musa will be brought, and he will say: I am not for that, but go to Isa, for he is the Spirit of Allah and His Word. He said: Then Isa will be brought and he will say: I am not for that, but go to Muhammad. So I will be brought, and I will say: I am for it. So I will set off and ask permission of my Lord. Permission will be given to me, and I will stand before Him, and He will inspire me with praises and I will praise Him with those praises. Then I will prostrate, and it will be said to me: O Muhammad, raise your head, speak and you will be heard, ask and you will be given, intercede and your intercession will be accepted. So I will say: O Lord, my ummah, my ummah! Then it will be said to me: Go, and whoever has in his heart the weight of a grain or a barley grain of faith, bring him out of it (the Fire). He said: So I will bring him out, then I will return and praise Him with those praises and prostrate. Then it will be said to me: O Muhammad, raise your head, speak and you will be heard, ask and you will be given, intercede and your intercession will be accepted. So I will say: O Lord, my ummah, my ummah! Then it will be said to me: Go, and whoever has in his heart the weight of a mustard seed of faith, bring him out of it. He said: So I will go and do that. Then I will praise Him with those praises, then I will prostrate, and it will be said to me: O Muhammad, raise your head, speak and you will be heard, ask and you will be given, intercede and your intercession will be accepted. So I will say: O Lord, my ummah, my ummah! Then it will be said: Go, and whoever has in his heart less than the weight of a grain of mustard of faith, bring him out of the Fire three times. And al-Hasan al-Basri added in this narration from Anas ibn Malik and twenty-three men. He said: Anas narrated to me that he said: "Then I will stand up a fourth time and praise Him with those praises, then I will prostrate. He said: Then it will be said to me: Raise your head, speak and you will be heard, ask and you will be given, intercede and your intercession will be accepted. So I will say: O Lord, permit me for whoever said: La ilaha illa Allah. Then it will be said to me: That is not for you, but by My might, majesty, and greatness, I will surely bring out from it whoever said: La ilaha illa Allah!"
Source pages p. 421

Commentary
This passage is a hadith narrative describing the Prophet's intercession (shafa'ah) on the Day of Judgment. It begins with the Prophet Muhammad reporting a hadith: when people are in distress, they approach Adam, then Ibrahim, then Musa, then Isa, each deferring to the next. Finally, they come to Muhammad, who accepts. He then describes three rounds of intercession for those with faith even the size of a grain or a mustard seed. A fourth round is added by al-Hasan al-Basri's narration, where the Prophet asks for those who said 'La ilaha illa Allah,' and Allah grants it by His own will. The hadith emphasizes that the Prophet's intercession is vast and covers even those with minimal faith. The sequence shows the unique status of Muhammad among the prophets. The addition by al-Hasan al-Basri shows the textual transmission of the hadith.

Key Terms
شفاعة (intercession)
يوم القيامة (Day of Resurrection)
إيمان (faith)
أمة (ummah/community)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession is only for major sinners or those with strong faith.
Correction: The hadith shows intercession is for all believers, even those with faith as small as a mustard seed, and ultimately for anyone who uttered 'La ilaha illa Allah'.

Checkpoint
In the hadith of intercession, which prophet is the first to be asked to intercede?
A) Ibrahim
B) Muhammad
C) Adam
D) Musa

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intercession encompasses all believers, even those with minimal faith, and it is a manifestation of Allah's mercy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet pleaded four times for his ummah, even for those with the smallest faith. When you sin or neglect your duties, do you feel that the Prophet's love and intercession cover you? What would it mean for you to truly rely on that intercession while striving to increase your faith?
?
In the hadith, the Prophet does not intercede for those who never said 'La ilaha illa Allah'. If you were to die tonight, would you be among those whom the Prophet would intercede for? What are you doing today to ensure that phrase is alive in your heart?
?
Allah says 'by My might, majesty, and greatness, I will bring out from it whoever said La ilaha illa Allah.' Does your hope in Allah's mercy outweigh your fear of punishment? How does this hadith challenge you to balance hope and fear in your daily life?

The Mass-Transmission of Intercession Reports
States that reports on intercession are abundant and mutawatir, confirming the exit of monotheists from the Fire.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the reports on intercession are mutawatir and unanimously confirm the salvation of monotheists, despite differences in wording.

Core Idea
The many hadiths on intercession all agree: monotheists will leave the Fire.

Imam Baqillani now addresses a key sam'iyyat issue—the reality of intercession. He argues that the sheer number and consistent meaning of these reports, even with varied wordings, establish certainty. This lesson explores how he defends the doctrine using hadith methodology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the confident tone and the claim of abundance.
2
Identify the core claim
The author states the reports are mutawatir and consistent (mutawāfiyah) on one key point: the exit of monotheists from the Fire by the Prophet's intercession. This is the foundation.
Mutawatir means transmitted by so many chains that collusion is impossible.
3
Examine the supporting details
He mentions three vivid details from different reports: being burnt to charcoal, emerging in groups, and entering Paradise with 'Jahannami' written on their foreheads. These details add texture but do not contradict the core.
The differences show the variety of narrations, not inconsistency.
4
Reflect on the methodological lesson
Ask yourself: how does this argument defend intercession against doubts? The answer is that tawātur provides certainty, and even differing wordings support the same essential truth.
This is a classic Sunni argument for relying on mass-transmitted hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأخبار في الشفاعة أكثر من أن يؤتى عليها، وهي كلها متواترة متوافية على خروج الموحدين من النار بشفاعة الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم، وإن اختلفت ألفاظها. ففي بعضها أنهم يخرجون بعد ما امتحشوا فيه وصاروا فحماً. وفي خبر أنهم يخرجون منها ضبائر ضبائر فيلقون في نهر الحياة فينبتون كما تنبت الطراثيث والحبة في جميل السيل. وأنهم يدخلون الجنة مكتوباً على جباههم "الجهنميون"
And the reports on intercession are more than can be enumerated. They are all mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and consistent upon the exit of the monotheists from the Fire by the intercession of the Messenger, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, even if their wordings differ. In some of them, they come out after having been burnt in it and become charcoal. And in a report, they come out of it in groups and are thrown into the River of Life, and they sprout as sprouts and seeds sprout in the silt of a flood. And they enter Paradise with 'Jahannami' (Hell-related) written on their foreheads.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument for the authenticity and consistency of the intercession reports. The author begins by stating that the reports about intercession (shafa'ah) are too numerous to count, establishing their abundance. He then asserts that they are all mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and that they agree (mutawaafiyah) on the core doctrine: that monotheists (muwahhidun) will be taken out of the Fire through the intercession of the Prophet, even though the wordings differ. This is a key point in kalam methodology: mutawatir reports give certainty. Then he mentions some specific details from different reports: some say they come out after being burnt to charcoal; another says they come out in groups (dhaba'ir) and are thrown into the River of Life, where they grow like plants; and they enter Paradise with 'Jahannami' written on their foreheads. These details reinforce the reality of intercession despite textual variations. The passage thus defends the doctrine against those who might deny it due to differences in narration.

Key Terms
متواتر (mutawatir/mass-transmitted)
موحدين (monotheists)
نار (Fire)
نهر الحياة (River of Life)
شفاعة (intercession)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the reports on intercession?
A) They are few and contradictory.
B) They are numerous, mutawatir, and consistent on the exit of monotheists.
C) They are only found in weak narrations.
D) They apply only to the Prophet's own family.

Key Takeaway
The intercession reports are mutawatir and unanimously confirm that monotheists will exit the Fire, despite varied wordings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The hadiths describe sinners exiting the Fire as charcoal, yet they are still called 'monotheists'. Do you truly believe that your tawhid is enough to secure your ultimate salvation, even if your deeds are deficient? How does this certainty change the way you view your own sins and your relationship with the Prophet (ﷺ)?
?
The Prophet's intercession is so vast that it rescues those who have been reduced to charcoal. Have you ever despaired of Allah's mercy for yourself or someone else? What would it take for you to genuinely hope for the worst of sinners, including yourself, to be saved by that intercession?
?
The reports on intercession are mutawatir—certain beyond doubt. Yet, do you live as if this intercession is guaranteed for you without condition? Or do you fear that your lack of love for the Prophet and neglect of his sunnah might distance you from his shafa‘ah? What one concrete change will you make today to strengthen your connection to him?

Salaf's Consensus Proves Intercession Reports
Baqillani uses Salaf's consensus to prove intercession hadiths are authentic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the consensus of the Salaf to argue for the authenticity of intercession hadiths and refute the Mu'tazila position.

Core Idea
The Salaf's unanimous acceptance proves intercession reports are authentic.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani presents a powerful argument from the early Muslim community's consensus (ijma' of practice) to defend the authenticity of hadiths about intercession (shafa'ah). He explains that the Companions and Successors accepted these reports without objection, and if they were false, they would have been rejected. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and its refutation of the Mu'tazila who claimed intercession contradicts reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its literal translation without analysis. Let the author's own rhythm and structure come through.
Notice the repeated conditional 'if... then' structure.
2
Analyze the reductio ad absurdum
Baqillani argues that if these hadiths were invalid, the Companions—who were best positioned—would have rejected them. Since no such rejection is recorded, the hadiths must be authentic.
This is a 'consequence argument' based on what would have happened.
3
Connect to the Mu'tazila debate
Understand how this argument directly refutes the Mu'tazila claim that intercession is rationally invalid. Baqillani concludes that the widespread transmission of these reports confirms their truth.
The Mu'tazila argued that forgiveness cannot be earned, so intercession is irrational.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أطبق سلف الأمة على تسليم هذه الرواية وصحتها ظهورها مع وانتشارها والعلم بأنها مرويّة في الصحابة والتابعين. ولو كانت مما لم تقم الحجّة بها، لطعن طاعن فيها بدفع العقل والسمع لها على ما يقوله المعتزلة، ولكانت الصحابة أعلم بذلك وأشدّ تسرعاً إلى إنكارها. ولو كانوا قد فعلوا ذلك، أو بعضهم، لظهر ذلك وانتشر ولتوفّرت الدواعي على إذاعته وإبدائه، حتى ينقل نقله ويحل العلم به محل العلم بخبر الشفاعة لأن هذه العادة ثابتة في الأخبار. وفي العلم بفساد ذلك دليل على ثبوت خبر الشفاعة وبطلان قول المعتزلة إن الغفران باطل بالعقل وموجب لتكذيب السمع وغير ذلك مما يدعونه.
And the Salaf of the Ummah have unanimously agreed upon accepting this narration and its authenticity, its [widespread] appearance, and [its] spread, and the knowledge that it is transmitted among the Companions and the Successors. And if it were something by which the proof was not established, an objector would have objected to it by repelling reason and transmission against it according to what the Mu'tazila say, and the Companions would be more knowledgeable of that and quicker to deny it. And if they had done that, or some of them, it would have appeared and spread, and the motives would have been ample to broadcast it and reveal it, until it would be transmitted like its transmission and knowledge of it would occupy the place of knowledge of the report of intercession, because this habit is established in reports. And in the knowledge of the corruption of that is evidence for the establishment of the report of intercession and the invalidity of the Mu'tazila's statement that forgiveness is invalidated by reason and necessitates the denial of transmission, and other things they claim.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is an argument from the consensus of the Salaf to prove the authenticity of hadiths about intercession (shafa'ah). Baqillani begins by stating that the early community (Salaf) unanimously accepted these reports, acknowledging their transmission among the Companions and Successors. He then employs a reductio ad absurdum: If these hadiths were not valid proof, critics (like the Mu'tazila) would have attacked them on both rational and scriptural grounds. Since the Companions were closest to the Prophet and most vigilant, they would have been quick to reject any false report. But no such rejection was recorded; on the contrary, these reports became widespread. The fact that the rejection did not occur, despite the strong motivation to spread it, indicates that the reports are authentic. He draws an analogy: the same way we know the report of intercession (i.e., the major intercession) is widely transmitted, so too are these reports. Finally, he concludes that knowing the falsehood of the Mu'tazila's claim that forgiveness is invalidated by reason proves the truth of the intercession hadiths and refutes their position.

Key Terms
سلف
رواية
شفاعة
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think consensus (ijma') here means a formal binding consensus; Baqillani uses 'itbaq' (agreement) as a practical indication of acceptance, not a formal legal consensus.
Correction: Baqillani's argument does not rely on formal ijma but on the historical fact that no early rejection occurred, indicating widespread acceptance.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue would have happened if the intercession hadiths were not valid?
A) The Mu'tazila would have accepted them
B) The Companions would have quickly rejected them
C) They would have been forgotten
D) The Salaf would have argued about them

Key Takeaway
The unanimous acceptance of intercession reports by the early Muslims proves their authenticity and refutes rational objections.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a religious teaching that seems to clash with your own rational judgment, do you immediately dismiss it or do you pause to consider how the early Muslims—who were closer to revelation—accepted it? What would it take for you to trust transmitted knowledge over your own reasoning in such a case? Spend time this week studying a hadith that challenges your assumptions.
?
The Salaf unanimously accepted the intercession reports without known objection. Is there any point of Islamic belief that you personally struggle to accept because of your intellect or culture? Rather than reject it, are you willing to investigate what the earliest generations understood, as Baqillani urges? Commit to reading one classical commentary on that issue.
?
If the Companions and Successors feared no contradiction between reason and revelation in the matter of intercession, what does that say about your own doubts? Are your hesitations perhaps influenced by modern 'rationalism' rather than the pure lens of the Salaf? Ask Allah to show you the truth as the early community saw it, and write down one step you will take to align your heart with theirs.

Answering the Objection of a Conflicting Hadith on Intercession
Baqillani refutes an objection to intercession hadiths.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes an objection by first questioning the authenticity of the opposing hadith and then interpreting it harmoniously with the established intercession hadiths.

Core Idea
An objection's hadith is dismissed as unreliable, then interpreted away.

Baqillani now addresses a potential objection: a hadith seems to deny intercession for major sinners. He must show it does not contradict the established teachings. His response is two-pronged: first he attacks the hadith's reliability, then he offers a reconciling interpretation, demonstrating a key method in Islamic theological debate.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first response
Identify the objection: a hadith from Hasan al-Basri claims the Prophet said his intercession will not reach major sinners. Notice Baqillani's first move: he questions the authenticity of this hadith, saying it is not well-known or established.
This is a common tactic—doubt the source before engaging its content.
2
Examine the second response and Quranic analogy
Even if the hadith were accepted, Baqillani says it must be interpreted alongside the other hadiths. He gives an example from the Quran of reconciling seemingly contradictory verses (Sura 77:35 vs. Sura 37:27) to show that interpretation is possible.
The key is to avoid discarding any authentic tradition if it can be harmonized.
3
Understand the final interpretation
Baqillani interprets 'people of major sins' in the objection hadith to mean apostates or disbelievers, not Muslims who commit sins. This removes the contradiction with the intercession hadiths that promise intercession for believers.
The interpretation is guided by other clear hadiths.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: فإن قالوا: هذه الأحاديث معارضة بمثلها. فروى الحسن البصري وغيره عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم أنه قال: «لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي». فوجب إطراحها. يقال لهم: هذه الرواية التي ذكرتموها غير معروفة ولا ثابتة عند أهل النقل. فلا يجب أن يدفع بها ما قد علمنا نحن وأنتم أنه مروي. ثم يقال لهم: لو سلمت روايتكم لوجب حملها مع الأخبار التي رويناها على ضرب من التأويل، حتى لا يدفع من السنن ما يمكن استعمالها وتصحيحها كما ذلك يصنع في قوله تعالى: هذا يوم لا ينطقون وقوله: وأقبل بعضهم على بعض يتساءلون. فنقول: قوله: «لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي» أراد بذلك: إن كانت الكبائر الواقعة منهم ردة بعد إسلام أو كفرا بعد إيمان، بدلالة الأخبار الأخر التي فيها إخراج أهل الإيمان بشفاعته فلا يكون لذلك معارضاً.
Issue: If they say: These hadiths are contradicted by similar ones. Al-Hasan al-Basri and others narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him and his family, that he said: 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my community.' So it is necessary to discard them. It is said to them: This narration you mentioned is unknown and not established among the people of transmission. So it is not necessary to reject by it what we and you know to be transmitted. Then it is said to them: Even if we accept your narration, it would be necessary to interpret it alongside the hadiths we narrated in a way of interpretation, so that from the traditions that can be used and corrected are not rejected, just as is done with His saying: 'This is a day they shall not speak' and His saying: 'And they will turn to one another asking questions.' So we say: His saying 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my community' meant by that: if the major sins that occurred from them were apostasy after Islam or disbelief after faith, as indicated by the other hadiths in which the people of faith are brought out by his intercession, so it is not contradictory to that.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objectors claim that there is a contradictory hadith: the Prophet said his intercession will not reach the people of major sins. Therefore the intercession hadiths should be rejected. Baqillani gives a two-part answer. First, he questions the authenticity of this hadith, saying it is not well-known or established among hadith scholars, so it cannot override what is well-known. Second, he argues hypothetically: even if the hadith were authentic, it must be interpreted in harmony with the other hadiths. He gives an example from the Quran where apparently contradictory verses are reconciled: Allah says 'This is a day they shall not speak' (al-Mursalat 35) and also says 'And they will turn to one another asking questions' (al-Saffat 27). These are reconciled by understanding that different times or groups are meant. Similarly, the hadith about shafa'ah not reaching the major sinners can be understood to mean those whose major sins are apostasy or disbelief (i.e., they are no longer Muslims), not the believers. This is supported by other hadiths that show the faithful are taken out of Hell by intercession. Thus no real contradiction exists.

Key Terms
معارضة
تأويل
شفاعة
كبائر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani respond to the hadith 'لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر'?
A) He accepts it and abandons other hadiths
B) He says it is inauthentic and if authentic, it refers to apostates
C) He says it applies to all sinners
D) He says it is abrogated

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends intercession hadiths by discrediting the opposing hadith and reinterpreting it to refer to apostates.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were faced with a hadith that seems to contradict what you believe about Allah's mercy, would you follow Baqillani's method of first verifying its authenticity, or would you be quick to reject the well-known? Are you willing to critically examine the sources before you reject a comforting truth about intercession?
?
The objectors used a hadith to deny intercession for major sinners. Are you confident that your own minor or major sins do not disqualify you from the Prophet's intercession? What assurance do you have that your faith, however weak, places you among those who are saved by intercession?
?
Baqillani interprets the objection hadith to refer to apostates. Examine your own heart: do you hold any belief that might be akin to apostasy? Are you clinging to Islam firmly enough to be included in the community of intercession?

Baqillani Responds to the 'Ummati' Objection
Baqillani responds to the objection by offering two possible meanings of 'Ummati'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends his interpretation by showing the term 'Ummati' can refer to apostates or contemporaries, not only believing Muslims.

Core Idea
The Prophet's word 'Ummati' is broader than just believing followers.

Baqillani now faces a direct objection: if the hadith says 'from my community', doesn't that imply they are Muslims? He responds by showing the phrase can be interpreted in more than one way. This lesson examines his two-fold answer and how it preserves his original argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting the structure: objection then two possible interpretations.
The answer is introduced with 'qīla lahum'.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Find the two interpretations Baqillani offers for 'Ummati' and understand each.
One refers to apostates, the other to contemporaries.
3
Reflect on the ambiguity
Consider why the term 'Ummati' is ambiguous and how that undermines the objection.
This shows the hadith does not necessarily refer to believing Muslims.
4
Connect to the broader argument
Think about how this answer defends Baqillani's original interpretation about intercession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: قوله: «لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي» يمنع تأويلكم هذا، لأنه حكم بأنهم من أمته، وذلك يقتضي أنهم قوم مسلمون. قيل لهم: يحتمل أن يكون أراد بقوله «أمتي» الذين كانوا من أمتي ثم ارتدوا. ويحتمل أن يكون أراد أهل قرني وعصري الذين بعثت فيهم فلا تعلق لهم في ذلك.
If they say: His saying 'My intercession will not reach the people of major sins from my community' prevents this interpretation of yours, because he ruled that they are from his community, and that necessitates that they are a people of Muslims. It is said to them: It is possible that by his saying 'my community' he meant those who were from my community then apostatized. And it is possible that he meant the people of my generation and my era whom I was sent to, so they have no connection to that.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage is a follow-up objection and answer. The objectors argue that Baqillani's interpretation (that the hadith refers to apostates) is invalid because the Prophet specifically said 'from my community' (min ummati), which implies they are Muslims. How can they be apostates if they are called his community? Baqillani offers two possible interpretations. First, 'Ummati' can refer to those who were once believers and part of his community but later left it through apostasy; the term can be used for their former status. Second, 'Ummati' might mean the people of his time and his era (ahl qarni wa 'asri) to whom he was sent, even if they later disbelieved. In either case, the objection does not refute his interpretation, because the term is ambiguous. The point is that the hadith does not necessarily apply to believing sinners; it can refer to those who have left the faith entirely.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'Ummati' always refers to current believing followers.
Correction: Baqillani shows it can also refer to former believers who apostatized or contemporaries regardless of belief.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani suggest as a possible meaning of 'Ummati' in the hadith?
A) All people, including non-believers
B) Those who were once Muslims then apostatized
C) Only the Companions
D) All Muslims until Judgment Day

Key Takeaway
The term 'Ummati' in prophetic hadith does not necessarily indicate belief; it can refer to those who were once part of the community or those alive in his time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Interpreting the Hadith on Intercession for Major Sinners
Imam Baqillani interprets a hadith and answers an objection regarding intercession for major sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani reconciles the hadith that seems to deny intercession for major sinners with other texts affirming intercession.

Core Idea
Apparent contradictions in hadith are resolved through careful interpretation, not rejection.

Imam Baqillani addresses a potential contradiction: a hadith says the Prophet's intercession does not reach major sinners, but other hadiths say it does. He shows that through proper interpretation, both can be true. This lesson walks through his argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and English translation to grasp the flow of the objection and answer. Notice the dialectical structure.
Look for the conditional acceptance at the start.
2
Identify the core interpretation
Baqillani interprets 'major sins' in the hadith as apostasy or disbelief after faith. Find where he states this and how he supports it with other narrations.
3
Understand the objection
The opponents argue that the phrase 'from my community' shows the sinners are Muslims, not apostates. Why does this objection seem strong?
This is a key point in the debate.
4
Analyze Baqillani's answer
He offers two possible interpretations of 'my community' that defuse the objection. Identify both and see how they work.
The first: those who were part of the community but then apostatized. The second: contemporaries only.
5
Reflect on the method
Notice how Baqillani uses other hadiths and Qur'anic examples to justify interpretation. This is a standard method in kalam.
He shows that reconciling texts is preferred over rejecting them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : لو سلمت روايتكم لوجب حملها مع الأخبار التي رويناها على ضرب من البناء و التأويل، حتى لا يُدْفَع من السنن يمكن استعمالها وتصحيحها [؟] كما ذلك [؟] يصنع في قوله تعالى : هذا يوم لا ينطقون [؟] وقوله : ﴿ وأقبل بعضهم على بعض يتساءلون . فنقول : قوله : «لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي أراد بذلك : إن كانت الكبائر الواقعة منهم ردّة بعد إسلام أو كفراً بعد إيمان ، بدلالة الأخبار الأخر التي فيها إخراج أهل الإيمان بشفاعته فلا يكون لذلك معارضاً . فإن قالوا : قوله : لا تنال شفاعتي أهل الكبائر من أمتي» يمنع تأويلكم هذا، لأنه حكم بأنهم من أمته، وذلك يقتضي أنهم قوم مسلمون . قيل لهم : يحتمل أن يكون أراد بقوله «أمتي» الذين كانوا من أمتي ثم ارتدوا . ويحتمل أن يكون اراد أهل قرني وعصري الذين بعثت فيهم فلا تعلق لهم في ذلك
Then it is said to them: If your narration is accepted, it must be interpreted alongside the narrations we have related in a way of interpretation and allegory, so that the traditions that can be used and verified are not rejected, just as is done in His saying: 'This is a day they shall not speak' and His saying: 'And they turn to one another, asking'. So we say: His statement: 'My intercession does not reach the people of major sins from my community' – He intended by that: if the major sins committed by them were apostasy after Islam or disbelief after faith, as indicated by the other narrations which affirm the removal of the people of faith by his intercession, so there is no contradiction. If they say: His statement: 'My intercession does not reach the people of major sins from my community' prevents this interpretation of yours, because it rules that they are from his community, and that requires that they are Muslim people. It is said to them: It is possible that He meant by 'my community' those who were from my community then apostatized. And it is possible that He meant the people of my era and century in whom I was sent, so they have no basis in that.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer regarding a hadith that seems to deny intercession for major sinners. The author begins by stating that even if the opponent's hadith is accepted, it must be interpreted in light of other hadiths that confirm intercession. He gives examples from the Qur'an where apparently contradictory statements are reconciled through interpretation. Then he provides a specific interpretation: the hadith 'My intercession does not reach the people of major sins from my community' refers to those whose major sins amount to apostasy, i.e., they became disbelievers. This is supported by other narrations that limit intercession to believers. He concludes that there is no contradiction. The objection follows: the hadith explicitly says 'from my community', implying they are Muslims, not apostates. The answer provides two possibilities: either 'my community' means those who were originally part of his community but then apostatized, or it means the people of his time and generation, so the objection is not valid.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'My intercession does not reach the people of major sins' contradicts other hadiths about intercession and cannot be reconciled.
Correction: Imam Baqillani shows that the hadith can be interpreted to refer only to apostates (those whose major sin is leaving Islam), not to believing Muslims. Thus, there is no contradiction.

Imam Baqillani shows that a hadith denying intercession can be interpreted harmoniously with other texts by understanding the intended meaning of 'major sins' and 'my community'.

The objectors held onto a literal reading of 'my community' and missed the deeper meaning. Where in your own understanding of Islam might you be clinging to a surface-level interpretation that closes off the mercy or wisdom Allah intends for you?

Objection: Eternal Punishment Hadiths vs. Intercession
Opponent cites hadiths threatening eternal punishment for suicide and wine drinking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the apparent contradiction posed by hadiths that threaten eternal punishment for certain sins against the promise of intercession.

Core Idea
Hadiths on eternal punishment seem to block intercession—unless read with condition.

Imam Baqillani continues to defend the reality of intercession. Here he considers a powerful objection: there are authentic hadiths that clearly say certain sinners will be punished eternally. If that is true, how can intercession save them? The opponent cites several specific sins. We will examine this objection to see the challenge it presents.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's objection
Read the Arabic passage presenting the hadiths from the Prophet. Notice the specific sins mentioned: suicide by poison, iron, falling from a height, and also perpetual wine drinking and disobedience to parents.
These hadiths are cited as evidence against intercession.
2
Identify the apparent contradiction
The opponent claims these hadiths contradict reports of intercession. Reflect on why they see a conflict. If these sinners are eternally punished, intercession cannot save them.
3
Understand the opponent's logic
The opponent treats these hadiths as absolute and unconditional. They think the threat of eternal punishment applies to anyone who commits these sins, making intercession impossible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أفليس قد روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم أنه قال: «من تحسى سماً فقتل نفسه، فهو يتحساه في نار جهنم خالداً مخلداً فيها أبداً» ؟ ورُوي مثله فيمن قتل نفسه بحديدة ومن تردى من جبل . وكذلك روي عنه أنه قال: «لا يدخل الجنة مدمن خمر عاق لوالديه» . وهذه الأخبار معارضة لأخبار الشفاعة . قيل لهم : لو ثبتت هذه الأخبار كثبوت خبر الشفاعة لم تكن متعارضة بل يجب أن يكون قوله : «من تحسى سماً فقتل نفسه، ومن أدمن الخمر ومن عق والديه وتردى من جبل، وقتل نفسه بحديدة» ينصرف إلى من فعل ذلك أجمع على وجه الاستحلال وتكذيب الخبر والتوقيف على تحريمه . لأن ذلك لا يقع على جهة التكذيب ممن يستحق الشفاعة .
If they say: Has it not been narrated from the Prophet, peace and blessings upon him and his family, that he said: 'Whoever drinks poison and kills himself, he will be sipping it in the fire of Hell, eternally abiding therein forever'? And similar is narrated about one who kills himself with an iron instrument and one who throws himself from a mountain. Likewise, it is narrated from him that he said: 'A perpetual wine drinker and one who is undutiful to his parents will not enter Paradise.' These reports contradict the reports of intercession. It is said to them: If these reports were established as firmly as the report of intercession, they would not be contradictory. Rather, His statement: 'Whoever drinks poison and kills himself, and whoever persists in drinking wine, and whoever is undutiful to his parents, and throws himself from a mountain, and kills himself with an iron instrument' must refer to one who does all that with the intention of deeming it lawful and denying the report and the warning of its prohibition, because such an act does not occur on the part of one who deserves intercession.
Source pages p. 424

Commentary
This passage presents another objection against the intercession reports. The opponent cites explicit hadiths that threaten eternal punishment for certain sins like suicide and perpetual drinking. These seem to contradict the idea that the Prophet's intercession can save people. The answer explains that the threat applies only to those who commit these acts while believing them to be lawful (istihlal) and rejecting the prophetic prohibition (takdhib al-khabar). Those who commit sins while still believing in their prohibition do not deserve eternal punishment and may benefit from intercession.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
قتل النفس
تحسى سماً
مدمن خمر
عاق لوالديه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadiths about eternal punishment for suicide and wine drinking are unconditional and apply to every person who commits these sins.
Correction: Imam Baqillani will explain that these punishments are conditional upon the person deeming the sin lawful and denying the prohibition.

Checkpoint
According to the opponent, what is the relationship between the hadiths on eternal punishment and the reports of intercession?
A) They support each other.
B) They are contradictory.
C) They are unrelated.
D) They are both about the same people.

Key Takeaway
The opponent uses hadiths on eternal punishment to argue that intercession is impossible for certain sinners.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Read the hadith about the perpetual wine drinker. Is there any habit or sin in your life that you have normalized, thinking it's not that serious? What would it mean for you if that sin actually barred you from Paradise without intercession? Will you take a concrete step today to break that habit?
?
The opponent claims these hadiths contradict intercession. Have you ever secretly doubted that God could forgive a particular sin you've committed? How does the existence of these severe warnings affect your trust in His mercy? Will you ask Allah tonight for forgiveness and renewed hope?

The Answer: Conditional Punishment Based on Istihlal
Baqillani explains that eternal punishment is conditional on istihlal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani resolves the apparent contradiction by stating that the eternal punishment applies only to those who commit the sins while deeming them lawful and rejecting the prophetic prohibition.

Core Idea
Eternal punishment is for those who deem the sin lawful, not for those who believe it's wrong.

Imam Baqillani now provides the answer to the objection. He argues that the hadiths are not unconditional. Rather, they refer to a specific type of person: one who commits these sins with istihlal (deeming them lawful) and takdhib (denial). This nuance resolves the conflict with intercession and preserves the mercy of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer carefully
Read the Arabic passage of Baqillani's response. Notice how he begins by conceding the authenticity of the hadiths hypothetically, then introduces the condition.
2
Understand the condition: istihlal and takdhib
Baqillani says the punishment applies to one who does all these acts 'on the face of istihlal and takdhib al-khabar wa al-tawqif 'ala tahrimihi.' This means they consider the sin lawful and deny the warning of its prohibition.
Istihlal is a key concept: deeming something haram as halal.
3
Connect to intercession
Baqillani explains that such an act does not occur from one who deserves intercession. That is, a person who commits a sin while still believing it is forbidden can be a candidate for intercession.
4
Reflect on the resolution
The apparent contradiction is resolved: the hadiths do not negate intercession for those who sin out of weakness but believe it is wrong. Only those who reject the Shariah are excluded.

The answer explains that the threat applies only to those who commit these acts while believing them to be lawful (istihlal) and rejecting the prophetic prohibition (takdhib al-khabar). Those who commit sins while still believing in their prohibition do not deserve eternal punishment and may benefit from intercession.

Resolving the Apparent Contradiction: Intercession and Threatening Hadith
Baqillani answers objection that hadith on suicide and alcohol contradict intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani reconciles hadith that threaten eternal punishment for certain sins with the doctrine of intercession (shafā'a) by invoking the concepts of istihlāl (considering sin permissible) and takdhīb (denying the prohibition).

Core Idea
Intercession is for believers who sin without considering it permissible.

This lesson presents a classic objection against intercession: certain authentic hadith threaten eternal punishment for suicide, habitual drinking, and disobedience to parents. How can intercession still be valid? Baqillani offers a precise answer by distinguishing between those who sin out of weakness and those who sin while denying the prohibition itself.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. The objector cites several hadith that seem to promise eternal punishment for specific sins and claims they contradict intercession reports. Notice the tone: the objector uses 'فإن قالوا' to introduce the challenge.
The hadith mentioned include suicide by poison, iron, jumping from a mountain, and habitual drinking.
2
Analyze Baqillani's response
Baqillani does not reject the hadith but argues they are not contradictory. Instead, he explains that these severe threats apply only to those who commit the sins with istihlāl (considering them permissible) and takdhīb (denying the prohibition). Such a person does not deserve intercession.
The key move is interpreting the threat as conditional on the perpetrator's attitude, not the act itself.
3
Understand the key terms
Focus on the Arabic terms: الاستحلال (istihlāl) meaning considering something permissible, and التكذيب (takdhīb) meaning denial. Also التوقيف على تحريمه (al-tawqīf 'alā taḥrīmih) meaning the notification of its prohibition. These terms are central to the argument.
Baqillani is using a principle from uṣūl al-fiqh: a threat may be conditional on the presence of an aggravating factor.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أفليس قد روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم أنه قال: «من تحسى سماً فقتل نفسه، فهو يتحساه في نار جهنم خالداً مخلداً فيها أبداً»؟ ورُوي مثله فيمن قتل نفسه بحديدة ومن تردی من جبل . وكذلك رُوي عنه أنه قال: «لا يدخل الجنَّةَ مُدمن خمر عاق لوالديه . وهذه الأخبار معارضة لأخبار الشفاعة 
قيل لهم : لو ثبتت هذه الأخبار كثبوت خبر الشفاعة لم تكن متعارضة بل يجب أن يكون قوله : من تحسّى سماً فقتل نفسه، ومن أدمن الخمر ومن عقّ والديه وتردّى من جبل، وقتل نفسه بحديدة ينصرف إلى من فعل ذلك أجمع على وجه الاستحلال وتكذيب الخبر والتوقيف على تحريمه . لأن ذلك لا يقع على جهة التكذيب ممن يستحق الشفاعة .
If they say: 'Has it not been narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) that he said: "Whoever swallows poison and kills himself, he will be swallowing it in the fire of Hell, eternally abiding therein forever"? And similar is narrated about whoever kills himself with an iron weapon and whoever throws himself from a mountain. And likewise it is narrated from him that he said: "An habitual drinker of wine, undutiful to his parents will not enter Paradise." These reports contradict the reports of intercession.' It is said to them: If these reports were as established as the report of intercession, they would not be contradictory. Rather, his statement: 'Whoever swallows poison and kills himself, and whoever habitually drinks wine, and whoever is undutiful to his parents, and throws himself from a mountain, and kills himself with an iron weapon' must be interpreted as referring to one who does all of that on the basis of considering it permissible (istihlāl) and denying the report and the notification of its prohibition. Because that does not occur on the basis of denial from one who deserves intercession.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer (mas'ala) in which an objector cites several hadith that appear to threaten eternal punishment for suicide, alcohol, etc., and claims these contradict reports about intercession (shafā'a). The responder argues that if these hadith were as authentic as the intercession report, they would not be contradictory. Instead, the threatening hadith must be interpreted as referring to those who commit these sins while considering them permissible (istihlāl) and denying the prohibition (takdhīb al-khabar wa al-tawqīf 'alā taḥrīmih). Such a person does not deserve intercession. So intercession is for believers who sin without considering it permissible.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
الاستحلال
التكذيب
التوقيف على تحريمه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that these hadith absolutely deny intercession for any sinner, even if they repent or do not consider the sin permissible.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that the threat applies only to those who commit the sin while considering it permissible and denying its prohibition, not to believers who sin out of weakness.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the condition for the hadith about suicide to apply without intercession?
A) The person committed the sin
B) The person considered it permissible and denied its prohibition
C) The person was a non-Muslim
D) The person committed the sin repeatedly

Key Takeaway
Baqillani resolves the apparent contradiction by restricting the threatening hadith to those who commit sins with istihlāl and takdhīb, thus preserving intercession for repentant believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever caught yourself making excuses for a sin by downplaying its seriousness or convincing yourself that it's not that bad? How does Baqillani's condition of istihlāl challenge you to examine whether you truly believe the prohibition in your heart?
?
You may rely on the hope of intercession to justify ongoing sin. But this lesson ties intercession to genuine belief in the prohibition. Ask yourself: Do I actively remind myself that this sin is forbidden, or do I commit it as if it were permissible?
?
Think of a sin you struggle with. In the quiet of your heart, do you truly accept that Allah has prohibited it, or do you harbor doubt? Your answer determines whether Baqillani would consider you deserving of intercession. What will you change today?

Three Interpretations of Hadith Denying Intercession
Baqillani interprets hadith that seem to deny intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three ways Baqillani interprets hadith that appear to deny intercession for non-believers, and why they do not contradict the doctrine of intercession.

Core Idea
Hadith that seem to deny intercession are open to multiple interpretations that preserve the doctrine.

This passage presents an objection against intercession based on prophetic hadith that appear to exclude sinners from the Prophet's community. Baqillani responds by showing that such hadith are not literal but admit three possible interpretations. By examining these interpretations, we see how intercession remains compatible with scriptural warnings.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and the cited hadith
The objector cites two hadith: 'the thief does not steal while he is a believer' and 'he is not of us who goes to bed full while his neighbor is hungry.' Understand the apparent conflict with intercession.
2
Identify the first interpretation
Baqillani says the hadith refer to those who commit sins while considering them permissible (mustahill). Such people reject the prohibition, so intercession does not apply to them.
3
Identify the second interpretation
The sinner is not a believer in the sense of being equal in righteousness and purity to one who avoids those sins entirely.
4
Identify the third interpretation
These hadith are hyperbolic warnings (taghlīẓ wa mubālagha) for deterrence, similar to 'no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque.'
5
Reflect on the implications
Under any interpretation, the hadith do not absolutely deny intercession, so they do not contradict the reports that affirm it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أفليس الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم عندكم لا يشفع إلا في مؤمن؟ وقد وردت الروايات بأن السارق لا يسرق حين يسرق وهو مؤمن، ولا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن. فكيف يشفع الرسل صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم فيمن ليس بمؤمن؟ وكذلك رُوي عنه أنه قال: ليس منا من بات بطيناً وجاره خميص. فكيف تحصل الشفاعة لمن ليس من أهل ملته؟ يقال لهم: هذه الأخبار أيضاً محتملة لوجوه، إذا صرفت إليها لم تكن معارضة لخبر الشفاعة.

فيحتمل أن يكون المراد بقوله: لا يزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن ولا يسرق السارق حين يسرق وهو مؤمن: إذا فعلا ذلك مستحلّين للزنى والسرقة ومكذبين بتحريمهما. ولا شفاعة لمن زنى مستحلاً لذلك. ويحتمل أن يكون المراد بذلك أنه ليس بمؤمن كالمؤمن الذي لم يكن منه زنى ولا سرقة في البر والطهارة والسلامة من الذنوب.

ويحتمل أن يكون ذلك إنما خرج على مذهب التغليظ والمبالغة في الزجر على سبيل قوله: لا صلاة لجار المسجد إلا في المسجد. وكذلك قوله: من غشنا فليس منا، وليس منا من بات بطيناً وجاره خميصا أيضاً.
If they say: 'Does not the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family) intercede only for a believer according to you? And reports have come that the thief does not steal while he is a believer, and the adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer. So how do the messengers intercede for one who is not a believer? And likewise it is narrated from him that he said: "He is not of us who goes to bed full while his neighbor is hungry." So how is intercession obtained for one who is not of his religion?' It is said to them: These reports are also susceptible to interpretations which, when applied, do not contradict the report of intercession. It is possible that the intended meaning of his statement: 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer, and the thief does not steal while he is a believer' is when they do that considering adultery and theft permissible (mustahillayn) and denying their prohibition. And there is no intercession for one who commits adultery considering it permissible. And it is possible that the intended meaning is that he is not a believer like the believer who has not committed adultery or theft in righteousness, purity, and safety from sins. And it is possible that this came out on the basis of emphasizing and exaggerating deterrence, like his statement: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque.' And likewise his statement: 'Whoever cheats us is not of us,' and 'He is not of us who goes to bed full while his neighbor is hungry.'
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer where the objector cites hadith that seem to deny intercession for non-believers, specifically the hadith about the thief and adulterer not being believers when they sin, and the hadith about not being of the Prophet's community if one is full while neighbor is hungry. The responder offers three possible interpretations (wujūh). First, the hadith refer to those who commit these sins while considering them permissible (mustahillayn) and denying the prohibition; such people have no intercession. Second, the hadith mean that such a person is not a believer in the sense of being at the same level of faith as one who abstains from those sins entirely, in terms of righteousness and purity. Third, these hadith are hyperbolic warnings (taghlīẓ wa mubālagha) intended to deter, similar to the hadith 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque,' which is not absolutely literal. Under any of these interpretations, the hadith do not contradict the established intercession.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
الاستحلال
التغليظ
المبالغة
الوجوه

Correction: Baqillani shows these hadith are open to interpretation and do not absolutely deny intercession.

Checkpoint

A) It means they are not believers at all
B) It is a hyperbolic warning
C) It applies only to unbelievers
D) It is abrogated

Key Takeaway
Hadith that appear to deny intercession are not absolute; they can be interpreted in ways that do not conflict with the established intercession for believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Intercession is for believers who sin, but not for those who take sins lightly. Are you living as if intercession is a safety net that allows you to be careless about obedience? What is one area where you need to repent and take sin more seriously right now?
?
The Prophet's words are sometimes hyperbolic to deter us. What areas of your life do you need to take more seriously, realizing that even hyperbolic warnings carry a real spiritual danger? How will you respond today?

Harmonizing Contradictory Hadiths on Salvation
Baqillani explains harmonization of conflicting reports about entering paradise through faith alone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's principle of 'building and ordering' for resolving apparent contradictions between hadiths about entering paradise.

Core Idea
Contradictory hadiths are not absolute; they are a foundation with conditions built upon it.

Baqillani presents a key hermeneutical rule: when hadiths seem to conflict, they must be interpreted as layered—a foundation with subsequent conditions. In this passage, he uses the famous hadith about the shahada guaranteeing paradise, even for sinners, to illustrate that the declaration of faith is the base, while other texts add requirements. This principle prevents rejection of any authentic text.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Baqillani uses a conditional sentence to introduce his solution.
2
Identify the hadith and the objection
Find the hadith narration and Abu Darda's question. What is the apparent contradiction the hadith raises?
3
Understand the principle of 'building and ordering'
Baqillani says these reports must be carried on 'building and ordering' (البناء والترتيب). What does this mean? Think of it as a foundation that other conditions are added to.
This is the core of the lesson.
4
Consider the Quranic analogy
Baqillani compares this to how we handle Quranic verses that seem outwardly contradictory. How does ordering resolve conflict?
5
Reflect on the misconception
One might think this hadith means deeds are unnecessary. Ask: Does Baqillani say that? What does he actually teach?
The misconception is that the hadith nullifies good deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: «من وإذا حملت هذه الأخبار على هذا التأويل بطل التعارض . وقد روى أبو الدرداء عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم أنه قال : لا إله إلا الله دخل الجنَّة» . قال : فقلت : يا رسول الله ، وإن زنى وإن سرق ؟ وأنه ردّد ذلك عليه حتى قال له في الثانية أو الثالثة: «نعم، وإن رغم أنف أبي الدرداء ! » وإذا كان ذلك كذلك، وجب حمل هذه الأخبار على البناء والترتيب كما يجب ذلك في آي القرآن المتعارضة الظواهر .
He said: "Whoever interprets these reports in this way, the contradiction becomes invalid. And Abu Darda narrated from the Prophet, peace be upon him and his family, that he said: 'There is no god but Allah, (he) enters Paradise.' He said: I said: O Messenger of Allah, even if he committed adultery and even if he stole? And he repeated that to him until he said to him on the second or third time: 'Yes, even if the nose of Abu Darda is rubbed in dust!' And when that is the case, it is necessary to carry these reports on building and ordering, as that is necessary in the verses of the Quran whose outward meanings are contradictory."
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage presents a hermeneutical principle for reconciling apparently contradictory scriptural reports about salvation. The author begins by stating a conditional: if these reports (i.e., the hadiths that seem to promise paradise unconditionally to those who utter the shahada) are interpreted in a particular way, then any apparent contradiction disappears. He then cites a specific, well-known hadith in which Abu Darda reports the Prophet's statement that whoever says 'There is no god but Allah' enters Paradise. When Abu Darda presses the Prophet, asking whether this applies even to one who commits adultery and theft, the Prophet emphatically affirms it, even to the point of humiliating Abu Darda. The author then draws the conclusion that such reports must be understood as 'building and ordering'—that is, they are not absolute but cumulative. The declaration of faith is the foundation; other conditions (like repentance or avoidance of major sins) may be built upon it, but the foundation itself secures entry. The author analogizes this to the way contradictory outward meanings of Quranic verses are resolved through ordering and prioritization. The passage does not yet enter into the specific issue of intercession but establishes a general rule for interpreting such texts.

التعارض
البناء والترتيب
الظواهر المتعارضة

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith 'There is no god but Allah enters Paradise' means that good deeds are unnecessary and all sinners go to paradise unconditionally.
Correction: Baqillani shows that this hadith is the foundation; other conditions (like refraining from major sins or repentance) are built upon it. The declaration of faith is the base, not the entire structure.

Checkpoint

B) It must be interpreted as a foundation that is built upon by other conditions.
C) It applies only to those who never commit major sins.
D) It is a weak hadith that cannot be relied upon.

Key Takeaway
Hadiths about salvation through faith alone must be understood as the foundation, not the complete rule; other conditions build upon it.

Do you truly believe your declaration of faith is a foundation that will hold despite your failures, or have you made it a cover for disobedience? What will you change today?

Intercession Only for the Approved: Baqillani's Interpretation of Q21:28
Baqillani interprets Q21:28 to allow intercession for sinful believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani interprets the Qur'anic verse (21:28) to defend intercession for sinful believers against those who restrict it to perfect believers.

Core Idea
Intercession is about God’s permission, not the sinner’s perfection.

Some have argued that the verse 'they do not intercede except for whom He approves' excludes sinful Muslims from intercession. Baqillani responds by offering two key interpretations: the verse refers to divine permission, and the 'approved' person is one who has some approved deeds (like faith) coexisting with sins. This clarifies that the verse actually only excludes disbelievers, not sinners among believers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the argument's flow.
Notice the objection-and-answer structure.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Find the two meanings Baqillani gives for 'whom He approves'. The first focuses on divine permission; the second on approved deeds coexisting with sins.
Consider why the first interpretation alone might be insufficient.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: How does this argument allow intercession for sinful believers while excluding disbelievers? Trace the logic for the fasiq (wicked person).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا فما معنى قوله: ﴿ ولا يشفعون إلا لمن ارتضى ؟ . قيل لهم : معناه : و لا يشفعون إلا لمن رضي الله سبحانه أن يشفعوا وأذن فيه . ولم يُرد بذلك أنهم لا يشفعون إلا لمن رضي عمله، لأن من رضي الله سائر عمله لا يحتاج إلى الشفاعة. ويحتمل أيضاً أن يكون أراد أنهم لا يشفعون إلا لمن ارتضى عمله الذي هو غير ذنبه الذي يستوجب به العقاب. فكأنه قال : لا يشفعون إلا لمن معه عمل مرتضى . والفاسق معه طاعات وبرّ وقرب وتصديق وتوحيد، وذلك أجمع مرتضى منه . وإنما تدل هذه الآية على أنه لا شفاعة لكافر، لأن الكافر لا طاعة معه .
If they say: Then what is the meaning of His statement: "And they do not intercede except for whom He approves"? It is said to them: Its meaning is: They do not intercede except for whom Allah, exalted, is pleased that they intercede and He permits it. And He did not intend by that that they do not intercede except for whom He approves of his deed, because the one for whom Allah is pleased with all of his deeds does not need intercession. And it is also possible that He intended that they do not intercede except for whom He approves of his deed which is other than his sin that warrants punishment. So as if He said: They do not intercede except for one who has an approved deed. And the wicked person has with him acts of obedience, righteousness, closeness, affirmation, and monotheism, and all of that is approved from him. And this verse only indicates that there is no intercession for a disbeliever, because the disbeliever has no obedience with him.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit addressing the verse 'They do not intercede except for whom He approves' (Q21:28). The objector apparently uses this verse to argue that intercession is only for those whose deeds are pleasing to God, thus excluding sinners. The author gives two interpretations. First, the verse means that intercession occurs only for those whom God permits the intercessors to intercede for—i.e., it is about divine permission, not the merit of the person. The author notes that if it meant those whose deeds are approved, such people would not need intercession, since their deeds already secure them salvation. Second, a possible interpretation: the phrase 'whom He approves' refers to the person's approved deed—namely, their faith and good works—which coexist with their sins. Thus the wicked person (fasiq) still has faith, charity, closeness to God, affirmation, and tawhid, all of which are approved by God. Therefore the verse does not negate intercession for sinful believers; rather, it excludes disbelievers who lack any obedience. The author thus defends the possibility of intercession for Muslims who commit sins.

Key Terms
الشفاعة
الارتضاء
الفاسق
الكافر
الطاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse only allows intercession for sinless believers.
Correction: Baqillani explains it refers to divine permission and the presence of some approved deeds (faith) even in sinful believers.

Checkpoint
What is the primary interpretation Baqillani gives for the verse 'They do not intercede except for whom He approves'?
A) Intercession is only for those whose deeds are completely sinless.
B) Intercession is only for those whom God permits the intercessors to intercede for.
C) Intercession is only for those who have repented of all sins.
D) The verse is abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends intercession for sinful Muslims by interpreting Q21:28 as concerning divine permission and the coexistence of approved deeds (faith) with sins.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

No Intercession for Wrongdoers (Q40:18)
Baqillani explains that 'wrongdoers' in Q40:18 refers to disbelievers, not Muslim sinners.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani interprets 'wrongdoers' in Q40:18 as referring specifically to disbelievers, not to sinful Muslims, and how this defends the possibility of intercession.

Core Idea
The ‘wrongdoers’ in Q40:18 are disbelievers, not Muslim sinners.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses an objection based on a Quranic verse that seems to deny intercession for all wrongdoers. He carefully delimits the term 'wrongdoers' to those whose wrongdoing is disbelief and polytheism, excluding the people of tawhid who commit minor sins. This argument defends the possibility of intercession for Muslim sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the flow of objection and answer come through.
Notice that this is framed as a new 'issue' (mas'ala).
2
Identify the objection and the verse cited
The objector quotes Q40:18. What is the apparent problem this verse poses for intercession?
3
Analyze Baqillani's specification of 'wrongdoers'
Baqillani restricts 'wrongdoers' to those guilty of disbelief and polytheism. Why does he add 'who have no obedience with them'?
He quotes Q31:13 to link 'wrongdoing' to shirk.
4
Examine the supporting proof and analogy
Notice how he uses the verse 'polytheism is a great wrongdoing' and then draws an analogy with the objector's own view on minor sins.
This shows consistency in interpretation.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that the objector has no support from this verse against the Ash'ari position on intercession.
Think about why this conclusion follows logically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة. فإن قالوا : فما معنى قوله عزّ وجلّ : و ما للظالمين من ولي ولا شفيع يطاع ؟ . قيل لهم : معنى ذلك أنه لا شفاعة للظالمين بالكفر والشرك الذين لا طاعة معهم . قال الله تعالى : إن الشرك لظلم عظيم . ولم يرد أهل التوحيد كما أنه لم يرد عندكم أهل الصغائر الواقعة منهم مع مجانبة الكبائر . فلا تعلق لهم في ذلك .
Issue. If they say: Then what is the meaning of His statement, Mighty and Majestic: "And for the wrongdoers there is no protector and no intercessor to be obeyed"? It is said to them: The meaning of that is that there is no intercession for the wrongdoers by disbelief and polytheism, those who have no obedience with them. Allah, exalted, said: "Indeed, polytheism is a great wrongdoing." And He did not intend the people of monotheism, just as He did not intend according to you the people of minor sins that occur from them while avoiding major sins. So they have no support in that.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a second objection-and-answer, framed as a new 'issue' (mas'ala). The objector cites the verse 'And for the wrongdoers there is no protector nor any intercessor to be obeyed' (Q40:18). They imply that this negates intercession for any wrongdoer, including Muslim sinners. The author responds by specifying that 'wrongdoers' here are those who commit wrongdoing through disbelief (kufr) and polytheism (shirk)—those who have no obedience at all. He supports this by quoting Q31:13: 'Indeed, polytheism is a great wrongdoing.' Then he argues that this verse does not refer to the people of monotheism (ahl al-tawhid), just as it does not refer (according to the objector's own school) to those who commit minor sins while avoiding major ones. Therefore, the objector cannot use this verse to deny intercession for sinful Muslims. The author concludes that the objector has no support (talluq) from this verse against the Ash'ari position on intercession.

الكفر
الشرك
الولي
الشفيع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse Q40:18 denies intercession for all wrongdoers, including Muslims who sin.
Correction: Baqillani shows that 'wrongdoers' in the verse are those whose wrongdoing is disbelief and polytheism, not sinful Muslims who maintain tawhid.

Checkpoint
