A) All people who commit any sin.
B) Only those who commit minor sins.
C) Those who commit wrongdoing through disbelief and polytheism.
D) Only those who commit major sins.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani restricts the 'wrongdoers' in Q40:18 to disbelievers, preserving the possibility of intercession for sinful Muslims.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever find yourself judging a fellow Muslim who struggles with sin, secretly believing that their sins make them beyond God's mercy? How does Baqillani's careful interpretation of this verse challenge that attitude? What can you do today to replace judgment with hope for their repentance?
?
When you read verses about punishment and judgment, does your heart feel a sense of despair or fear that God might not accept you? Pause and ask yourself: Do I truly believe that my tawhid—my affirmation of Allah's oneness—keeps me within the scope of His mercy, even when I fall into sin? Commit to memorizing Q31:13 and reminding yourself that shirk is the only unforgivable sin if unrepented.
?
If you were to commit a major sin, would you honestly believe that intercession is possible for you? Or do you, like the objector in this lesson, subconsciously limit God's mercy to only those who never sin? Repent today and sincerely ask Allah to include you among those for whom intercession will be granted.

Who Faces Eternal Punishment? Baqillani's Answer
Baqillani argues that Quranic threats of eternal torment target disbelievers, not Muslims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Baqillani refutes the claim that Quranic verses threatening eternal punishment and denying intercession apply to sinful Muslims, showing they are instead directed at disbelievers.

Core Idea
Eternal punishment verses target disbelievers, not Muslims.

In this passage, Baqillani tackles a strong objection: if the Quran says the punishment never ends and intercession won't help, how can intercession benefit sinful believers? His answer is simple but theologically crucial—those verses describe the fate of those who rejected faith entirely, not Muslims who affirm it. He backs this up by quoting the very words of the disbelievers from the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
The objector cites three verses: one about never-ending despair (Q43:75), one about replacing skins to prolong torment (Q4:56), and one saying intercession is useless (Q74:48). Notice how they frame the challenge.
2
Read Baqillani's answer
Baqillani responds that all such verses are directed at 'the people of disbelief, denial, and rejection.' He then quotes the context of Q74:48—the disbelievers' own admission that they did not pray, feed the poor, and denied the Day of Judgment.
3
Reflect on the principle
The key move: the threat of eternal punishment is conditional on disbelief (kufr), not on sin in general. Verses about eternal torment do not apply to believers who affirm the faith, even if they commit sins.
This is how Baqillani preserves the possibility of intercession for sinful Muslims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة. فإن قالوا فما معنى قوله لا يفتر عنهم وهم فيه مبلسون ، ولا يخفف عنهم من عذابها ، وكلما نضجت جلودهم بدلناهم جلوداً غيرها ليذوقوا العذاب؟ . قيل لهم : جميع هذه الآيات وما كان بمعناها يراد بها أهل الكفر والجحد والتكذيب. وكذلك قوله فما تنفعهم شفاعة الشافعين لأن الله تعالى خبّر عنهم أنهم قالوا : قالوا لم نك من المصلين ولم نك نطعم المسكين وكنا نخوض مع الخائضين وكنا نكذب بيوم الدين . ولم يَعْنِ بهذا الوعيد أحداً من أهل الإسلام والتصديق .
Issue. If they say: Then what is the meaning of His statement: "It is not lightened for them, and they are therein in despair" (Q43:75), and "They will not have relief from the punishment, and every time their skins are roasted, We will replace them with other skins so they may taste the punishment" (Q4:56)? It is said to them: All of these verses and what is like them are intended for the people of disbelief, denial, and rejection. And likewise His statement: "So no intercession of intercessors will benefit them" (Q74:48), because Allah, exalted, informed about them that they said: "They will say, 'We were not of those who prayed, nor did we feed the poor, and we used to engage with those who engaged, and we used to deny the Day of Judgment'" (Q74:43-46). And He did not intend by this threat anyone from the people of Islam and affirmation.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a third objection-and-answer, also introduced as a new issue. The objector brings several Quranic verses that describe eternal punishment and the replacement of skin, as well as the verse 'So no intercession of intercessors will benefit them' (Q74:48). The intention is to argue that intercession is ineffective and punishment is eternal, thus denying intercession for sinful Muslims. The author responds collectively: all these verses and similar ones are directed at the people of disbelief (kufr), denial (juhud), and rejection (takdhib). He supports this by citing the context of Q74:48, where Allah informs about the disbelievers that they themselves will confess: 'We were not of those who prayed, nor did we feed the poor, and we used to engage with those who engage, and we used to deny the Day of Judgment.' Consequently, the threat in these verses does not refer to anyone from the people of Islam and affirmation (tasdiq). Thus, the verses cannot be used to argue against intercession for believers who commit sins.

Misconception: Some might think that Quranic verses threatening eternal punishment (e.g., 'every time their skins are roasted...') apply to all sinners, including Muslims who commit major sins.
Correction: Baqillani shows that these verses are specifically about disbelievers who reject the faith entirely, as evidenced by the disbelievers' own confession in Q74:43-46. Therefore, they do not negate intercession for sinful Muslims.

Baqillani defends intercession for sinful Muslims by restricting Quranic verses of eternal punishment exclusively to disbelievers.

?
Baqillani distinguishes between disbelievers and Muslims in the application of severe Quranic verses. Intercession for Whom? Unpacking the Verse
Baqillani explains the verse denying intercession for disbelievers only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani interprets the Quranic verse 'و ما للظالمين من ولا شفيع يطاع' to deny intercession only for disbelievers, not for sinful believers.

Core Idea
The verse limits intercession to oppressors of disbelief, not sinful monotheists.

This passage addresses a key objection: if the Quran says wrongdoers have no intercessor, how can Muslims hope for intercession? Baqillani clarifies that the verse refers specifically to those who commit shirk, not to monotheists guilty of minor sins. This distinction preserves the possibility of intercession for believing sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the structure: an objection followed by an answer.
The Arabic has an uncertain phrase marked [؟]; we present it as in the source.
2
Identify the objection and the answer
What is the objection being raised? How does Baqillani answer it? Look for the Quranic verse cited and its interpretation.
The objectors are likely using the verse to argue against intercession altogether.
3
Spot the limitation of 'wrongdoers'
Baqillani specifies that 'wrongdoers' in the verse means those who commit disbelief and shirk. Notice how he supports this with another Quranic verse.
The supporting verse is: 'Indeed shirk is a great injustice.'
4
Compare to the case of minor sins
Baqillani argues that just as the objectors do not apply the verse to minor sins, so it does not apply to monotheists. Understand the analogy.
This shows the objectors' inconsistency.
5
Reflect on the doctrinal significance
Why is this interpretation important? How does it defend intercession for Muslim sinners?
This passage defends the Sunni position that intercession benefits even sinful believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : فما معنى قوله عزّ وجلّ : و ما للظالمين من ولا شفيع يطاع ؟ قيل لهم : معنى ذلك أنه لا شفاعة للظالمين بالكفر والشرك الذين لا [؟] قال الله تعالى : إن الشرك لظلم عظيم . ولم يرد معهم . أهل التوحيد كما أنه لم يرد عندكم أهل الصغائر الواقعة منهم مع مجانبة الكبائر . فلا تعلق لهم في ذلك .
Then they said: What is the meaning of His saying, Mighty and Majestic: 'And for the wrongdoers there is no helper nor intercessor to be obeyed'? It was said to them: The meaning of that is that there is no intercession for the wrongdoers by disbelief and shirk, those who [؟] Allah Almighty said: 'Indeed shirk is a great injustice.' And He did not intend thereby the people of tawhid, just as He did not intend according to you the people of minor sins occurring from them while avoiding major sins. So they have no argument in that.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objectors ask about the meaning of the Quranic verse 'و ما للظالمين من ولا شفيع يطاع' (Surah Ghafir 40:18). The answer clarifies that this verse denies intercession specifically for 'wrongdoers' (الظالمين) who are characterized by disbelief (كفر) and shirk (شرك). The answer cites another verse, 'إن الشرك لظلم عظيم' (Surah Luqman 31:13), to establish that shirk is the greatest injustice. Thus, the verse does not apply to the people of tawhid (monotheists), just as it does not apply, in the objectors' own view, to those who commit minor sins while avoiding major sins. The conclusion is that the objectors cannot use this verse to deny intercession for sinful monotheists.

Severe Punishment Verses Apply Only to Disbelievers
Baqillani answers objection about severe punishment verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani insists that Quranic verses about perpetual and severe punishment refer exclusively to disbelievers, not to Muslims who sin.

Core Idea
Perpetual punishment verses target only deniers, not believers.

In this objection-and-answer, Baqillani faces a critical challenge: the Quran contains verses describing an unrelenting, horrific punishment. If these apply to all sinners, even Muslims would be threatened. How does he resolve this? He argues that the context and accompanying descriptions (like confessing to neglecting prayer and charity) prove these warnings are for disbelievers alone. Let's examine his reasoning from the source text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the objection
Read the objection that quotes verses about unrelenting punishment. Notice the specific verses cited: 'لا يفتر عنهم وهم مبلسون' and others.
This objection assumes these verses threaten Muslims who commit major sins.
2
Analyze Baqillani's answer
Baqillani states that all such verses refer to 'أهل الكفر والجحد والتكذيب' – people of disbelief, denial, and rejection. Underline these key terms.
3
See the supporting evidence
He then cites another verse (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:48) and notes the confessions of the punished: they denied prayer, charity, and the Day of Judgment. This proves they were not Muslims.
The confession shows they were not among 'أهل الإسلام والتصديق'.
4
Draw the conclusion
Therefore, the severe punishment verses do not apply to any Muslim who affirms faith. Only disbelievers are intended.
This protects the doctrine that Muslims will eventually be saved from eternal punishment.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is another objection-and-answer. The answer states that all these verses and similar ones refer specifically to the people of disbelief (الكفر), denial (الجحد), and rejection (التكذيب). To confirm this, the answer invokes another verse, 'فما تنفعهم شفاعة الشافعين' (Surah al-Muddaththir 74:48), and notes that Allah informed about these people that they will confess: they were not among those who prayed, did not feed the poor, engaged in falsehood, and denied the Day of Judgment. This description proves these verses cannot refer to Muslims. Therefore, the threat does not apply to any of the people of Islam and affirmation of truth.

Refuting That Intercession Is a Reward from the Intercessors
Baqillani refutes that intercession is a reward from intercessors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that intercession cannot be a reward from the intercessors, based on logical principles and consensus.

Core Idea
Intercession is not a reward from the intercessors but a gift from Allah.

How do we know that the Prophet's intercession is not a reward for believers' deeds? Some might think the verse about angels asking forgiveness proves it is a reward. Baqillani carefully unpacks the verse and applies a logical principle: if intercession were a reward, the intercessors would be the rewarders, but only Allah rewards. This lesson walks through his refutation step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the structure: an objection, a verse citation, and a two-part response.
The passage is a classic objection-and-answer format common in kalam.
2
Understand the objector's claim
The objector argues that intercession is due as a reward (thawab) for believers' deeds, citing the verse where angels ask forgiveness. Why might someone think that?
3
Analyze Baqillani's first response
Baqillani first questions whether the verse actually says the intercession is a reward—it only says the angels ask forgiveness. This is a challenge to the proof.
4
Analyze Baqillani's logical argument
He then argues: if intercession were a reward, the intercessors would be the rewarders, because the doer of an act is attributed with its effect. But consensus says only Allah rewards.
This is a strong logical rebuttal using the principle that the agent of reward is the rewarder.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Baqillani concludes that intercession cannot be a reward from the intercessors. It is a mercy from Allah granted through their supplication. How does this affect your understanding of intercession?
This lesson strengthens the doctrine that Allah alone is the ultimate bestower of reward.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل منهم : ما أنكرتم أن تكون شفاعة الرسول صلّى الله عليه وآله وسلم ، وشفاعة الملائكة مستحقة للمؤمنين على وجه الثواب لهم والجزاء على أعمالهم وطاعاتهم وتوبتهم ؟ لأن الله تعالى أخبر بذلك فقال : الذين يحملون العرش ومن حوله يسبحون بحمد ربهم ويؤمنون به ويستغفرون للذين آمنوا ربنا وسعت كل شيء رحمة وعلماً فاغفر للذين تابوا واتبعوا سبيلك وقهم عذاب الجحيم ربنا وادخلهم جنات عدن التي وعدتهم ومن صلح من آبائهم وأزواجهم وذرياتهم . فأخبر سبحانه أن ذلك على وجه الثواب لهم . يقال لهم : متى أخبر الله سبحانه بذلك ، وليس في الآية أكثر من أن الملائكة يستغفرون لهم فقط؟ ثم يقال لهم : لو كان استغفار الرسول والملائكة وشفاعتهم إلى الله سبحانه ثواباً على أعمالهم والرسول والملائكة هم الفاعلون الخالقون لكلامهم وطلبهم وشفاعتهم عندكم لكانوا هم المثيبين للمؤمنين التائبين بهذه الشفاعة. لأن فاعل الثواب مثيب، كما أن فاعل العقاب معاقب وفاعل الألم والتفضّل مؤلم متفضّل . فلما أجمع المسلمون على أن الأنبياء والملائكة لا يثيبون الطائعين الله على طاعاتهم له سبحانه ، وأن الله هو المثيب .
Then if one of them says: What prevents you from [acknowledging] that the intercession of the Messenger, may Allah bless him and his family and grant them peace, and the intercession of the angels is due to the believers as a reward for them and recompense for their deeds, acts of obedience, and repentance? Because Allah Almighty informed of that when He said: 'Those who bear the Throne and those around it exalt [Allah] with praise of their Lord and believe in Him and ask forgiveness for those who have believed: Our Lord, You have encompassed all things in mercy and knowledge, so forgive those who have repented and followed Your way and protect them from the punishment of Hellfire. Our Lord, and admit them to the Gardens of Eden which You have promised them and those who were righteous among their fathers, their spouses, and their offspring' (Surah Ghafir 40:7-9). So He, exalted, informed that that is as a reward for them. It is said to them: When did Allah, exalted, inform of that? There is nothing in the verse more than that the angels ask forgiveness for them only. Then it is said to them: If the seeking of forgiveness by the Messenger and the angels and their intercession to Allah, exalted, were a reward for their deeds, and the Messenger and the angels, according to you, are the doers, creators of their speech, their request, and their intercession, then they would be the rewarders of the believing repentant ones with this intercession. Because the doer of reward is a rewarder, just as the doer of punishment is a punisher, and the doer of pain and favor is an inflicter of pain and a bestower of favor. Since the Muslims have agreed that the prophets and angels do not reward the obedient ones for their obedience to Allah, exalted, and that Allah is the Rewarder.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer with a logical proof. The objector claims that the intercession of the Prophet and angels is a reward (ثواب) for believers' deeds, citing Quranic verses where angels ask forgiveness for believers. The answer begins by questioning whether the verse actually states that the intercession is a reward; it only says the angels ask forgiveness. Then it presents a logical argument: if intercession were a reward, then the intercessors (prophets and angels) would be the rewarders (مثيب), because the agent of an act is the one attributed with its effect. However, the Muslim consensus (إجماع) is that prophets and angels do not reward the obedient; only Allah rewards. Therefore, intercession cannot be a reward for deeds. The argument follows the principle that the doer of reward is a rewarder, analogous to the doer of punishment being a punisher and the doer of pain being an inflicter of pain.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that intercession is a reward given directly by the Prophet and angels to believers for their deeds.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the verse does not say it is a reward, and the logical principle that the doer of reward is the rewarder, combined with consensus that only Allah rewards, proves that intercession is not a reward from the intercessors.

Checkpoint

A) Intercession is only for major sinners.
B) The intercessors are not the rewarders; only God rewards.
C) The angels' intercession is only for disbelievers.
D) The Prophet's intercession is only for his family.

Key Takeaway
Intercession is not a reward from the intercessors but a gift from Allah granted through their supplication.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform good deeds, do you ever feel you have 'earned' a reward from Allah, forgetting that even the intercession of the Prophet ﷺ is not a reward but a gift? Does your heart expect Allah to owe you something, or do you realize all mercy is from His grace alone? Will you reflect on this before your next prayer?
?
Have you ever relied on a righteous person or a saint to intercede for you, thinking their status guarantees Allah's response? This lesson shows that even prophets and angels are not rewarders—they only ask. Where is your true trust: in the means or in the One who grants? Will you repent from any misplaced dependence and turn solely to Allah?
?
The argument in this lesson uses logic and consensus to uphold Allah's exclusive right to reward. Do you ever find yourself attributing good outcomes to your own efforts or to others, subtly denying that the ultimate rewarder is Allah alone? Examine your thoughts after a success: do you thank Allah wholeheartedly, or do you subconsciously credit yourself or someone else? Name one specific area where you need to realign your gratitude.

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Denial of Intercession for Sinners
Refutes the Mu'tazilite denial of intercession through logical argument and Quranic reinterpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni response to the Mu'tazilite claim that intercession cannot be for forgiveness of sins, including the reinterpretation of Quranic verses and the logical flaws in their position.

Core Idea
Intercession for sinners is not disproven by the Quran; the verse on repentance refers to repentance from unbelief.

Imam al-Baqillani engages a key Mu'tazilite objection: that intercession cannot be for forgiveness because the Quran restricts forgiveness to those who repent. He first concedes their premise but shows it does not preclude forgiveness, then offers an alternative interpretation of the verse, and finally exposes the absurd consequences of their view. This lesson unpacks his layered argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concession
Note how the author accepts the Mu'tazilite premise that intercession is merited by faith, then argues this does not prevent it from being for forgiveness of sins.
This is a standard dialectical move in kalam: accepting the opponent's premise to show it does not support their conclusion.
2
Examine the verse objection
Identify the Mu'tazilite proof text: the Quranic verse 'Forgive those who repent and follow Your way.' They use it to bar the persistent sinner from intercession.
The Mu'tazilites argued that only repentant sinners can be forgiven, so intercession for the unrepentant is impossible.
3
Follow the alternative interpretation
See how the author reinterprets 'those who repent' as referring to repentance from unbelief and criticism of the prophets, not from minor sins of believers.
This interpretation harmonizes the verse with the possibility of intercession for sinful believers.
4
Analyze the reductio and contrast of principles
Observe the argument that if intercession were only for the sinless, it would imply God could be unjust—beneath prophets and angels. Then note the contrast between Sunni (repentance as divine favor) and Mu'tazilite (repentance as obligatory) views.
The Mu'tazilite view forces them to consider God unjust if He does not accept repentance, which contradicts their own principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : لو سلمنا لكم أن الشفاعة مستحقة بالإيمان ، لم يدل ذلك على أنها ليست بشفاعة في غفران الذنوب. لأن الإيمان بالله سبحانه والتوبة من الكفر يُستحق به الثواب عندكم . فيجوز أيضاً أن يُستحق به شفاعة النبي صلّى الله عليه وآله وسلم في ذنوبهم التي قارنت الإيمان . فما الذي يدفع ذلك ؟
فإن قالوا : لأنه أخبر عنهم أنهم يقولون : فاغفر للذين تابوا واتبعوا سبيلك والمصر ليس بتائب .
قيل لهم : ما أنكرتم أن يكون أراد بقوله : للذين تابوا من كفرهم وطعنهم على النبيين ودين المسلمين واتبعوا سبيله سبحانه واعتقدوا توحيده وتصديق رسله والإقرار بما جاء من عنده ؟ فهل تجدون لهذا مدفعاً؟
ولو كانت الملائكة لا تشفع إلا لمؤمن تقي تائب مقلع متنسك لا سبيل ولا حجة عليه، لم يكن لشفاعتها معنى إلا الرغبة إلى الله عزّ وجلّ في أن لا يظلمه ولا يجوز عليه ولا يسفه بعقابه، لأن عقاب من هذه سبيله ظلم وسفه على أصولهم. والأنبياء والملائكة أجلّ عند الله عزّ وجلّ وأعظم قدراً من أن ترغب إليه في أن لا يظلم عباده ولا يجور في حكمه . ويمكن أيضاً على أصولنا أن يكون معنى قوله: ﴿ فاغفر للذين تابوا ﴾ أي : تفضّل عليهم بقبول توبتهم فاغفر لهم . لأن قبول التوبة تفضل الله له أن يفعله وله أن لا يفعله وهذا التأويل غير مطرد على أصول المعتزلة، لأنها توجب قبول التوبة على الله وتُظلمه وتُجوِّره في ردّها وترك قبولها والعقاب على ما هي توبة منه . فلا يسوغ لهم مع ذلك مثل تأويلنا .
Then it is said to them: If we concede to you that intercession is merited by faith, that does not indicate that it is not intercession for the forgiveness of sins. Because faith in God Almighty and repentance from unbelief merit reward according to you. So it is also permissible that the intercession of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family) be merited for their sins which accompanied faith. So what repels that? If they say: Because He informed about them that they say: 'Forgive those who repent and follow Your way,' and the persistent sinner is not a repenter. It is said to them: What prevents you from understanding His saying: 'for those who repent' as those who repented from their unbelief and their criticism of the prophets and the religion of Muslims and followed His way and believed in His oneness and affirmed His messengers and acknowledged what came from Him? Do you find any objection to this? And if the angels did not intercede except for a believing, pious, repentant, desisting, devout person who has no sin or proof against him, then their intercession would have no meaning except supplication to God Almighty that He not wrong him or treat him unjustly or foolishly punish him, because punishing someone with such attributes would be injustice and foolishness according to their principles. And the prophets and angels are more exalted and greater in status with God Almighty than to ask Him not to wrong His servants or be unjust in His judgment. And it is also possible according to our principles that the meaning of His saying: 'Forgive those who repent' is: Bestow favor upon them by accepting their repentance, so forgive them. Because the acceptance of repentance is a favor of God; He may do it or not do it. And this interpretation is not consistent with the principles of the Mu'tazila, because they make the acceptance of repentance obligatory upon God and consider Him unjust and oppressive if He rejects it and does not accept it and punishes for that from which one repents. So they are not permitted, given that, an interpretation like ours.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a detailed refutation of the Mu'tazilite position that intercession cannot be for the forgiveness of sins. The author first establishes that if the Mu'tazila concede that faith merits intercession, this does not preclude it being for forgiveness of sins. He then addresses their objection based on the Quranic verse that restricts forgiveness to those who repent. He offers an alternative interpretation: the verse refers to repentance from unbelief, not from minor sins committed by believers. He further argues that if intercession were only for the sinless, it would be redundant and would imply that God might be unjust—which is beneath the dignity of prophets and angels. Finally, he contrasts the Sunni view that God accepts repentance as a favor with the Mu'tazilite view that He is obliged to accept it, showing that their own principles prevent them from adopting his interpretation.

Key Terms
شفاعة
إيمان
توبة
غفران الذنوب
معتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quranic verse 'Forgive those who repent' clearly excludes persistent sinners from intercession.
Correction: The verse can be interpreted as referring to repentance from unbelief, not from minor sins, so it does not exclude intercession for sinful believers.

Checkpoint
What is the author's alternative interpretation of the verse 'Forgive those who repent' in response to the Mu'tazilite objection?
A) It refers to repentance from minor sins.
B) It refers to repentance from unbelief and following the prophets.
C) It refers to repentance from hypocrisy.
D) It refers to repentance from major sins only.

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazilite objection to intercession for sinners is refuted by reinterpreting the Quranic verse and exposing logical inconsistencies in their own principles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you genuinely believe that God's mercy through the Prophet's intercession can cover your sins, or do you secretly rely on your own deeds to earn His forgiveness? If intercession is a gift, not a wage, does that humble you or make you anxious?
?
When you read this passage, do you realize that the Mu'tazilite fear of God being unjust if He forgives without repentance reflects a deeper doubt in God's mercy? Have you ever felt that God 'owes' you something—or do you truly accept that His acceptance of repentance is a favor, not a right?
?
The author says the prophets are too exalted to ask God not to be unjust. Does your own prayer life reflect a similar reverence, or do you sometimes pray as if you need to remind God to be fair? What would it mean for you to pray with the confidence that God's justice and mercy are perfect, and that intercession is not a correction of God but a channel of His grace?

Refuting the Mu'tazilite Limited View of Intercession
Refutes the Mu'tazilite view that intercession is for the repentant and sinless

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why intercession for those who are already sinless or repentant is meaningless according to Imam Baqillani's argument.

Core Idea
Intercession that asks God not to be unjust is meaningless because God is never unjust.

Imam Baqillani continues his refutation of the Mu'tazilite positions on intercession. Here he addresses a specific group who claimed intercession is only for the repentant and the sinless. He shows that such intercession would imply asking God to avoid injustice, which is a nonsensical request given God's perfect justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the concise refutation style.
2
Identify the two groups being interceded for
The passage refers to 'the first two groups'. From context, these are minor sinners and repentant major sinners. Understand why the Mu'tazilites thought intercession applies to them.
3
Analyze the logical argument
The author argues that intercession for these groups would be asking God not to be unjust. Ask yourself: Is it possible for God to be unjust? Why would such an intercession be meaningless?
This connects to the core idea that God is never unjust.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقال لهم : أما الشفاعة للفريقين الأولين، فلا معنى لها. لأنها شفاعة إلى الله في أن لا يظلم ولا يجور على عباده بعقاب غير مستحق
So it is said to them: As for intercession for the first two groups, it has no meaning. Because it is intercession to God that He not wrong nor be unjust to His servants with undeserved punishment.
Source pages p. 431

Commentary
This passage is a concise refutation of the second Mu'tazilite faction's view on intercession. The author argues that intercession for the first two groups (minor sinners and repentant major sinners) is meaningless because it essentially asks God not to be unjust. Since God is never unjust, such a request is superfluous and implies a misunderstanding of God's attributes. The author thus dismisses the Mu'tazilite position as illogical.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that intercession for those who have no sins or have repented is meaningful and beneficial.
Correction: Imam Baqillani shows that such intercession is meaningless because it would imply asking God to avoid being unjust, which He never is.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Intercession for those who are already sinless or have repented is meaningless because it would imply asking God to avoid injustice, which He never commits.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Refuting Intercession for Increased Reward
Baqillani refutes intercession for increased reward using Qur'an and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani rejects intercession for increase in reward for sinless believers as unscriptural.

Core Idea
Intercession in revelation is for forgiveness, not for increasing reward.

Baqillani now turns to a third alleged type of intercession: that which would increase the reward of sinless believers. He argues that this concept is completely absent from both the Qur'an and the prophetic traditions. Instead, the only intercession attested in revelation is intercession for forgiveness. This lesson examines his scriptural argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice how Baqillani structures his refutation.
2
Identify the scriptural sources
Find where Baqillani cites the Qur'an and hadith. How does he use them to support his argument?
He uses both the absence of evidence and the specific content of angelic intercession in the Qur'an.
3
Reflect on the rhetorical conclusion
Consider the final sentence: what does Baqillani attribute the Mu'tazila's error to? Why is this significant?
He accuses them of obstinacy and following devilish whispers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما الشفاعة للسالم من كل الذنوب في أن يزاد على قدر ما يستحقه، فإنها خلاف الشفاعة المروية عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم، ولأن ذلك لم يذكر في شيء من الأخبار. وكذلك مخالفة هي للقرآن، لأن الشفاعة التي ذكرها الله سبحانه عن الملائكة إنما هي شفاعة في الغفران للذين تابوا من الكفر والظلم لأن يقيهم السيئات، وليس فيها ذكر الزيادة في النعيم. ولولا العناد والميل إلى سبيل الضالين ووساوس المردة والشياطين، لم يعدلوا عن إثبات الشفاعة المذكورة في نص الكتاب والمأثور في الأخبار إلى الترهات وطريق التأويلات وتلفيق الجهل والضلالات.
As for intercession for the one free from all sins for increase beyond what he deserves, it is contrary to the intercession reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family), and because that is not mentioned in any of the reports. Likewise, it is contrary to the Qur'an, because the intercession that Allah the Exalted mentioned from the angels is only intercession for forgiveness for those who repented from disbelief and wrongdoing so that He protects them from evil deeds, and there is no mention of increase in bliss. Were it not for obstinacy and inclination to the path of the misguided and the whisperings of the devils and demons, they would not have turned away from affirming the intercession mentioned in the text of the Book and transmitted in the reports to nonsense and the way of interpretations and the patching together of ignorance and misguidance.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage refutes the third category: intercession for sinless believers to increase their reward. Baqillani argues that this concept is alien to the Qur'an and Sunnah. The intercession mentioned in the Qur'an is for forgiveness, not for increase. By rejecting the established intercession and inventing a new type, the Mu'tazila are led by obstinacy and devilish whispers.

Misconception: That intercession can increase reward for sinless believers beyond what they deserve.
Correction: The Qur'an and hadith only mention intercession for forgiveness, not for increase in reward.

The only intercession attested in revelation is for forgiveness, not for increasing reward.

The True Meaning of Intercession
Baqillani argues that intercession is for forgiveness, not for increase of reward.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that intercession (shafa'ah) is specifically for forgiveness of sins, not for increasing reward, and how he refutes opposing views.

Core Idea
Intercession is for forgiveness, not for extra reward.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani tackles a key theological dispute about intercession. He begins by showing that, based on the opponents' own principles, intercession would be meaningless if it were for those who already avoid punishment. Then he clarifies that the Quranic and prophetic intercession is solely for forgiveness, and he challenges opponents to either accept this or face logical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal English translation. Let the flow of Baqillani's argument come through before analyzing it.
Notice the polemical tone and direct address to opponents.
2
Identify the two types of intercession
Baqillani distinguishes between intercession for increase of reward and intercession for forgiveness. Find where he makes this distinction and see how he rejects the former.
The Quranic intercession is for forgiveness after repentance.
3
Understand the refutation strategy
Baqillani presents a dilemma to opponents: they must either deny intercession altogether (rejecting Quran and hadith) or affirm it but interpret it away, which he claims has already been refuted.
This is a classic kalam technique of forcing a contradiction.
4
Reflect on the broader implications
Consider why this definition of intercession matters in Sunni soteriology. It preserves both divine justice and mercy without implying undeserved rewards.
Intercession reaffirms the need for repentance and God's forgiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لأن صاحب الصغيرة غير مستحق للعذاب إذا فعلها مع مجانبة الكبائر عندكم وعلى أصولكم. وكذلك التائب من الكبيرة قد أزال عن نفسه العقاب بتوبته وصار عقابه عليها مع التوبة ظلماً قبيحاً. فلا معنى للشفاعة فيمن هذه حاله. فأما الشفاعة للسالم من كل الذنوب في أن يزاد على قدر ما يستحقه، فإنها خلاف الشفاعة المروية عن النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم، ولأن ذلك لم يذكر في شيء من الأخبار. وكذلك مخالفة هي للقرآن، لأن الشفاعة التي ذكرها الله سبحانه عن الملائكة إنما هي شفاعة في الغفران للذين تابوا من الكفر والظلم لأن يقيهم السيئات، وليس فيها ذكر الزيادة في النعيم. ولولا العناد والميل إلى سبيل الضالين ووساوس المردة والشياطين، لم يعدلوا عن إثبات الشفاعة المذكورة في نص الكتاب والمأثور في الأخبار إلى الترهات وطريق التأويلات وتلفيق الجهل والضلالات. ويقال لهم: ليس الكلام بين الأمة في الزيادة على قدر الثواب وإنما الكلام في الشفاعة التي جاءت بها الأخبار والقرآن فهل لها عندكم معنى أم لا؟ فإن قالوا: لا صاروا إلى جحد القرآن والروايات، وسألناهم على حد ما تقدم. وإن أثبتوها وتأولوها على بعض ما تقدم كلمناهم بما سلف، ولا جواب لهم عن شيء منه.
Because the doer of a minor sin is not deserving of punishment when he commits it while avoiding major sins according to you and your principles. Likewise, the one who repents from a major sin has removed punishment from himself by his repentance, and his punishment for it along with repentance would be ugly injustice. So there is no meaning for intercession for one whose state is this. As for intercession for the one free from all sins that he be increased beyond what he deserves, it is contrary to the intercession related from the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family), and because that is not mentioned in any of the traditions. And likewise it is contrary to the Qur'an, because the intercession that Allah Almighty mentioned concerning the angels is only intercession for forgiveness for those who repented from disbelief and wrongdoing, that He protect them from evil deeds, and there is no mention in it of increase in bliss. Were it not for stubbornness and inclination to the way of the misguided and the whisperings of the rebellious and the devils, they would not have turned away from affirming the intercession mentioned in the text of the Book and reported in the traditions to nonsense and the path of allegorical interpretations and the piecing together of ignorance and misguidance. And it is said to them: The discussion among the community is not about increase over the measure of reward; rather the discussion is about the intercession that the traditions and the Qur'an have brought. So does it have a meaning for you or not? If they say: No, they would come to denial of the Qur'an and the narrations, and we would question them in the manner that preceded. And if they affirm it and interpret it in some of the ways that preceded, we have spoken to them with what has passed, and they have no answer to any of it.
Source pages p. 432

Commentary
This passage is a polemical argument against opponents (likely Mu'tazila) regarding the nature of intercession (shafa'ah). The author begins by stating that according to the opponents' own principles, the doer of minor sins is not punishable if he avoids major sins, and the repentant from major sins has removed punishment. Therefore, intercession for such persons would be meaningless. Then he distinguishes between two types of intercession: one for the sinless to increase reward, which is not the intercession reported from the Prophet (peace be upon him) or in the Quran. The Quranic intercession mentioned for angels is for forgiveness of those who repented from disbelief and wrongdoing, not for increase in blessings. The author accuses opponents of stubbornness and following misguided ways. Then he addresses them directly: the issue is not increase of reward but the intercession mentioned in Quran and hadith. If they deny it, they reject Quran and hadith; if they affirm it but interpret it away, they have been refuted. The passage ends by asserting that opponents have no answer.

Key Terms
شفاعة (shafa'ah)
صغيرة (minor sin)
كبيرة (major sin)
توبة (repentance)
غفران (forgiveness)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession can be for increasing the reward of sinless believers beyond what they deserve.
Correction: Baqillani argues that Quranic intercession is exclusively for forgiveness of sins after repentance, and there is no mention of increase in reward.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the nature of the intercession mentioned in the Quran concerning the angels?
A) Intercession for increase of reward for the sinless.
B) Intercession for forgiveness for those who repented from disbelief and wrongdoing.
C) Intercession for all believers regardless of sins.
D) Intercession for the Prophet to raise his rank.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani establishes that the only intercession affirmed by Quran and Sunnah is for forgiveness of sins, not for increasing reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you sometimes postpone repentance, secretly hoping that the Prophet's intercession will cover you on the Day of Judgment? After reading Baqillani's argument that intercession is for those who repent from disbelief and wrongdoing, how does this challenge your assumption? Will you change your reliance on intercession to a more urgent call to immediate repentance?
?
Baqillani warns against stubbornness and interpreting texts to suit one's desires. Is there any Islamic concept you have reinterpreted in a way that makes you comfortable with a sin or a shortcoming? What would it cost you to accept the clear meaning and let it transform your actions?
?
Consider the notion that intercession could increase your reward without extra effort. If Baqillani says this is contrary to the Quran and Sunnah, how does that affect your motivation to seek good deeds? Are you more driven by the desire for reward or by love that prompts action? How will this lesson change your daily practice?

Attaining Intercession Through Obedience, Not Sin
Baqillani answers a question about what action fulfills an oath to attain the Prophet's intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Baqillani refutes the opponents' question about an oath to attain intercession by clarifying that intercession is attained through obedience and faith, not sin.

Core Idea
Intercession is earned through righteousness and faith, not through sin.

Imam al-Baqillani addresses a question from opponents who ask what action fulfills an oath to attain the Prophet's intercession, implying that sin might be required. He refutes this by affirming that the path to intercession is obedience to Allah and steadfast faith. This passage clarifies the true basis of intercession and nullifies the opponents' objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to understand the question and answer.
Notice how the opponents try to force a dilemma.
2
Identify Baqillani's direct answer
Find the part where he says 'بل نأمره أن يطيع الله' and understand why this nullifies the question.
3
Examine the analogy of Zayd
Consider the analogy comparing intercession in the Hereafter to intercession among people, focusing on the basis of friendship and kindness.
This helps clarify that intercession is not based on sin.
4
Summarize the key points
Write a brief summary of why the opponents' question fails and what the correct path to intercession is.
Reflect on how this corrects the misconception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة لهم في هذا الباب. فإن قالوا: خبرونا عمن حلف بالطلاق أنه يعمل عملاً ينال به شفاعة الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم - ما الذي يجب عليه أن يعمل؟ أتأمرونه بعمل المعاصي، أو بماذا تأمرونه؟ يقال لهم: لا، بل نأمره أن يطيع الله سبحانه حتى ينال شفاعة الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم، في الزيادة على قدر عمله على ما ارتضيتموه في أقسام الشفاعة. وفي ذلك سقوط سؤالكم. وكذلك الجواب إن قالوا: حلف أن يعمل عملاً يصير به من أهل الشفاعة. ثم يقال لهم: الذي يجب عندنا على هذا الإنسان أن يستديم الإيمان ويتمسك بفعل الخير والطاعات، لأنه بذلك عندنا ينال الشفاعة دون ذنوبه. لأنه لو أذنب ولم يتب مع ذلك ويؤمن، لم ينل الشفاعة. فالذي تثبت له الشفاعة برّه، وإيمانه، كما أن الذي به تثبت لزيد شفاعة هو صداقته وسالف الجميل منه، وليس هو نفس الذنب والجناية عليه. وهذا معلوم بما يغني عن الحجاج والإكثار.
A question from them in this chapter: For if they say: Inform us concerning one who swears by divorce that he will do an action by which he will attain the intercession of the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family) — what must he do? Do you command him to commit acts of disobedience, or what do you command him? It is said to them: No, rather we command him to obey Allah Almighty until he attains the intercession of the Messenger (peace be upon him and his family) in increase over the measure of his deed according to what you have approved in the divisions of intercession. And in that lies the fall of your question. And likewise the answer if they say: He swore that he would do an action by which he would become among the people of intercession. Then it is said to them: What is incumbent upon us for this person is that he continually maintain faith and hold fast to doing good and acts of obedience, because by that, according to us, he attains intercession without his sins. Because if he committed sins and did not repent along with that and maintain faith, he would not attain intercession. So that by which intercession is established for him is his righteousness and his faith, just as that by which intercession is established for Zayd is his friendship and previous kindness from him, and it is not the sin itself and the offense against him. And this is known without need for argument and abundance.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage presents a specific question from opponents and its answer. The opponents ask about a person who swears by divorce that he will perform an action to gain the Prophet's intercession: should he be commanded to commit sins or what? The author's answer is that he must obey Allah to attain intercession, specifically in the sense of increase of reward (according to the opponents' own classification). The answer nullifies the question. Then the author adds that if the oath is to become among the people of intercession, the person must maintain faith and good deeds, because intercession is attained through righteousness and faith, not through sin. He gives an analogy: just as intercession for Zayd is based on friendship and past kindness, not on the offense itself. So the intercession is tied to the person's virtue, not his sin. This refutes the opponents' implied notion that intercession might be attained through sin.

Key Terms
حلف بالطلاق (oath of divorce)
طاعة (obedience)
إيمان (faith)
برّ (righteousness)
صداقة (friendship)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can attain the Prophet's intercession by committing sins or through a specific oath-triggered action that might be sinful.
Correction: Intercession is attained through obedience to Allah, maintaining faith, and performing good deeds, not through sin or mere oath.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, how does a person attain the Prophet's intercession?
A) By committing sins to show humility.
B) By obeying Allah and maintaining faith.
C) By swearing an oath to do something.
D) By avoiding all good deeds.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's intercession is attained through obedience and faith, not through sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you fall into sin, do you secretly hope that the Prophet's intercession will cover you without requiring you to change? How does Baqillani's argument challenge that hope?
?
If you were the one who swore by divorce to do an action that attains intercession, would your immediate thought be to commit a sin or to obey? What does your answer reveal about your heart's reliance?
?
The analogy of Zayd's friendship shows intercession based on prior kindness, not offense. In your relationship with the Prophet, have you built that 'kindness' through obedience, or are you relying on the offense itself? What will you do today to change that?

Answering an Objection on Oaths for Intercession
Baquillani answers an objection about oaths for intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baquillani refutes the claim that intercession might be sought through sin.

Core Idea
Intercession is attained through obedience, not transgression.

In this passage, Baquillani addresses a hypothetical objection: if someone swears by divorce to perform an act that gains the Prophet’s intercession, would that act be sinful? The response clarifies that intercession is reserved for the obedient, so the commanded action is always obedience to Allah.

Guided Path
1
Set the scene
Understand the objection about swearing by divorce to attain intercession. The objectors suggest that if intercession is earned by deeds, one might be commanded to sin.
This is a common tactic: pushing a theological position to an absurd conclusion.
2
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the direct style of objection and response.
The phrase 'في ذلك سقوط سؤالكم' indicates the refutation is decisive.
3
Analyze Baquillani's response
Identify how Baquillani turns the argument: he insists on obedience, and notes that intercession increases according to deeds, not that sin earns it.
The response also covers a variant where one swears to become from 'ahl al-shafa'ah'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة لهم في هذا الباب
فإن قالوا : خبرونا عمّن حلف بالطلاق أنه يعمل عملاً ينال به شفاعة الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم - ما الذي يجب عليه أن يعمل ؟ أتأمرونه بعمل المعاصي، أو بماذا تأمرونه؟
يقال لهم : لا، بل نأمره أن يطيع الله سبحانه حتى ينال شفاعة الرسول صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم، في الزيادة على قدر عمله على ما ارتضيتموه في أقسام الشفاعة. وفي ذلك سقوط سؤالكم. وكذلك الجواب إن قالوا : حلف أن يعمل عملاً يصير به من أهل الشفاعة.
A question for them in this chapter: If they say: Inform us about one who swore by divorce that he will do an action by which he attains the intercession of the Messenger (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) – what is obligatory upon him to do? Do you command him to commit sins, or what do you command him? It is said to them: No, rather we command him to obey Allah, may He be exalted, until he attains the intercession of the Messenger (may Allah bless him and grant him peace), in the increase beyond his deed according to what you have accepted in the categories of intercession. And in that is the failure of your question. And likewise is the answer if they say: He swore that he will do an action by which he becomes from the people of intercession.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and answer. The objectors argue that if intercession is earned by deeds, then a person who swears by divorce to do an action for intercession might be commanded to sin if that is how it is attained. The response clarifies that we command obedience to Allah, as intercession is for the obedient. The answer also applies to a variant where one swears to become among the people of intercession, affirming that it is through obedience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That intercession can be earned by committing sins.
Correction: Baquillani clarifies that intercession is attained through obedience to Allah, not through sin. Any oath to seek intercession must be fulfilled by good deeds.

Checkpoint
According to Baquillani's response, how does a person attain the Prophet's intercession?
A) By committing sins
B) By obeying Allah and increasing in good deeds
C) By swearing an oath by divorce
D) By merely believing without actions

Key Takeaway
Intercession is for the obedient; any oath to seek it must be fulfilled through obedience to Allah, not sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Intercession Requires Persistence in Faith
Baqillani explains the condition for intercession and refutes a misconception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that, according to Baqillani, intercession is attained through persistent faith and good deeds, not through sins without repentance.

Core Idea
Intercession is earned by persistence in faith and righteousness, not by sins.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a key objection about intercession. He clarifies that intercession is not a blanket pardon for sins; rather, it is granted to those who maintain faith and perform good deeds. He uses a clear analogy to illustrate that intercession is based on virtue, not on the offense itself. This lesson will walk through his argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if he sinned and did not repent... he would not attain intercession.'
2
Identify the condition for intercession
Baqillani states that a person must persist in faith and adhere to good deeds. Find where he lists these requirements.
The phrase 'يستديم الإيمان ويتمسّك بفعل الخير والطاعات' is key.
3
Understand the analogy
He compares intercession to a friend's intercession based on friendship and past kindness, not on the sin committed against him. Explain this analogy in your own words.
The analogy reinforces that intercession is merited by goodness, not evil.
4
Reflect on the misunderstanding
Consider the common misconception that intercession applies even if one persists in sin. Baqillani explicitly denies this.
This guards against the false hope of intercession without repentance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : الذي يجب عندنا على هذا الإنسان أن يستديم الإيمان ويتمسّك بفعل الخير والطاعات، لأنه بذلك عندنا ينال الشفاعة دون ذنوبه. لأنه لو أذنب ولم يتب مع ذلك ويؤمن ، لم ينل الشفاعة. فالذي تثبت له الشفاعة برّه ،وإيمانه، كما أن الذي به تثبت لزيد شفاعة هو صداقته وسالف الجميل منه، وليس هو نفس الذنب والجناية عليه. وهذا معلوم بما يغني عن الحجاج والإكثار.
Then it is said to them: What is obligatory in our view upon this person is that he persist in faith and adhere to doing good and acts of obedience, because by that in our view he attains intercession without his sins. For if he sinned and did not repent along with that and believe, he would not attain intercession. So the one for whom intercession is established is his righteousness and his faith, just as that by which intercession is established for Zayd is his friendship and past kindness, and it is not the sin and offense against him. And this is known by what suffices from argument and excess.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on intercession. Baquillani states that the person must maintain faith and good deeds, as intercession is not for sins without repentance. He uses an analogy: just as a friend's intercession for another is based on friendship and past kindness, not on the sin of the friend, similarly intercession from the Prophet is based on one's own righteousness and faith, not on sins. This is considered obvious and needs no lengthy proof.

C) Commission of sins and then repentance

Key Takeaway
Intercession is not a license for sin; it requires persistent faith and righteous actions.

Distinguishing Attaining from Deserving Intercession
Baquillani distinguishes two meanings of 'deserving' intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that 'deserving' intercession can only mean attaining it through obedience, not claiming a right upon Allah or His messenger.

Core Idea
Intercession is a gift, not a right — no deed obligates Allah.

Baquillani addresses a subtle but critical theological confusion: what does it mean to 'deserve' the Prophet's intercession? Many might think that good deeds create a binding claim. In this passage, he clarifies that intercession is granted by Allah's grace, not earned as a right. Let's examine his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then its literal English translation. Pay attention to the two meanings of 'deserving' (istihqaq) mentioned.
2
Identify the two definitions
Baquillani presents two interpretations of 'deserving' intercession. Find them: one is attainment, the other is entitlement upon Allah or His messenger.
3
Understand the consequence for oaths
Notice that if someone swears to do what deserves intercession, the validity of their oath depends on which meaning they intend. The first is possible, the second is impossible.
This shows the practical importance of the distinction.
4
Reflect on the theological principle
Ask yourself: why can no action create a binding right on Allah? Baquillani states it is because proof has established that intercession cannot be deserved as a right upon Allah or His messenger.
This guards against any notion of obligating the Creator by created deeds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
وإن سألوا عمّن حلف أنه يفعل ما يستحق أو يستوجب به شفاعة النبي صلّى الله عليه وآله وسلّم فإنه إن عنى بالاستحقاق والاستيجاب النيل لها والكون من أهلها، أمرناه بما سلف طاعة الله عزّ وجلّ وإن عنى به الاستحقاق على الله أو على رسوله واعتقد ذلك، فلا مخرج عن يمينه لقيام الدلالة على أنه لا يجوز أن يستحق على الله ولا على رسوله وملائكته الشفاعة بشيء من الأعمال.
Question: And if they ask about one who swore that he will do what merits or entails by it the intercession of the Prophet (may Allah bless him and grant him peace): if he means by merit and entailing the attainment of it and being among its people, we command him with what has preceded: obedience to Allah Almighty. And if he means by it the entitlement upon Allah or upon His Messenger and he believes that, then there is no way out of his oath due to the establishment of the proof that it is not permissible to deserve intercession upon Allah or upon His Messenger or His angels by any of the deeds.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage addresses an ambiguity in the word 'deserving' (istihqaq) concerning intercession. Baquillani clarifies that if one means simply attaining intercession and being among its recipients, then it is through obedience as before. But if one means a right or claim upon Allah or His messenger, that is impossible because no action can create an obligation upon Allah or His messenger to grant intercession. The oath in the latter case is impossible to fulfill, so the swearer remains obligated.

Key Terms
استحقاق
استيجاب
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One can deserve intercession as a binding right upon Allah or His messenger.
Correction: Baquillani shows that this is impossible; intercession is attained through obedience but never as an entitlement.

Checkpoint
According to Baquillani, what does it mean to 'deserve' intercession in a way that is impossible?
A) Attaining it through obedience
B) Having a rightful claim upon Allah or His messenger
C) Being among the people of intercession
D) Doing a deed that leads to intercession

Key Takeaway
Intercession is a gift from Allah, not a right earned by deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform acts of worship, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'I have done enough to earn Allah's favor'? How does this lesson’s claim that no deed obligates Allah challenge that internal ledger of rights and rewards?
?
Is there an area of your life—your prayers, charity, or even your relationships—where you subtly demand something from Allah in return? What would it cost you to release that demand and trust intercession as pure gift?
?

Oath for an Action that May Intercede Against Punishment
Baqillani rules on an oath for intercession against punishment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's ruling that one is never commanded to sin in fulfillment of an oath, and that the oath is void if sin occurs.

Core Idea
Oaths do not justify sin; sin voids the oath.

This passage presents a nuanced question about oaths and sin. The opponent assumes that an oath might require a sinful act to gain intercession. Baqillani responds by affirming the absolute prohibition of sin and explaining that the oath becomes void if sin is committed. This reinforces the principle that no obligation can override Allah's commands.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to get the full context of the question and answer.
2
Identify the opponent's assumption
Notice that the opponent suggests the oath might mandate a sinful act for intercession.
3
Analyze Baqillani's response
He rejects commanding sin and explains that sin makes the oath void, using the analogy of minor sins.
This aligns with the principle that sin cannot be commanded.
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider how this ruling prevents using oaths as excuses for disobedience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
وإن قالوا : فما تقولون فيمن حلف أن يفعل فعلاً يجوز أن يشفع له فيما استحق عليه من العقاب؟
قيل لهم : هذا لا نأمره بشيء من معاصي الله تعالى. فإن ابتلي بشيء من ذلك، فقد زال عنه حكم اليمين كما أنكم لا تأمرونه بفعل الصغير من الذنوب، فإن ابتلي بشيء من ذلك ، زال عنه حكم اليمين.

Commentary
This passage deals with an oath to perform an action that might serve as intercession against deserved punishment. The response is that we never command sin; if the person happens to fall into sin, the oath is no longer binding because its purpose (intercession through a good deed) is not achieved. This is consistent with the opponent's own position that minor sins do not invalidate oaths made for similar purposes.

Repentance Requires Good Deeds
Baquillani uses a rhetorical question to argue repentance requires good deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baquillani uses a rhetorical question to demonstrate that valid repentance is achieved through good deeds, not sins.

Core Idea
Repentance is built on good deeds, not sins.

Baquillani presents a simple but powerful example to expose a contradiction in his opponents' logic. If someone wants to repent and seek forgiveness, what action should they command? The answer reveals a key principle: divine favor comes through obedience, not disobedience.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Note the structure: a question followed by the opponents' reply.
The passage is very short, so read it slowly to absorb the rhetorical force.
2
Identify the rhetorical question and the answer
Baquillani asks: what should a person who wants to repent and seek forgiveness do? The opponents answer: command him to do good and righteous deeds.
The opponents' answer is crucial because it reflects their own principle.
3
Reflect on the logical implication
If even the opponents agree that repentance requires good deeds, then they cannot claim that sin (like seeking intercession from sinners) can be a means to forgiveness. Their own logic disproves their position.
This is a classic argument from agreed premises.
4
Connect to the broader theme
This passage supports the overall argument that all forms of divine favor, including intercession, are attained through obedience, not disobedience.
The lesson ties into the samiyyat section on intercession and repentance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
ثم يقال لهم : فما تقولون أنتم فيمن أحب أن يكون من التوابين والمستغفرين، فحلف أن يعمل عملا تصح توبته واستغفاره منه؟
فإن قالوا : نأمره بفعل الخير والبرّ.
Question: Then it is said to them: What do you say yourselves about one who loves to be among the repentant and the seekers of forgiveness, and he swore that he will do an action by which his repentance and seeking forgiveness become valid? Then they said: We command him to do good and righteousness.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage uses a rhetorical question against the opponents. If someone wants to achieve valid repentance and seeking forgiveness, they would naturally command good deeds, not sins. This shows that intercession, like repentance, is attained through obedience, supporting the overall argument that sin cannot be a means to divine favor.

Key Terms
توبة
استغفار
شفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that sincere repentance requires engaging in sin first, so that one can seek forgiveness and trigger God's mercy. This passage corrects that by showing that even opponents command good deeds as the means to valid repentance.
Correction: Repentance and seeking forgiveness are achieved through righteous actions, not through sin.

Checkpoint
According to the opponents' admission in this passage, what should one do to achieve valid repentance and seeking forgiveness?
A) Commit a sin
B) Do good and righteous deeds
C) Swear an oath
D) Seek intercession

Key Takeaway
True repentance and seeking forgiveness are achieved through righteous deeds, not through sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly believe that your sins make you more deserving of God's mercy, or that repentance is a cheap reset button that requires no real change? What would it cost you to actually perform a good deed today as an act of sincere repentance?
?
If you were asked to swear an action to make your own repentance valid, what would you choose? Is that action already part of your daily life, or are you waiting for a 'better time' to start obeying?
?
Think of a sin you keep repeating while telling yourself you'll repent later. How does the truth that repentance is built on good deeds, not on sins, demand a different response from you right now? What one righteous act can you commit to before you sleep tonight?

The Consensus Proof for the Imamate
Baqillani presents the consensus proof and cites Abu Bakr's example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the consensus of the Companions as evidence for the obligation of appointing an imam.

Core Idea
The Companions' consensus after the Prophet's death establishes the imamate as obligatory.

Baqillani begins his proof for the imamate by appealing to a historical fact: the immediate and unanimous agreement of the Prophet's Companions that the community cannot remain without a leader. He quotes Abu Bakr's moving sermon and notes that this consensus continued through generations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the key terms: تواتر, إجماع, الصدر الأول. Then read the translation.
This passage presents a historical argument.
2
Identify the claim
What is the precise claim Baqillani makes about consensus? He says it 'تواتر' (mutawatir) that the imam is obligatory.
Tawatur is a technical term for universal transmission.
3
Examine the evidence
Look at the evidence: Abu Bakr's statement and the Companions' actions. How does this support the claim?
The burial postponement shows priority.
4
Reflect on continuity
Baqillani says this practice continued until the Ottoman era. Why is this long continuity important for his argument?
It reinforces the consensus across generations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لوجهين الأول: إنه تواتر إجماع المسلمين في الصدر الأول بعد وفاة النبي على امتناع خلو الوقت عن إمام، حتى قال أبو بكر رضي الله عنه في خطبته: ألا إن محمداً قد مات، ولا بد لهذا الدين ممن يقوم به، فبادر الكل إلى قبوله وتركوا له أهم الأشياء، وهو دفن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، ولم يزل الناس على ذلك في كل عصر إلى زمن آخر سلاطين بني عثمان السلطان عبد الحميد رحمه الله. فإن قيل: لا بد للإجماع من مستند ولو كان لنقل لتوفر الدواعي. قلنا: استغني عن نقله بالإجماع أو كان من قبيل ما لا يمكن نقله من قرائن الأحوال التي لا يمكن معرفتها إلا بالمشاهدة والعيان لمن كان في زمن النبي.
Two aspects: First: That there has been continuous consensus of the Muslims in the first generation after the death of the Prophet upon the impossibility of the time being empty of an imam, until Abu Bakr, may God be pleased with him, said in his sermon: 'Indeed Muhammad has died, and this religion must have someone to uphold it.' So everyone hastened to accept him and left for him the most important things, which was the burial of the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace. And the people continued upon that in every age until the time of the last of the sultans of the house of 'Uthman, Sultan 'Abd al-Hamid, may God have mercy on him. If it is said: Consensus must have a source, and if there were one it would have been transmitted due to abundant motives. We say: There was no need for its transmission due to the consensus, or it was of the kind that cannot be transmitted, like circumstantial evidence that can only be known by witnessing and direct observation for those who were in the time of the Prophet.
Source pages p. 435

Commentary
This passage presents the first proof for the obligation of appointing an imam. Baqillani states that there are two proofs; the first is the consensus (ijma') of the early Muslims. He argues that after the Prophet's death, the companions unanimously agreed that the community could not remain without an imam. He cites Abu Bakr's famous statement 'and this religion must have someone to uphold it' and notes that everyone accepted him immediately, even postponing the Prophet's burial. This practice continued through the ages, even to the Ottoman sultans. Then an objection is raised: consensus must have a textual source (mustanad), and if such a source existed it would have been transmitted because motives for transmission were abundant. Baqillani answers in two ways: either the transmission was unnecessary because the consensus itself suffices, or the source was of a type that cannot be transmitted, such as circumstantial evidence (qara'in al-ahwal) known only to those who witnessed the Prophet's time.

Key Terms
إجماع
الصدر الأول
أبو بكر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani claim about the consensus of the early Muslims?
A) It is a weak argument
B) It is mutawatir (continuously transmitted)
C) It is based on a single report
D) It is unrelated to imamate

Key Takeaway
The Companions' unanimous agreement on the necessity of an imam after the Prophet's death is a foundational proof for the imamate in Sunni theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a major life decision, do you consider the need for a guiding leadership in the community, or do you act as if the matter is purely personal? The Companions left the Prophet's burial to secure the imamate—what are you willing to leave behind for the sake of establishing Allah's order in your life?
?
The Companions unanimously accepted Abu Bakr without dissent. Is your heart equally united behind the legitimate leadership of your community, or do you harbor division and individualism that weakens the collective?
?
Baqillani argues that the consensus on the imamate is mutawatir and undeniable. Do you honestly treat the obligation of unity under a recognized imam as a non-negotiable duty, or have you subtly dismissed it as irrelevant in your time and place?

Responding to the Objection: The Source of Consensus
Baqillani answers the objection about the source of consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's response to the objection that consensus must have a transmitted textual source.

Core Idea
Consensus can be self-validating or based on circumstantial evidence that cannot be transmitted.

Having presented the consensus argument, Baqillani anticipates an objection: every valid consensus must be based on a known textual source (mustanad). If such a source existed, it would have been reported due to the abundant motives. Baqillani offers two creative answers: either the consensus itself suffices as evidence, or the source was non-transmittable circumstantial knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Read the objection carefully: 'لا بد للإجماع من مستند'. Understand the logic behind requiring a source.
The objection assumes that consensus alone is not sufficient proof.
2
Analyze the first response
Baqillani says 'استغني عن نقله بالإجماع'. What does this mean? How can consensus be independent of a textual source?
This is a technical point about the authority of ijma'.
3
Analyze the second response
He says the source might be 'قرائن الأحوال' that cannot be transmitted. What are circumstantial evidences? Why can't they be transmitted?
This refers to observable contexts from the Prophet's time.
4
Synthesize
How do these two responses together defend the consensus proof? Which one do you find more compelling?

?

?

Conditions of the People of Tawatur
Enumeration of conditions for transmitters of tawatur.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two essential conditions for transmitters of tawatur: necessary knowledge and sufficient number with verified integrity.

Core Idea
Tawatur requires transmitters with necessary knowledge and a number beyond collusion.

Imam Baqillani now turns to the qualities that must be present in those who transmit a mutawatir report. He presents these conditions in a question-and-answer format, clarifying what makes a report certain. This passage introduces two key conditions: the transmitters' knowledge must be necessary (not based on reasoning), and their number must be large enough to preclude collusion, with their integrity verified.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the question-answer structure and the two conditions introduced.
The passage is cut off at the end, but the first two conditions are clearly stated.
2
Identify the first condition
Find where the author states that the transmitters must have necessary knowledge (ʻilm ḍarūra) from observation, hearing, or something implanted in the soul. Understand why reasoning is excluded.
The author explains that if knowledge came through reasoning, the report would not produce certainty.
3
Identify the second condition
Locate the second condition: the transmitters must be a number exceeding one, two, three, etc., and we are commanded to examine their integrity. Note the mention of single witness and the requirement of ijtihad in assessing their ʻadāla.
The text cuts off during the explanation of why this condition is necessary.

باب آخر في صفات أهل التواتر فإن قال قائل : هل يجب أن يكون لأهل التواتر صفات لا بد من كونهم عليها؟ قيل له : أجل، فإن قال : وما هي ؟ قيل له : منها أنه يجب أن يكونوا عالمين بما ينقلونه علم ضرورة واقعاً مشاهدة أو سماع أو مخترع في النفس من غير نظر واستدلال وإلا لم يقع العلم بخبرهم وكذلك ما لم يجب أن يقع العلم بخبر كافة المسلمين لمن خالفهم بحَدَثِ الأجسام وإثبات صانعها وكون القرآن معجزاً وغير ذلك من الأخبار عن صحة الأمور المعلوم ثبوتها عندهم من جهة الاستدلال لأن الله تعالى لم يُجْرِ العادَةَ بفعل العلم بالمُخْبَرِ عنه إذا علمه المُخبرون عنه من هذه الطريقة ولأنا إنما نُخبر عن استدلال واقع استدلال واقع لنا به العلم فمن عرفه واستعمله ورتبه في موضعه عرف من ذلك ما عرفناه ومن صدَفَ عنه وأعرض عن تأمله لم يعرف صحة ما عنه خبرنا . ومن صفاتهم أن يكونوا عدداً يزيدون على الواحد والاثنين والثلاثة والأربعة وكلّ عدد أمرنا الله بالاستدلال على صدق المُخبر به كالشاهد الواحد ومَنْ أمرنا بالاجتهاد في عدالتهم وتأمل أحوالهم لأنه لو علم تعالى أن
Another chapter on the qualities of the people of tawatur. If one says: Must the people of tawatur have qualities without which they cannot be? It is said to him: Yes. Then he says: And what are they? It is said to him: Among them is that they must be knowers of what they transmit with necessary knowledge, actual [knowledge] from observation, hearing, or something implanted in the soul without investigation and reasoning, otherwise knowledge would not occur from their report. And similarly, knowledge does not necessarily occur from the report of all Muslims to those who oppose them regarding the temporality of bodies, the affirmation of their Maker, and that the Qur'an is miraculous, and other reports about the correctness of matters whose establishment is known to them through the method of reasoning, because God, exalted, does not conduct His custom by creating knowledge of the reported information when the reporters know it through this method; and because we only report about reasoning that has occurred, reasoning that has occurred by which we have knowledge. So whoever knows it, uses it, and arranges it in its proper place, will know from that what we know, and whoever turns away from it and abstains from contemplating it will not know the correctness of what we report about it. And among their qualities is that they be a number exceeding one, two, three, and four, and every number regarding which God has commanded us to seek evidence of the truthfulness of the reporter, like a single witness, and those regarding whom He commanded us to exert effort in assessing their integrity and examining their conditions, because if God, exalted, knew that
Source pages p. 443

Commentary
This passage is a new chapter on the conditions of the transmitters of tawatur. It begins with a question-answer format. The first condition is that the transmitters must have necessary knowledge (ʻilm ḍarūra) of what they transmit, not through reasoning. The passage then explains why reports about theological truths (like creation, divine attributes, miracles) do not yield tawatur-based knowledge to opponents: because the transmitters themselves know these through reasoning, not necessity, and God's custom does not produce necessary knowledge from such reports. Then it gives a second condition: the number must be large enough to preclude collusion, and we are commanded to verify their integrity. The passage is cut off before completing the explanation.
