Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any large group report yields necessary knowledge regardless of the transmitters' own knowledge.
Correction: The author specifies that the transmitters must themselves have necessary knowledge (not reasoning-based) for the report to produce certainty. Reports based on reasoning do not create necessary knowledge for others.

Checkpoint
What is the first quality of the people of tawatur mentioned in this passage?
A) They must be numerous.
B) They must have necessary knowledge of what they report.
C) They must be upright and just.
D) They must be scholars of kalam.

Key Takeaway
The people of tawatur must have necessary knowledge and be of a sufficient number with verified integrity for their report to yield certain knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'I testify that there is no god but Allah,' is your certainty based on necessary knowledge from direct observation, or are you relying on the report of others? What would it take for you to have the same necessary knowledge that the Prophet ﷺ had?
?
The author warns that those who turn away from contemplation do not know the correctness of what is reported. Is there a core belief of Islam that you hold without having personally reasoned through its proofs? Will you commit to studying the evidence until it becomes necessary knowledge for you?
?
If the people of tawatur must be free from collusion and their integrity verified, how carefully do you examine the sources of your religious knowledge? Name one report you accept uncritically and decide today to trace its chain and understand its epistemological status.

Evidence for the Quraysh Condition of Imamate
Al-Baqillani proves imamate must be from Quraysh via hadith and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence from hadith and early consensus that the imam must be from Quraysh.

Core Idea
The Quraysh condition is proven by authentic hadith and early Muslim consensus.

This passage presents the key proofs for the condition that the imam must be from Quraysh. Al-Baqillani cites specific hadith, including the Prophet's statement that the people are followers of Quraysh, and then argues for their authenticity through the acceptance of the early community at Saqifah. He further supports this with the consensus of the Muhajirun and Ansar after their initial dispute. Understanding these proofs is essential for grasping the Sunni position on imamate.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Get a sense of the author's argument flow.
Pay attention to the hadith citations and the mention of Saqifah.
2
Identify the two types of evidence
The author presents two distinct proofs: hadith reports and the consensus of the early community. Find where each is introduced.
3
Understand the hadith authenticity argument
Notice how al-Baqillani argues that the hadith must be authentic because the Ansar accepted them at Saqifah without objection.
He uses the principle that custom (al-ʿādah) prevents the acceptance of false reports in such a critical situation.
4
Understand the consensus argument
The author cites the agreement of the Muhajirun and Ansar after Saqifah that imamate is only for Quraysh, and the statement of Sa'd ibn Abi 'Ubadah as evidence.
This consensus strengthens the hadith evidence.
5
Reflect on the implications
Consider why the Quraysh condition is not a tribal preference but a matter of scriptural and communal authority.
The condition is rooted in textual evidence and early practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من قريش ما بقي منهم اثنان» (۱) وقوله للعباس حيث وصى بالأنصار في الخطبة المشهورة وكانت آخر خطبة خطبها لما قال للرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم: «توصي لقريش»، فقال له : «إنما أوصى قريشاً بالناس وبهذا الأمر وإنما الناس تبع لقريش ؛ فبَرُّ الناس تبع لبرهم وفاجرهم تبع لفاجرهم»(۲) في نظائر هذه الأخبار أو الألفاظ التي قد استفاضت وتواترت واتفقت على المعنى وإن اختلفت ألفاظها .
ويدل على ذلك وعلى صحة هذه الأخبار أيضاً احتجاج أبي بكر وعمر على الأنصار في السقيفة بها، وما روي عن العباس من ذكره لها والأمر باعتماد عليها وما كان من إذعان الأنصار ورجوعهم لموجبها عند سماعها وإدكارِهم بها والاستشهاد عليهم بها ولولا علمهم بصحتها لم يلبثوا أن يقدحوا فيها ويتعاطوا ردّها ؛ ولا كانت قريش بأسرها بالتي تقر كذباً يُدعى عليها ولها لأن العادة جارية فيما لم يثبت من الأخبار أن يقع الخلاف فيه والقَدْحُ عند التنازع والحِجَاج لا سيما إذا احتج به في مثل هذا الأمر العظيم الجسيم مع السيوف واختلاط القول ومحاولة الإمْرَةِ والميل إلى الرياسة والعادة أصل في الأخبار فصح بذلك ثبوت هذا الأمر.
إشهار
ويدل على ما قلناه إطباق الأمة في الصدر الأول من المهاجرين والأنصار بعد الاختلاف الذي شَجَرَ بينهم على أن الإمامة لا تصح إلا في قريش وقول سعد بن أبي عبادة (۳) لأبي بكر وعمر عند الاحتجاج بهذه الأخبار وادكارِه بها : رضي
نحن الوزراء وأنتم الأمراء» (۱) ؛ فثبت أن الحق في اجتماعها وأنه لا معتبر بقول ضرار وغيره ممن حدث بعد هذا الإجماع .
...from Quraysh, there remains not two of them (1) and his statement to al-Abbas when he commended the Ansar in the famous sermon, which was the last sermon he delivered, when he said to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'You commend Quraysh?' So he said to him: 'I only commend Quraysh regarding the people and this matter, and the people are followers of Quraysh; so the righteous of the people follow their righteous, and the wicked of them follow their wicked' (2) among similar reports or expressions that have become widespread and mutawatir, agreeing in meaning even if their wordings differ. And evidence for that and for the correctness of these reports also is the argument of Abu Bakr and 'Umar against the Ansar in the Saqifah using them, and what is narrated from al-Abbas about his mentioning them and commanding reliance upon them, and what occurred of the Ansar's compliance and their return to their implication upon hearing them and their being reminded by them and the use of them as evidence against them. And had they not known their authenticity, they would not have delayed in criticizing them and attempting to reject them. Nor would the entirety of Quraysh be the one to accept a lie alleged against them and for them, because the custom regarding reports that are not established is that disagreement and criticism occur during dispute and argument, especially when used as evidence in a matter as great and grave as this, amidst swords, confusion of speech, striving for command, and inclination towards leadership. And custom is the foundation regarding reports; thus the establishment of this matter is proven by that. [Section header: Ishhar (Publication)] And evidence for what we have said is the consensus of the community in the first generation among the Muhajirun and Ansar after the disagreement that occurred among them that the imamate is only valid in Quraysh, and the statement of Sa'd ibn Abi 'Ubadah to Abu Bakr and 'Umar when they argued with these reports and reminded him of them: 'We are the ministers and you are the rulers' (1); so it is established that the truth is in their consensus and that no consideration is given to the statement of Dirar and others who came after this consensus.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This passage provides evidence for the condition that the imam must be from Quraysh. It begins by citing hadith reports and then argues for their authenticity by noting that the early community, including the Ansar, accepted them, and that if they were false, Quraysh would not have accepted them. Then it cites the consensus of the early Muslims after the dispute at Saqifah that the imamate is only valid in Quraysh, and the statement of Sa'd ibn Abi 'Ubadah acknowledging that the Ansar are ministers and Quraysh are rulers. The passage concludes that the truth is in this consensus and that later opinions contrary to it are invalid.

Key Terms
قريش
الإمامة
الإجماع
السقيفة
الأنصار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Quraysh condition is a tribal preference without scriptural basis.
Correction: The author shows it is based on authentic hadith and early consensus, not mere tribalism.

Checkpoint
What evidence does the author use to prove that the imam must be from Quraysh?
A) Only hadith reports
B) Only consensus of the early community
C) Both hadith and consensus
D) Theological reasoning alone

Key Takeaway
The Quraysh condition is established by authentic hadith and early consensus, not tribal bias.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Quraysh condition is based on hadith and consensus. Is there any aspect of your faith that you follow merely because it is established by authority, even if it goes against your personal preference? Will you submit to it wholeheartedly?
?
The Ansar accepted the Quraysh condition despite losing the leadership to the Muhajirun. When you are passed over for a position or honor, can you accept it with the same grace and recognition of divine wisdom? What would need to change in your heart?
?
The author uses the argument of 'custom' (ādah) to affirm the authenticity of the hadith. In your own life, do you allow the consensus and established practice of the righteous predecessors to guide your decisions, or do you prioritize your own reasoning? Which leads to true success?

The Imam Must Be Highly Knowledgeable: Three Proofs
Baqillani provides three proofs that the imam must be knowledgeable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the imam must be a scholar according to Imam al-Baqillani, using three arguments from consensus and the nature of his judicial role.

Core Idea
The imam must be a scholar because he oversees judges and can judge himself.

Imam al-Baqillani continues his discussion of the qualifications of the imam. Having established that the imam must be from Quraysh and possess certain attributes, he now turns to a critical requirement: knowledge. In this passage, he provides three distinct proofs—two based on consensus and one based on the imam's role as the appointing authority over judges. As you read, notice how each argument reinforces the central point that the imam must be at least as knowledgeable as the judges he appoints.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three proofs
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note that the author states three things (أمور) and enumerates them with 'منها'. Try to identify each proof.
The proofs are marked by 'منها' which means 'among them'.
2
Understand the logic of the second proof
The second proof argues that since the imam appoints judges and reviews their judgments, he must have knowledge at least equal to theirs. Think about why this is necessary.
3
Reflect on the third proof
The third proof says the imam can personally serve as a judge, so he must be qualified to be a judge. This reinforces the requirement of high knowledge.
This is also supported by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما يدل على أنه يجب أن يكون من العلم بمنزلة ما وصفناه فأمور: منها إجماع الأمة على ذلك ممن قال بالنص والاختيار. ومنها أنه الذي يولى القضاة والحكام وينظرُ في أحكامهم وما يوجب صرفهم وجَرحَهم ونقض أحكامهم ؛ ولن يملك علمه بذلك وتمكّنه منه إلا بأن يكون كَهُمْ في العلم أو فوقهم. ومنها إجماع الأمة على أن للإمام أن يباشر القضاء والأحكام بنفسه ولا يستخلف قاضياً ما استغنى بنفسه ونظره ؛ ولن يصلح للحكم إلا من صلح أن يكون قاضياً من قضاة المسلمين فصح بذلك ما قلناه .
As for what indicates that he must be of knowledge in the degree we have described, there are matters: among them is the consensus of the community on that, from those who say (the imam is appointed) by text and by choice. And among them is that he is the one who appoints judges and rulers and examines their judgments and what necessitates their dismissal, their discreditation, and the annulment of their judgments; and he can only have knowledge of that and capability in it if he is like them in knowledge or above them. And among them is the consensus of the community that the imam may personally undertake judiciary and judgments and does not need to appoint a judge as long as he can dispense with his own judgment and examination; and no one is fit for judgment except one who is fit to be a judge among the judges of the Muslims. Thus what we have said is proven by that.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage proves that the imam must be highly knowledgeable. It gives three proofs: first, consensus of the community. Second, because he appoints judges and reviews their rulings, he must be at least as knowledgeable as them. Third, consensus that he can act as judge himself, so he must be qualified to be a judge. Therefore, he must be a scholar.

Key Terms
العلم
القضاة
الإجماع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think political leadership does not require deep religious knowledge.
Correction: The author argues it does because the imam oversees the judiciary and can personally judge, so he must be at least as knowledgeable as the judges.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must the imam be knowledgeable?
A) Because he must lead military campaigns
B) Because he appoints judges and can act as a judge himself
C) Because he needs to perform miracles
D) Because he must be from Quraysh

Key Takeaway
The imam must be a scholar because the community agrees and because his judicial oversight demands it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The imam is allowed to personally judge. Are you prepared to be judged by yourself for your own decisions? Do you seek knowledge so that you can stand accountable for your actions, not just rely on others?
?
The community demands a knowledgeable imam. Do you demand the same of yourself when you lead others, even in small matters? What is one area where you have stopped growing in knowledge, and how will you restart?

The Imam Must Be Brave and Composed
The author proves the imam must be courageous to enforce punishments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the imam must possess courage and composure to fulfill his duty of enforcing prescribed punishments.

Core Idea
The imam's role requires bravery to execute hudud without fear.

In this passage, the author establishes a necessary quality of the imam: courage. He argues that without it, the imam would fail in his primary duty of enforcing punishments and extracting rights. Let's examine the proof and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the logical flow of the argument.
Pay attention to the list of qualities: firmness, composure, strength of soul and heart.
2
Identify the required qualities
The author lists specific qualities the imam must have. Note each one and understand how they relate to the task of enforcing hudud.
3
Understand the consequence of lacking these qualities
The passage explains what would happen if the imam lacked courage: he would fall short in his duties and harm the community.
This is the logical consequence that proves the necessity.
4
Connect to the overall purpose of the imamate
Reflect on why this quality is essential for the community's well-being and the implementation of Islamic law.
This connects the specific proof to the broader theory of leadership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما يدل على أنه لا بد أن يكون من الصرامة وسكون الجأش وقوة النفس والقلب بحيث لا تَرُوعُه إقامة الحدود ولا يهوله ضرب الرقاب وتناول النفوس فهو أنه إذا لم يكن بهذه الصفة قصَّرِ عمـا لأجله أقيم من إقامة الحد واستخراج الحق وأضر فشله في هذا الأمر بما نُصِبَ له .
As for what indicates that he must possess firmness, composure, strength of soul and heart, such that the execution of prescribed punishments does not frighten him nor does striking necks and taking lives terrify him, it is that if he does not have this quality, he would fall short of what he was established for, namely the execution of the prescribed punishment and extraction of rights, and his failure in this matter would harm what he was appointed for.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage proves that the imam must be brave and composed. The reason is that he must enforce prescribed punishments (hudud), which include capital punishment. If he lacks courage, he would fail in this duty and harm the community.

Key Terms

الحدود
النفوس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

The Imam Must Know Warfare and Strategy
Proof that the imam must know warfare by consequence of harm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational necessity for the imam to be knowledgeable in military affairs and the chain of harms that justifies this obligation.

Core Idea
The imam's ignorance in warfare endangers the entire community.

Imam Baqillani now turns from internal leadership to external defense. He argues that the imam's responsibility includes protecting the ummah from its enemies, which requires personal knowledge of warfare. This passage establishes a rational proof that ignorance in this domain would defeat the very purpose of his office.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then read the translation. Notice how the author presents a conditional argument: if the imam is ignorant, then specific harms follow. Identify the key terms for military affairs.
The passage is one long sentence, so pay attention to the logical connectors (فإذا لم, فـ).
2
Trace the chain of consequences
List the harms that would result from the imam's ignorance: defect in military matters, harm spreads to the community, enemies covet the Muslims, mutual overpowering increases, judgments are suspended, and ultimately the purpose of the imam's appointment is nullified.
Each consequence leads to the next, building a cumulative argument.
3
Understand the argument's structure
This is a proof by contrapositive: if the imam does not have knowledge, the very objective for which he was appointed (preserving religion and worldly affairs) is destroyed. Therefore, he must have that knowledge.
The obligation is derived from the need to prevent these harms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما يدل على وجوب كونه عالماً بأمر الحرب وتدبير الجيوش وسد الثغور وحماية البيضة وما يتصل بذلك من الأمر، فهو أنه إذا لم يكن عالماً بذلك لحِقَ الخَلَلُ في جميعه وتعدى الضرر بجهله بذلك إلى الأمة وطمع في المسلمين عدوهم وكثر تغالبهم ووقفت أحكامهم وأدى ذلك إلى إبطال ما أقيم لأجله فوجب بذلك ما قلناه .
As for what indicates the necessity of his being knowledgeable in matters of war, organizing armies, securing frontiers, protecting the core territory, and what is connected to that of affairs, it is that if he is not knowledgeable in that, defect would occur in all of it, and harm due to his ignorance in that would spread to the community, and their enemy would covet the Muslims, their mutual overpowering would increase, their judgments would be suspended, and that would lead to the nullification of what he was established for. Therefore what we said is obligatory by that.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage proves that the imam must be knowledgeable in military affairs. The consequence of ignorance is that defects would spread, enemies would attack, chaos would increase, and the very purpose of his appointment would be nullified.

Key Terms

الجيوش
الثغور
البيضة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The imam can delegate military affairs completely and does not need personal knowledge of warfare.
Correction: The passage argues that the imam must himself be knowledgeable because ignorance leads to harms that delegation cannot prevent. The proof shows that the imam's personal ignorance would cause defects and harm, implying that mere delegation does not relieve him of responsibility.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
The imam must be knowledgeable in warfare because his ignorance would lead to harm, enemy aggression, chaos, and the nullification of his very purpose.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

Examine your life: where have you excused your ignorance by saying 'I trust the experts'? Write down one commitment to personally learn the basics of that area before next month.

Baqillani's Proof That Uthman Was Killed Unjustly
Baqillani answers the charge against Uthman with two proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's twofold argument that Uthman was killed unjustly, based on his established merits and the illegitimacy of extrajudicial killing.

Core Idea
Uthman's killing was unjust because his merits prove innocence and his non-resistance demands legal procedure.

Imam Baqillani defends the Sunni position that Uthman was killed wrongfully. He anticipates a question about whether Uthman deserved death and responds with both a substantive argument from his virtues and a procedural argument about the manner of killing. This passage shows how kalam combines textual claims and rational jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and Baqillani's categorical answer
Notice the question: Was Uthman killed justly or unjustly? Baqillani immediately asserts he was killed wrongfully and denies any fault on Uthman's part.
2
Identify the first proof: merits of Uthman
Baqillani says it is established that Uthman had faith, purity, precedence, virtue, and jihad. These put the burden of proof on the killers to show a valid reason.
This is an argument from known character.
3
Identify the second proof: even if fault, killing was illegal
Baqillani argues that even if there were grounds for removal, the killing was invalid because Uthman did not resist or wage war. The proper response would be arrest, imprisonment, or forced abdication, not killing.
This is a procedural argument based on the rules of warfare and punishment.
4
Reflect on the combination
Notice how Baqillani uses two independent lines of reasoning. The first establishes Uthman's innocence, the second shows the killers' action was wrong regardless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الكلام في مقتل عثمان رضي الله عنه والدليل على أنه قتل مظلوماً فإن قال قائل : فهل تقولون إن عثمان قتل مستحقاً للقتل أم مظلوماً وهل كان منه حَدَث أوجب قتله والمطالبة بخلعه أم لا؟ قيل له : نقول إن عثمان رضي الله عنه قتل مظلوماً وإنه لم يكن منه ما يوجب قتله ولا المطالبة بخلعـه ولا سقوط عدالته وموالاته وإن الذين تولوا قتله والإغراق في السعي عليه أهلُ فتنة ولفيف الأمصار ومن لا مدخل له في هذا الشأن أعني أمر الإمامة وحلهـا وعقدها وإنهم لم يستندوا في شيء مما خرجوا إليه في أمره إلى ما يمكن أن يكون شبهة فضلا أن يكون حجة. فإن قالوا وما الدليل على ذلك؟ عن الدليل عليه أنه قد ثبت من إيمان عثمان ونزاهته وسابقته وفضله وجهاده ما من فضائله ومن صحة إمامته وثبوت بيعته ووجوب طاعته والانقياد له ما نستغني عن إعادته وردّ قول فيه وإذا كان ذلك كذلك أن نعتقد أنه على هذه الأوصاف وأنه قتل مظلوماً حتى يذكر القاتلون لـه والساعون عليه جميع والمنتصرون لفجورهم ما يبيحون به دمه على ذلك الوجه ويوجب خلع طاعته وزوال عدالته ؛ وأنّى لهم بذلك؟ . قدمناه وجب وعلى أنه لو ثبت عليه أمر يستحق به خلع الطاعة ويجب به زوال العدالة لم يكن مبيحاً لقتله على ذلك الوجه لأنه لم يخم داراً ويمتنع على المسلمين ولا نَصَبَ الحرب بينه وبين من سار إليه فقد كان يجب عليهم القبض عليه لما أخذوه وتمكنوا من داره وحريمه أو حبسه وإبعاده عن المدينة أو أخذه بغاية الإرهاب بخلع نفسه لو كان مستحقاً للخلع فأما أن يُقتل على ذلك الوجه وهو غير ناصب للحرب فضلال وظلم لا محالة
Chapter on the discourse concerning the murder of Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) and the proof that he was killed wrongfully. If someone says: 'Do you say that Uthman was killed deserving of killing or wrongfully, and was there from him an act that necessitated his killing and the demand for his removal, or not?' It is said to him: 'We say that Uthman (may Allah be pleased with him) was killed wrongfully, and that there was not from him anything that would necessitate his killing nor the demand for his removal nor the nullification of his justice (adala) and loyalty (muwalat). And those who undertook his killing and incited against him are people of fitna, a rabble of the cities, and people with no standing in this matter, i.e., the affair of imamate, its dissolution and contract. And they did not rely in anything they undertook against him on any possible specious argument, let alone a proof.' If they say: 'What is the proof of that?' The proof is that it has been established from the faith of Uthman, his purity, his precedence, his virtue, and his jihad, such that we are dispensed from repeating it and from replying to a statement concerning it. And if that is the case, then it is necessary that we believe that he was on these attributes and that he was killed wrongfully, until the killers and those who incited against him and the supporters of their immorality mention what would render his blood permissible in that manner and necessitate the dissolution of obedience to him and the disappearance of his justice—and how can they do that? And moreover, if a matter were established against him that would necessitate the dissolution of obedience and the disappearance of justice, it would not be permissible to kill him in that manner, because he did not defend his house and resist the Muslims, nor did he wage war between himself and those who marched against him. They should have rather arrested him when they seized him and had access to his house and his sanctuary, or imprisoned him and exiled him from Medina, or forced him to abdicate if he deserved removal. As for killing him in that manner while he was not waging war—that is misguidance and injustice without doubt.
Source pages p. 524

Commentary
This passage is a kalam argument proving that Uthman was killed unjustly. It begins with a chapter heading indicating the proof. Then a questioner asks whether Baqillani holds that Uthman was killed justly or unjustly, and whether he had done something to warrant it. Baqillani unequivocally states that Uthman was killed wrongfully, with no action on his part that would justify killing or deposition. He identifies the killers as people of fitna with no legitimate authority. When asked for proof, Baqillani invokes Uthman's established merits of faith, precedence, and virtue, which dispense with the need to repeat them. Since he is known to be such, the burden of proof falls on the killers to show a valid reason for shedding his blood. Then Baqillani presents a second argument: even if there were a reason to depose him, the manner of killing was illegitimate because he did not resist violently. The proper procedure would have been arrest, exile, or forced abdication, not extrajudicial killing. Therefore, the killing was misguidance and injustice.

Key Terms
مظلوماً
عدالة
فتنة
إمامة
دم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Baqillani only argues from Uthman's piety without addressing the possibility of fault.
Correction: Baqillani includes a second argument that even if there were fault, the killing was procedurally invalid because Uthman did not resist.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, even if Uthman had done something wrong that warranted removal from office, why was his killing unjust?
A) Because only the caliph can be killed.
B) Because he did not resist or wage war, so the proper course was arrest, imprisonment, or forced abdication.
C) Because he was a companion.
D) Because the killers were not qualified.

Key Takeaway
Baqillani defends Uthman's innocence on two fronts: his known virtues and the illegality of his killing given his non-resistance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear someone accused of a wrongdoing, do you immediately assume guilt or do you, like Baqillani, demand proof and consider their known virtues? Which of your relationships would be harmed if you abandoned this principle?
?
If you were wronged by a leader or authority figure, would your first instinct be to take matters into your own hands or to seek lawful recourse? How does Uthman's non-resistance challenge your desire for revenge?
?
Are there people in your life whom you have judged harshly without giving them the benefit of the doubt? What would it cost you to seek proper procedure and evidence before condemning them?

Uthman Was Not the First to Compile the Quran
Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman was first to compile the Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman was the first to compile the Quran, and learn that earlier compilations existed.

Core Idea
Uthman's compilation was not a novel act; earlier compilations existed.

Some critics argued that Uthman innovated by being the first to collect the Quran. Baqillani counters by showing that the Quran was already compiled in the Prophet's and early caliphs' times, albeit in scattered forms. This lesson examines his refutation of the 'precedent' claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening refutation
Read from the beginning up to 'ما حدث في أيامه' to see how Baqillani frames the criticism as ignorance.
Notice he first calls it 'great ignorance' (جهل عظيم).
2
Identify the obligation argument
Look at the sentence starting with 'وهذا كان الواجب' – Baqillani argues Uthman was obligated to act, otherwise he would be sinful.
This sets the stage for defending Uthman's action.
3
Focus on the precedent refutation
Examine the sentence 'وأما قولهم إنه سبق إلى ذلك فباطل' and the evidence that compilation existed earlier.
Baqillani cites the materials used in earlier compilations.
4
Connect to the broader defense
Understand how this refutation supports the overall defense of Uthman's integrity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تعلقهم بأن عثمان جمع القرآن وحرق المصاحف وسبق إلى ذلك فإنه جهل عظيم لأن هذا من فضائله وتسديد عمله عندما حدث الاختلاف من والتهارج بين القراء وعدوان بعضهم على بعض ووجود كل ملحد ومدغل السبيل إلى الطعن في الدين وإفساد التأويل والهزل بأئمة المسلمين. وهذا كان الواجب على عثمان إذا وقع له وخطر بباله وظن الصلاح ولَمَّ الشَّعَثِ ؛ ولو عدل عنه لكان عاصياً مُفَرِّطاً قائداً إلى الإهمال والتضييع. وأما قولهم إنه سبق إلى ذلك فباطل لأنه قد جُمِعَ في أيام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأيام أبي بكر وعمر في الجلود والخَزَفِ والأكتاف وغير ذلك ولم تحتج الصحابة إلى جمعه على وجه ما جمعه عثمان لأنه لم يحدث في أيامهما الخلاف بين القراء ما حدث في أيامه وأما تعلقهم بأن جمعه معصية وبدعة فإنه جهل لأن المعصية هي ما نهِي فاعلها عنها ونحن نقول إن جمعه من فَرْض عثمان إذا قدر في جمعه من الصلاح ما ذكرناه وليس من نص الكتاب أو السنة الثابتة أو إجماع الأمة أو حجج العقول ما يُحظُرُ جمع القرآن ويقضي على عصيان فاعله فبطل بذلك ما ظنوه
And as for their claim that Uthman collected the Quran and burned the manuscripts and was precedent in that, it is great ignorance because this is from his virtues and the rectitude of his action when the disagreement occurred from the confusion among the reciters and the aggression of some of them against others, and the existence of every atheist and one sneaking a way to attack the religion, corrupting interpretation, and mocking the imams of the Muslims. And this was obligatory upon Uthman when it occurred to him and came to his mind and he thought it was good, and to bring together the scattered parts; and if he had turned away from it, he would have been a disobedient, negligent leader toward neglect and waste. And as for their statement that he was precedent in that, it is false because the Quran was collected in the days of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) and the days of Abu Bakr and Umar on leather, pottery, shoulder blades, and other things, and the Companions did not need to collect it in the manner that Uthman collected it because in their days the disagreement among the reciters that occurred in his days did not happen. And as for their claim that his collection was a sin and innovation, it is ignorance because sin is what the doer is forbidden from doing, and we say that his collection was a duty of Uthman if he deemed in his collection the benefit we mentioned, and there is nothing from the text of the Book, or established Sunnah, or consensus of the community, or rational proofs that prohibits the collection of the Quran and judges the doer as sinful. So what they supposed is invalidated.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of accusations against Caliph Uthman's actions regarding the Quran. The author, Baqillani, addresses three claims: that Uthman was first to compile the Quran, that his compilation was a sin/innovation, and that he burned manuscripts. In this lesson, he refutes the first two. He begins by stating that the accusation is born of ignorance, as Uthman's act was a virtue and a necessary response to emerging disputes among reciters, which led to corruption of the religion. Baqillani argues that it was Uthman's duty to act when he saw the need, and failure to do so would have been sinful. He then refutes the claim that Uthman was the first to compile the Quran, noting that compilation existed in the Prophet's and early caliphs' times, but the need for an official unified version arose only in Uthman's era due to new disagreements. Finally, he refutes the claim that the compilation was a sin, defining sin as an act explicitly forbidden by revelation or reason, and asserts that no such prohibition exists against gathering the Quran. Thus the accusations are baseless.

Key Terms
جمع القرآن
سبق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman was the first to collect the Quran into a book.
Correction: The Quran was collected earlier on various materials, but Uthman's compilation was a unified standard necessitated by disputes.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why is the claim that Uthman was first to compile the Quran false?
A) Because Uthman used the same method as Abu Bakr
B) Because the Quran was already compiled earlier in various forms
C) Because the Prophet had compiled it before
D) Because Uthman did not actually compile it

Key Takeaway
Uthman's compilation was not a new invention but a necessary response to new challenges, building on earlier compilations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear criticism of a respected scholar or leader, do you rush to judgment or do you pause to understand the full context—as Baqillani insists we must with Uthman? What one accusation have you accepted too quickly, and what will you do to investigate it properly?
?
Baqillani argues that if Uthman had ignored the crisis, he would have been sinful. Are there situations in your life where inaction in the face of division or corruption makes you complicit? What is one step you can take today to bring unity or protect the truth, even if it is difficult?
?
The reciters' conflict nearly led to 'atheists sneaking in to attack the religion.' Where in your own community do you see small disagreements escalating into a crisis? How can you be a peacemaker, like Uthman, rather than a spectator?

Uthman's Compilation Was Not a Sin or Innovation
Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman's compilation was a sin or innovation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defines sin and argues that Uthman's compilation of the Quran does not fall under any prohibition, thus refuting the accusation of sin or innovation.

Core Idea
Sin is defined by prohibition; no prohibition exists for compiling the Quran.

Another accusation against Uthman was that his compilation of the Quran was a sin (ma'siya) and innovation (bid'a). Baqillani refutes this by first defining sin as an act that is explicitly forbidden, then showing that there is no textual or rational prohibition against compiling the Quran. This lesson examines his decisive argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the sin accusation refutation
Start from 'وأما تعلقهم بأن جمعه معصية وبدعة' to the end. Note how Baqillani begins by calling this claim ignorance.
He directly labels it as ignorance (جهل).
2
Understand the definition of sin
Baqillani defines sin as something the doer is forbidden from doing. Grasp this definition.
This is key to his argument.
3
Identify the basis of permissibility
Baqillani states that Uthman's compilation was a duty (فرض) based on the benefit mentioned, and no prohibition exists from the Book, Sunnah, consensus, or reason.
He lists four sources: text of Quran, established Sunnah, consensus, and rational proofs.
4
Conclude the refutation
He concludes that the accusation is invalidated (فبطل بذلك ما ظنوه).
The burden of proof is on the accusers to show a prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تعلقهم بأن عثمان جمع القرآن وحرق المصاحف وسبق إلى ذلك فإنه جهل عظيم لأن هذا من فضائله وتسديد عمله عندما حدث الاختلاف من والتهارج بين القراء وعدوان بعضهم على بعض ووجود كل ملحد ومدغل السبيل إلى الطعن في الدين وإفساد التأويل والهزل بأئمة المسلمين. وهذا كان الواجب على عثمان إذا وقع له وخطر بباله وظن الصلاح ولَمَّ الشَّعَثِ ؛ ولو عدل عنه لكان عاصياً مُفَرِّطاً قائداً إلى الإهمال والتضييع. وأما قولهم إنه سبق إلى ذلك فباطل لأنه قد جُمِعَ في أيام رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وأيام أبي بكر وعمر في الجلود والخَزَفِ والأكتاف وغير ذلك ولم تحتج الصحابة إلى جمعه على وجه ما جمعه عثمان لأنه لم يحدث في أيامهما الخلاف بين القراء ما حدث في أيامه وأما تعلقهم بأن جمعه معصية وبدعة فإنه جهل لأن المعصية هي ما نهِي فاعلها عنها ونحن نقول إن جمعه من فَرْض عثمان إذا قدر في جمعه من الصلاح ما ذكرناه وليس من نص الكتاب أو السنة الثابتة أو إجماع الأمة أو حجج العقول ما يُحظُرُ جمع القرآن ويقضي على عصيان فاعله فبطل بذلك ما ظنوه
And as for their claim that Uthman collected the Quran and burned the manuscripts and was precedent in that, it is great ignorance because this is from his virtues and the rectitude of his action when the disagreement occurred from the confusion among the reciters and the aggression of some of them against others, and the existence of every atheist and one sneaking a way to attack the religion, corrupting interpretation, and mocking the imams of the Muslims. And this was obligatory upon Uthman when it occurred to him and came to his mind and he thought it was good, and to bring together the scattered parts; and if he had turned away from it, he would have been a disobedient, negligent leader toward neglect and waste. And as for their statement that he was precedent in that, it is false because the Quran was collected in the days of the Messenger of God (peace be upon him) and the days of Abu Bakr and Umar on leather, pottery, shoulder blades, and other things, and the Companions did not need to collect it in the manner that Uthman collected it because in their days the disagreement among the reciters that occurred in his days did not happen. And as for their claim that his collection was a sin and innovation, it is ignorance because sin is what the doer is forbidden from doing, and we say that his collection was a duty of Uthman if he deemed in his collection the benefit we mentioned, and there is nothing from the text of the Book, or established Sunnah, or consensus of the community, or rational proofs that prohibits the collection of the Quran and judges the doer as sinful. So what they supposed is invalidated.
Source pages p. 537

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of accusations against Caliph Uthman's actions regarding the Quran. The author, Baqillani, addresses three claims: that Uthman was first to compile the Quran, that his compilation was a sin/innovation, and that he burned manuscripts. In this lesson, he refutes the first two. He begins by stating that the accusation is born of ignorance, as Uthman's act was a virtue and a necessary response to emerging disputes among reciters, which led to corruption of the religion. Baqillani argues that it was Uthman's duty to act when he saw the need, and failure to do so would have been sinful. He then refutes the claim that Uthman was the first to compile the Quran, noting that compilation existed in the Prophet's and early caliphs' times, but the need for an official unified version arose only in Uthman's era due to new disagreements. Finally, he refutes the claim that the compilation was a sin, defining sin as an act explicitly forbidden by revelation or reason, and asserts that no such prohibition exists against gathering the Quran. Thus the accusations are baseless.

Key Terms
معصية
بدعة
فرض
نص الكتاب
سنة ثابتة
إجماع الأمة
حجج العقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman's compilation was a sin (ma'siya) and innovation (bid'a).
Correction: Sin requires a clear prohibition; no such prohibition exists for compiling the Quran, so it cannot be sinful.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what makes an act a sin?
A) If it is a new action not done by the Prophet
B) If the doer is forbidden from doing it by revelation or reason
C) If it causes disagreement among Muslims
D) If it is done without consensus

Key Takeaway
Uthman's compilation cannot be sinful because there is no prohibition against it from any authoritative source.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you judge an action as sinful or bid'ah, do you ever pause to ask whether there is a clear prohibition against it from Allah or His Messenger? How often do you rely on assumptions rather than evidence? Will you commit to verifying prohibitions before condemning others from today?
?
Think of a good deed you have hesitated to perform because you feared it might be an innovation. Based on this lesson, what criteria can you use to determine whether it is permissible or even a duty? Is there a specific act of kindness or community service you will undertake this week, trusting that without a prohibition, it is not sinful?

Baqillani's Defense of Uthman's Burning of Manuscripts
Baqillani defends Uthman's burning of manuscripts by questioning its factual basis and interpreting it hypothetically.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's method of defending Uthman against the accusation of burning manuscripts wrongfully, including his reliance on presumption of justice and hypothetical interpretation.

Core Idea
Uthman's justice requires interpreting his actions positively.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a historical accusation against Caliph Uthman: that he burned copies of the Quran. He does not even concede the factual basis of the claim, but then argues that if it were true, it must have been justified. This lesson examines how Baqillani uses the established justice of the Companions to defend Uthman's action.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation once. Notice how Baqillani begins by questioning the reliability of the report before offering a hypothetical interpretation.
Pay attention to the phrase 'فإنه غير ثابت'.
2
Identify the two-part argument
Baqillani first says the claim is unproven, then argues hypothetically: even if true, it was justified because Uthman acted as a knowledgeable imam.
3
Examine the supporting evidence
Notice that Baqillani points to the lack of objection from other Companions as indirect evidence of Uthman's correctness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولهم إنه حَرَّقَ المصاحف فإنه غير ثابت ولا مما يَلْزَمُ قُلوبَنَا العِلْمُ به ولو ثبت لوجب أن يحمل على أنه حَرَّق مصاحف قد أودعت ما لا تحل قراءته وقد خرج عن أن يكون قرآناً بإفساد نظمه وإحالة معناه في الجملة فإنه إمام من أهل العلم غير مُعَانِدٍ للنبي صلّى الله عليه وسلم ولا طاعن على التنزيل. هذا المعلوم من أمره ؛ فيجب أن يكون حرق ما يجب إحراقه . ولذلك ما لم يُرْوَ عَنْ أحد من الصحابة أنه قال له : قد عَصيت الله وأذللت الدين بإحراقك مصاحف لا يحل إحراقها. وقد شاهد القوم من ذلك وعرفوا ما ذهب علينا معرفة كنهه وقد ثبت عدالة عثمان وطهارته ؛ فلا مُتَعَلَّقَ في ذلك .
And as for their statement that he burned the manuscripts, it is not established nor something that our hearts are obligated to know. And if it were established, it would be necessary to interpret that he burned manuscripts that contained what it is not permissible to recite, and that had ceased to be Quran due to corruption of its order and alteration of its meaning in general. For he is an imam of knowledge, not obstinate towards the Prophet (peace be upon him) nor a critic of the revelation. This is the known state of his affair; so it must be that he burned what must be burned. That is why it is not reported from any Companion that he said to him: 'You have disobeyed God and degraded the religion by burning manuscripts that it is not permissible to burn.' They witnessed that and knew what has escaped our knowledge of its reality, and Uthman's justice and purity are established. So there is no basis in that.
Source pages p. 538

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the accusation that Uthman burned Qurans wrongfully. Baqillani first questions the factual basis of the claim, stating it is not proven and not necessary for us to know. He then argues hypothetically: even if true, it must be interpreted positively—Uthman only burned manuscripts that had become corrupted and no longer valid as Quran, because he was a knowledgeable and righteous imam, not an enemy of the revelation. The author supports this by noting that no Companion condemned the act, which would be expected if it were sinful. Since Uthman's justice is established, any action attributed to him must be assumed lawful unless proven otherwise. Thus the accusation lacks foundation.

Key Terms
إحراق المصاحف
عدالة الصحابة
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Uthman's burning of manuscripts proves his wrongdoing or disregard for the Quran.
Correction: Baqillani argues that even if the burning happened, Uthman's known justice and the lack of Companion condemnation indicate that he only burned corrupted texts that were no longer Quran.

Checkpoint
What is Baqillani's main argument if the burning of manuscripts is accepted as true?
A) Uthman was forced to do it by the Companions
B) Uthman only burned manuscripts that were no longer valid Quran
C) Uthman admitted his mistake
D) The manuscripts were duplicates

Key Takeaway
Baqillani shows that the presumption of justice for the Companions means any ambiguous action attributed to them must be interpreted lawfully.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative report about someone known for their piety and justice, do you instinctively question the report's reliability and interpret the action charitably, or do you rush to judgment? What does your reaction reveal about the state of your heart towards God's righteous servants?
?
Baqillani defends Uthman even before considering the evidence, based on his known character. Is there someone in your life—a scholar, a parent, or a friend—whom you are quick to defend when they are accused? If not, why? Are you afraid of being seen as biased, or do you truly distrust their virtue?
?
If you were to apply Baqillani's method—first questioning the report, then assuming the best possible interpretation—to a current situation where a fellow Muslim is criticized, would you be able to maintain that discipline, or would you find yourself swayed by the accusation? What concrete step can you take today to practice this kind of intellectual and spiritual fairness?

Defense of Uthman Regarding Completing Prayer at Mina
Baqillani refutes the claim that Uthman erred by completing the prayer at Mina during travel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani argues that Uthman did not err by completing the prayer at Mina, and that completing prayer during travel is permissible.

Core Idea
Completing prayer during travel is permissible; the Prophet and companions did it.

In this passage, Baqillani defends Uthman against the accusation of error in completing the four-rakat prayer at Mina. He argues that the accusation itself reflects obstinacy, and then provides evidence from the Prophet's practice and the companions' actions to show that completing travel prayer is permissible.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the tone of refutation and the arguments presented.
The passage is part of a larger debate; focus on the argument structure.
2
Identify the two main arguments
Baqillani gives two reasons why Uthman's action was not an error. First, completing travel prayer is permissible. Second, Uthman had his own valid justifications. Find these in the text.
The second argument is only mentioned briefly; the justifications are not detailed in this excerpt.
3
Reflect on the evidence
Look at the evidence Baqillani gives: the Prophet completed and shortened during travel, and Aisha and other companions completed this prayer. Ask yourself why this evidence is effective.
Consider how the practice of the Prophet and companions establishes permissibility.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to ensure you have grasped the core point about permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما تعلقهم بأنه أتم الصلاة بمنى فإنه أيضاً من قلة التوفيق وللدلالة على العناد لأن هذه الصلاة صلاة سفر يجوز له إتمامها ويجوز له قصرها وقد كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يتم في السفر تارة ويقصر أخرى وكانت عائشة رضي الله عنها وغيرها من الصحابة يتمون هذه الصلاة خاصة، فما أنكر ذلك أحد ولا عده ذنباً وعلى أن عثمان قد احتج في ذلك بشيئين، لما نقم من ذلك شيء.
And as for their claim that he completed the prayer at Mina, it is also due to lack of success and an indication of obstinacy, because this prayer is a travel prayer; it is permissible for him to complete it and it is permissible for him to shorten it. And the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, would sometimes complete the prayer during travel and sometimes shorten it. And Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, and other companions would complete this prayer specifically. So no one disapproved of that nor considered it a sin. And also, Uthman had argued for that with two things, which are not disapproved of in that matter.
Source pages p. 540

Commentary
This passage refutes the accusation that Uthman committed a sin by completing the four-rakat prayer at Mina during the Hajj, where the Prophet had shortened it. Baqillani states that this accusation itself shows lack of guidance and obstinacy. He gives two reasons: first, it is permissible for a traveler to either complete or shorten the prayer. The Prophet himself sometimes completed and sometimes shortened during travel. Furthermore, Aisha and other companions used to complete this particular prayer at Mina, and no one criticized them. Second, Uthman had his own two justifications for completing the prayer (though the text cuts off before listing them). The author concludes that there was no grounds for criticism.

Key Terms
إتمام الصلاة
صلاة السفر
القصر
منى
عائشة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claimed that Uthman committed a sin by completing the prayer at Mina during travel.
Correction: Baqillani shows that completing prayer during travel is permissible; the Prophet did it, and companions approved.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani say about the permissibility of completing prayer during travel?
A) It is forbidden
B) It is permissible but disliked
C) It is permissible, and the Prophet sometimes did it
D) It is only permissible if one intends to stay

Key Takeaway
Completing the prayer at Mina during travel is not a sin; it is permissible based on the Prophet's practice and the companions' actions, and Uthman had his own valid justifications.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you quick to accuse others of error when they do something different from what you believe is the only correct practice, especially in matter of worship? This lesson shows that the Prophet himself did both shortening and completing, and the companions differed. How can you check your heart before judging others' actions in religion?
?
Do you have a habit of assuming that later generations (like the Companions) must have fallen short if they did not follow every detail of what you think is the 'authentic' practice? How does this lesson challenge that assumption, and what would it mean for you to trust the sahaba's understanding more than your own?
